PREFACE 
    This Code constitutes a complete republication of the ordinances of the Town of Cheraw, South Carolina, of a general and permanent nature. 
    Source materials used in the preparation of the Code were the 1971 Code, as supplemented through Ord. No. 2010-08, adopted on June 8, 2010, and ordinances subsequently adopted by the commission. The source of each section is included in the history note appearing in parentheses at the end thereof. The absence of such a note indicates that the section is new and was adopted for the first time with the adoption of the Code. By use of the comparative tables appearing in the back of this volume, the reader can locate any section of the 1971 Code, as supplemented, and any subsequent ordinance included herein. 
    The chapters of the Code have been conveniently arranged in alphabetical order and the various sections within each chapter have been catchlined to facilitate usage. Footnotes which tie related sections of the Code together and which refer to relevant state laws have been included. A table listing the state law citations and setting forth their location within the Code is included at the back of this volume. 
Numbering System 
    The numbering system used in this Code is the same system used in many state and municipal codes. Each section number consists of two component parts separated by a dash, the figure before the dash referring to the chapter number and the figure after the dash referring to the position of the section within the chapter. Thus, the first section of Chapter 2 is numbered 2-1 and the third section of Chapter 3 is 3-3. Under this system, each section is identified with its chapter and at the same time new sections or even whole chapters can be inserted in their proper place simply by using the decimal system for amendments. By way of illustration: If new material consisting of three sections that would logically come between sections 5-1 and 5-2 is desired to be added, such new sections would be numbered 5-1.1, 5-1.2 and 5-1.3 respectively. New chapters may be included in the same manner. If the new material is to be included between Chapters 10 and 11, it will be designated as Chapter 10.5. Care should be taken that the alphabetical arrangement of chapters is maintained when including new chapters. New articles and new divisions may be included in the same way or, in the case of articles, may be placed at the end of the chapter embracing the subject, and, in the case of divisions, may be placed at the end of the article embracing the subject, the next successive number being assigned to the article or division. 
    The page numbering system used in this Code is a prefix system. The letters to the left of the colon are an abbreviation which represents a certain portion of the volume. The number to the right of the colon represents the number of the page in that portion. In the case of a chapter of the Code, the number to the left of the colon indicates the number of the chapter. In the case of an appendix to the Code, the letter immediately to the left of the colon indicates the letter of the appendix. The following are typical parts of codes of ordinances, which may or may not appear in this Code at this time, and their corresponding prefixes: 
Charter CHT:1 Charter Comparative Table CHTCT:1 Code CD1:1 Code Appendix CDA:1 Code Comparative Tables CCT:1 Charter Index CHTi:1 Code Index CDi:1  
Indices 
    The indices of the Code have been prepared with the greatest of care. Each particular item has been placed under several headings, some of the headings being couched in lay phraseology, others in legal terminology, and still others in language generally used by municipal officials and employees. There are numerous cross references within the indices which stand as guideposts to direct the user to the particular item in which he is interested. 
Looseleaf Supplements 
    A special feature of this Code to which the attention of the user is especially directed is the looseleaf system of binding and supplemental servicing for the Code. With this system, the Code will be kept up-to-date periodically. Upon the final passage of amendatory ordinances, they will be properly edited and the appropriate page or pages affected will be reprinted. These new pages will be distributed to holders of copies of the Code, with instructions for the manner of inserting the new pages and deleting the obsolete pages. Each such amendment, when incorporated into this Code, may be cited as a part hereof. 
    The successful keeping of this Code up-to-date at all times will depend largely upon the holder of the volume. As revised sheets are received, it will then become the responsibility of the holder to have the amendments inserted according to the attached instructions. It is strongly recommended by the publisher that all such amendments be inserted immediately upon receipt to avoid misplacing them and, in addition, that all deleted pages be saved and filed for historical reference purposes. 
Acknowledgments 
    The republication of this Code was by Municipal Code Corporation, Tallahassee, Florida, under the direct supervision of Regina Sosinski, Editor, and Rachael Jamison, Proofreader. Credit is gratefully given to other members of the publisher's staff for their able assistance throughout the project. 
    The publisher is most grateful to Mike Smith, Town Administrator, for his cooperation and assistance during the progress of the work on this Code. It is hoped that their efforts and those of the publisher have resulted in a Code of Ordinances which will make the active law of the town readily accessible to all citizens and which will be a valuable tool in the day-to-day administration of the town's affairs. 
MUNICIPAL CODE CORPORATION 
Tallahassee, Florida

Ordinances that are not of a general and permanent nature are not codified in the Code Book and are considered "Omits." 
    In addition, by adding to this table with each supplement, users of this Code of Ordinances will be able to gain a more complete picture of the Code's historical evolution.

Chapter 1 - GENERAL PROVISIONS[1] 

Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
Editor's note- Ord. No. 2010-03, adopted Feb. 9, 2010, repealed the former Ch. 1, §§ 1-1-1-8, and enacted a new Ch. 1 as set out herein. The former Ch. 1 pertained to similar subject matter. See also the Code Comparative Table. 

Sec. 1-1. - How Code designated and cited. 
    The ordinances embraced in this and the following chapters and sections shall constitute and be designated the "Code of Ordinances, Town of Cheraw, South Carolina," and may be so cited. 
(Ord. No. 2010-03, 2-9-2010) 
Sec. 1-2. - Definitions and rules of construction. 
    In the construction of this Code and all ordinances of the town, the following definitions and rules of construction shall be observed, unless inconsistent with the manifest intent of the town council: 
    Computation of time. The time within which an act is to be done shall be computed by excluding the first day and including the last day; provided, however, that if the last day of the period so computed is a Saturday, a Sunday, or a legal holiday, such day shall be excluded and the time period shall run until the end of the next day which is not a Saturday, Sunday, or legal holiday. 
    Council, town council, governing body. The terms "the council," "town council," and "governing body" shall mean the town council of the Town of Cheraw. 
    County. The term "county" shall mean the County of Chesterfield, State of South Carolina. 
    Delegation of authority. Whenever a provision appears requiring the manager of a department or other officer of the town to do some act or perform some duty, it shall be construed to authorize the manager of the department or other officer to designate, delegate, and authorize subordinates to perform the required act or make the required inspection unless the terms of the provision of section designate otherwise. 
    Gender. Words importing one gender shall include the other genders, unless the context indicates otherwise. 
    Month. The word "month" shall mean a calendar month. 
    Name of official, board, commission, or agency. The name of any officer, board, commission, or agency, when appearing alone shall be construed as if the words "of the Town of Cheraw" were added. 
    Number. Words used in the singular include the plural and the plural shall include the singular. 
    Oath. The word "oath" shall be construed to include an affirmation in all cases in which, by law, an affirmation may be substituted for an oath, and in such cases the words "swear" and "sworn" shall be equivalent to the words "affirm" and "affirmed." 
    Or, and. "Or" may be read "and," and "and" may be read "of," if the sense requires it. 
    Owner. The word "owner," applied to a building or land, shall include any part owner, joint owner, tenant in common, tenant in partnership, joint tenant, or tenant by the entirety, of the whole or of a part of such building or land. 
    Person. The word "person" shall include a corporation, firm, partnership, association, organization and any other group acting as a unit, as well as an individual. 
    Personal property. The term "personal property" includes every species of property except real property, as herein defined. 
    Preceding, following. The terms "preceding" and "following" shall mean next before and next afterward, respectively. 
    Property. The term "property" shall include real and personal property. 
    Public place. The term "public place" shall mean any park, cemetery, school yard, or open space adjacent thereto, and any river or other waterway. 
    Real property, real estate. The terms "real property" and "real estate" shall include lands, tenements, and hereditaments. 
    Residence. A person's residence is his domicile. "Domicile" means a person's fixed home where he has an intention of returning when he is absent. A person has only one domicile. For voting purposes, a person has changed his domicile if he: 
(1)  Has abandoned his prior home; and 
(2)  Has established a new home, has a present intention to make that place his home, and has no present intention to leave that place. For voting purposes, a spouse may establish a separate domicile. (§ 7-1-25 of the S.C. Code of Laws 1976, as amended). 
    Roadway. The word "roadway" shall mean that portion of a street improved, designed or ordinarily used for vehicular travel. 
    Shall, may. The word "shall" is mandatory; "may" is permissive. 
    Sidewalk. The word "sidewalk" shall mean any portion of a street between the curb line and the adjacent property line, intended for the use of pedestrians. 
    State. The terms "the state" or "in this state" shall mean the State of South Carolina. 
    Street. The word "street" shall include avenues, boulevards, roads, alleys, lanes, bridges and approaches thereto and all other public thoroughfares in the town, and shall mean the entire width thereof between opposed abutting property lines; it shall be construed to include a sidewalk or footpath, unless the contrary is expressed or unless such construction would be inconsistent with the manifest intent of the town council. 
    Tenant, occupant. The terms "tenant" and "occupant" applied to a building or land, shall include any person holding a written or oral lease or who occupies the whole or a part of such building or land, either alone or with others. 
    Town, municipality. The terms "town" and "municipality" shall mean the Town of Cheraw, in the County of Chesterfield, State of South Carolina, except as otherwise provided. 
    Written, in writing. The words "written" and "in writing" shall include printing and any other mode of representing words and letters. 
    Year. The word "year" shall mean a calendar year. 
(Ord. No. 2010-03, 2-9-2010) 
Sec. 1-3. - Catchlines of sections. 
    The catchlines of the several sections of this Code are intended as mere catchwords to indicate the contents of the section and shall not be deemed or taken to be titles of such sections, nor as any part of the section, nor, unless expressly so provided, shall they be so deemed when any of such sections, including the catchlines, are amended or reenacted. 
(Ord. No. 2010-03, 2-9-2010) 
Sec. 1-4. - Effect of repeal of ordinances. 
(a)  The repeal of an ordinance shall not revive any ordinances in force before or at the time the ordinance repealed took effect. 
(b)  The repeal of an ordinance shall not affect any punishment or penalty incurred before the repeal took effect, nor any suit, prosecution or proceeding pending at the time of the repeal, for an offense committed or cause of action arising under the ordinance repealed. 
(Ord. No. 2010-03, 2-9-2010) 
Sec. 1-5. - Severability of parts of Code. 
    It is hereby declared to be the intention of the town council that if any section, paragraph, sentence, clause or phrase of this Code shall be declared unconstitutional by the valid judgment or decree of any court of competent jurisdiction, such unconstitutionality shall not affect any of the remaining phrases, clauses, sentences, paragraphs, and sections of this Code, since the same would have been enacted by the town council without the incorporation in this Code of any such unconstitutional phrase, clause, sentence, paragraph, or section. 
(Ord. No. 2010-03, 2-9-2010) 
Sec. 1-6. - General penalty; continuing violations. 
    Whenever in this Code, or in any ordinance of the town, or rule, regulation or order promulgated by any officer or agency of the town under authority duly vested in such officer or agency, any act is required, or the failure to do any act is declared to be unlawful or an offense or a misdemeanor, and no specific penalty is provided for the violation thereof, the violator of any such provisions of this Code, or any such ordinance, rule, regulation, or order shall be punished by a fine of not more than $500.00 or by imprisonment for not more than 30 days. Each day any violation of this Code, or any such ordinance, rule, regulation, or order shall constitute, except where otherwise provided, a separate offense. 
(Ord. No. 2010-03, 2-9-2010) 
Sec. 1-7. - Altering Code. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to change or amend, by additions or deletions, any part or portion of this Code, or to insert or delete pages or portions thereof, or to alter or tamper with such Code in any manner whatsoever which will cause the law of the town to be misrepresented thereby. 
(Ord. No. 2010-03, 2-9-2010) 
Sec. 1-8. - Certain ordinances not affected by Code. 
    Nothing in this Code shall affect any of the following ordinances: 
(1)  Any appropriation ordinance; 
(2)  Any ordinance levying or imposing taxes; 
(3)  Any ordinance requiring licenses or imposing license fees or taxes not in conflict herewith; 
(4)  Any ordinance providing for any public improvement; 
(5)  Any ordinance making any assessment; 
(6)  Any ordinance opening, establishing or re-establishing the lines, relocation, closing, or altering of any street or alley; 
(7)  Any ordinance establishing or changing the name of any street or alley; 
(8)  Any ordinance setting salaries, compensation or bonds of town employees and officials or members of town boards or commissions not in conflict herewith; 
(9)  Any zoning ordinance or ordinance making zoning map changes; 
(10)  Any ordinance regulating subdivisions, or approving subdivision plats, not in conflict herewith; 
(11)  Any ordinance establishing, extending, or contracting the corporate limits of the town; 
(12)  Any ordinance continued in force elsewhere in this Code; 
(13)  Ordinance adopted June 15, 1976 adopting the mayor-council form of government; and all such ordinance[s] are hereby recognized as continuing in full force and effect to the same extent as if set out in length in this Code. 
(Ord. No. 2010-03, 2-9-2010) 
Chapter 2 - ADMINISTRATION[1] 
Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
Editor's note- Ord. No. 2010-03, adopted Feb. 9, 2010, repealed the former Ch. 2, §§ 2-1-2-64, and enacted a new Ch. 2 as set out herein. The former Ch. 2 pertained to similar subject matter. See also the Code Comparative Table. 

ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Sec. 2-1. - Mayor-council form of government. 
    The form of government for the Town of Cheraw shall be the mayor-council form provided in S.C. Code § 5-11-10 et seq. as amended. 
(Ord. No. 2010-03, 2-9-2010) 
Sec. 2-2. - Composition of council. 
    The governing body of the Town of Cheraw shall consist of a mayor elected at large and six councilmembers elected one from each of six separate districts. 
(Ord. No. 2010-03, 2-9-2010) 
Sec. 2-3. - Eligibility for office. 
    To be eligible for the position of mayor or councilmember a person shall be a duly qualified elector of the town and the county under the constitution and statutes of the state. 
(Ord. No. 2010-03, 2-9-2010) 
Sec. 2-4. - Elections and tenure. 
(a)  General elections for mayor and town council shall be held on the first Tuesday following the first Monday of November in odd-numbered years. 
(b)  The mayor and councilmembers shall hold office for the period of four years and until their successors shall be duly elected and qualified. 
(c)  Terms shall be staggered so that not more than one-half of the council and mayor shall be elected in the same general election. 
(Ord. No. 2010-03, 2-9-2010) 
Sec. 2-5. - Oath of office. 
    Before entering upon the duties of their respective offices, the mayor and councilmembers shall take the following oath: 
I do solemnly swear (or affirm) that I am duly qualified, according to the Constitution of this State, to exercise the duties of the office to which I have been elected, and that I will, to the best of my ability, discharge the duties thereof, and preserve, protect, and defend the Constitution of this State and of the United States. 
As mayor (or councilmember) of the Town of Cheraw, I will equally, fairly, and impartially, to the best of my ability and skill, exercise the trust reposed in me, and will use my best endeavor to preserve the peace and carry into effect, according to law, the purposes for which I have been elected. So help me God. 
(Ord. No. 2010-03, 2-9-2010) 
Sec. 2-6. - Inauguration of members; mayor pro tempore. 
(a)  The newly elected mayor and/or council members shall take office on the first regularly scheduled council meeting in January following the certification of the results of any general election. For special elections any newly elected mayor and/or council members shall take office on the first regularly scheduled council meeting immediately following the certification of the results. 
(b)  The council shall, at the first meeting of the newly constituted council after any general election for municipal council, elect one of its members as mayor pro tempore for a term of two years. It shall be the duty of the mayor pro tempore to act as mayor during the absence or disability of the mayor, or in the case of a vacancy of mayor. 
(Ord. No. 2010-03, 2-9-2010; Ord. No. 2016-09, 2-9-2016) 
Sec. 2-7. - Duties of the mayor. 
(a)  The mayor or in his absence, the mayor pro tempore, shall preside at all meetings of the council. In the absence of both the mayor and the mayor pro tempore the council can elect by majority vote a council member to preside at the meeting. 
(b)  In addition the mayor shall have the following duties and powers: 
(1)  To appoint and, when he deems necessary for the good of the municipality, suspend or remove all municipal employees and appointive officers provided for by or under Chapters 1 through 17 of the Title 5 of the S.C. Code of Laws, except as otherwise provided by law, or personnel rules adopted pursuant to Chapters 1 through 17. He may authorize any administrative officer who is subject to his direction and supervision to exercise these powers with respect to subordinates in that officer's department, office, or agency. 
(2)  To direct and supervise the administration of all departments, offices, or agencies of the municipality except as otherwise provided by Chapters 1 through 17. 
(3)  To preside at meetings of the council and vote as other councilmen. 
(4)  To act to insure that all laws, provisions of Chapters 1 through 17 and ordinances of the council, subject to enforcement by him or by officers subject to this direction and supervision, are faithfully executed. 
(5)  To prepare and submit the annual budget and capital program to the council. 
(6)  To submit to the council and make available to the public a complete report on the finances and administrative activities of the municipality as of the end of each fiscal year. 
(7)  To make such other reports as the council may require concerning the operations of municipal departments, offices, and agencies subject to his direction and supervision. (§ 5-9-30 of the S.C. Code of Laws, 1976 as amended). 
(8)  All departments, offices and agencies under the direction and supervision of the mayor shall be administered by an officer appointed by and subject to the direction and supervision of the mayor. (§ 5-9-40 of the S.C. Code of Laws, 1976 as amended). 
(Ord. No. 2010-03, 2-9-2010) 
Sec. 2-8. - Duties of the council. 
(a)  The council may establish municipal departments, offices, and agencies, in addition to those created by Chapters 1 through 17 of Title 5 of the S.C. Code of Laws 1976, as amended, and may prescribe the functions of all departments, offices, and agencies, except that no function assigned by law to a particular department, office, or agency may be discontinued or assigned to any other agency. 
(b)  The council shall have the right at all times to develop the duties of all officers and employees of the town and, from time to time, impose such additional duties as it may deem proper. 
(c)  The mayor and council may employ an administrator to assist the mayor in his office. 
(d)  The council shall adopt an annual budget for the operation of the municipality and capital improvements. 
(Ord. No. 2010-03, 2-9-2010) 
Sec. 2-9. - Compensation. 
(a)  The annual salary of the mayor shall be $5,400.00 and each council member's annual salary shall be $4,800.00. 
(b)  No ordinance changing such salary shall become effective until the date of commencement of the terms of councilmembers elected at the next general election following such change. 
(c)  The mayor and councilmembers may also received payments for actual expenses incurred in the performance of their official duties. 
(Ord. No. 2010-03, 2-9-2010) 
Sec. 2-10. - Meetings of council. 
(a)  Regular meetings of the town council shall be held on the second Tuesday in each month unless rescheduled by the mayor or changed by a majority vote of members present at any regular or special meeting. Each regular meeting of the council shall be called to order at 5:30 p.m. 
(b)  Special meetings of council may be held on the call of the mayor or of a majority vote of the members. Notice of a special meeting shall be given immediately to all available members and the media by the town clerk. 
(c)  All regular and special meetings of council shall be opened to the public. 
(Ord. No. 2010-03, 2-9-2010) 
Sec. 2-11. - Conference or executive sessions. 
(a)  Town council may have conference or executive sessions as permitted by the South Carolina Freedom of Information Act at such times and in such places as may be deemed necessary and in the public interest. 
(b)  The reasons for the executive session must be clearly stated for the record and no public vote shall be taken upon any matter under discussion at any such session. 
(c)  A vote of council in a public meeting shall be necessary to call a conference meeting. 
(Ord. No. 2010-03, 2-9-2010) 
Sec. 2-12. - Quorum and rules of order. 
(a)  A majority of the council members serving constitutes a quorum for the conduct of business at any meeting. 
(b)  The mayor or mayor pro tempore shall preside, except that in the absence of both, the members shall elect a presiding member. 
(c)  Except as otherwise required by state law or ordinance, all proceedings of council shall be governed by Robert's Rules of Order. 
(Ord. No. 2010-03, 2-9-2010) 
Sec. 2-13. - Voting requirements. 
(a)  All actions of council must be made by majority vote of the members present at a public meeting. 
(b)  Every member of council present shall vote on every question except where required to refrain from voting by state law. 
(c)  The vote on every question shall be by voice vote and recorded in the council minutes by the town clerk. 
(d)  No member of council may leave the council chamber while in public session without permission of the presiding officer. 
(e)  Should the vote of all present result in a tie, the question shall be decided in the negative. 
(Ord. No. 2010-03, 2-9-2010) 
Sec. 2-14. - Minutes of meetings. 
    The town clerk shall keep the minutes of all meetings of council, except executive sessions, which shall be a matter of permanent public record. It shall be the responsibility of the town clerk, or his or her designee, to maintain records on all town committees, boards, and commissions. 
(Ord. No. 2010-03, 2-9-2010) 
Sec. 2-15. - Agenda. 
    Matters to be considered by council at a regular meeting must be placed on a written agenda by the chief administrative officer and publicly posted by the town clerk by noon of the day preceding the meeting. 
(Ord. No. 2010-03, 2-9-2010) 
Sec. 2-16. - Appearance of citizens. 
    Any person is entitled to an appearance before council at any regular meeting concerning a municipal matter with the exception of personnel matters. To be placed on the council agenda a person will be required to adhere to the following: 
(1)  Persons desiring to speak must notify the town clerk or town administrator by noon of the Friday before the regularly scheduled council meeting. 
(2)  Persons must specify what topic they intend to speak about. 
(3)  Persons will be limited to five minutes to address council. The mayor or presiding officer may grant the speaker additional time if circumstances warrant it. 
(4)  Persons that speak on other matters not specified will be deemed out of order and will not be allowed to continue speaking. 
(5)  Mayor and council members have the right to answer questions that may be posed. 
    Persons not placed on the agenda will also have the right to speak at the end of the town council meetings during a citizen comment period. The citizen comment period is designed and intended to allow members of the public to provide information directly to the town council. Other than asking a question to clarify a statement council members will refrain from entering into a dialogue with the speaker. This time on the agenda is not intended to be a discussion between town council and the speaker and should not be intended for that purpose. Persons wishing to make comments during this time will need to observe the following: 
(1)  Person should approach the podium and state their full name and address before addressing the town council. 
(2)  All speakers must conduct themselves in a professional manner. 
(3)  All speakers will be limited to three minutes to speak. This time allotment may not be transferred to anyone else. The town's clerk/treasurer will notify the speaker if they exceed their three minutes to talk. 
(4)  Speakers will refrain from using: profanity; language likely to incite violence or outbursts from the audience; language that is disruptive to the orderly process of the meeting; engaging in conversations with individual council members; making comments of a personal nature regarding others; shouting, yelling, or screaming. 
(5)  Speakers should understand that the town council cannot deliberate on any questions presented by the speaker if the question or topic is not posted on the agenda. 
(Ord. No. 2010-03, 2-9-2010; Ord. No. 2018-02, 11-14-2017) 
Sec. 2-17. - Order of business. 
    The order of proceedings of the council shall be as follows: 
(1)  Prayer. 
(2)  Pledge to the flag. 
(3)  Approval of minutes of the preceding meeting. 
(4)  Approval of financial reports. 
(5)  Special presentations. 
(6)  Ordinances already in possession of the council shall be taken for a final reading. 
(7)  Introduction of ordinances or resolutions. 
(8)  Reports from special council committees. 
(9)  Department reports. 
(10)  Miscellaneous business not included in any of the preceding categories. 
(11)  Citizen comments. 
(12)  Executive session (when applicable). 
(13)  Adjournment. 
(Ord. No. 2010-03, 2-9-2010) 
Sec. 2-18. - Personal interest of members. 
    No member of council shall vote on any question of a private nature in the event of which such member is personally or pecuniary interested. 
(Ord. No. 2010-03, 2-9-2010) 
Sec. 2-19. - Special committees. 
    Council may appoint a special committee to assist in or hold a public hearing for council at any time upon any matter pending before it. Minutes or reports of hearings by special committees shall be filed with the town clerk as public records. 
(Ord. No. 2010-03, 2-9-2010) 
Sec. 2-20. - Ordinances and resolutions. 
(a)  The town council shall act by ordinance in all matters required by law to be done by ordinance, including: 
(1)  The adoption or amending of an administrative code or the establishment, alteration, or abolition of a municipal department, office, or agency; 
(2)  The establishment of a fine or other penalty or the establishment of any rule or regulation in which a fine or other penalty is imposed for violations; 
(3)  The adoption of budgets or the levy of taxes; 
(4)  The granting, renewal, or extension of franchises; 
(5)  The authorization to borrow money or issue bonds; 
(6)  The selling, leasing, or contracting to sell or lease any lands of the municipality; 
(7)  The annexation of property into the town limits; and 
(8)  The amending or repealing of any ordinances listed above. 
(b)  In all other matters council may act either by ordinance or resolution, oral or written, recorded in the minutes. 
(Ord. No. 2010-03, 2-9-2010) 
Sec. 2-21. - Form of ordinances and resolutions. 
(a)  Every proposed ordinance shall be introduced in writing and in the form required for final adoption which shall include: 
(1)  A title briefly describing the content; 
(2)  Findings, reasons, or basis for the ordinance, if desired and appropriate; 
(3)  An enacting clause; 
(4)  Citation of any ordinance repealed; 
(5)  The provisions of the ordinance including section numbers if the ordinance is to be codified or amends and existing codified ordinance; 
(6)  The effective date of the ordinance; 
(7)  The approval of the town attorney as to form and the assignment of an ordinance number; and 
(8)  Space for the signatures of the mayor, members of council and the town clerk. 
(b)  Written resolutions shall be in such similar form as deemed appropriate by the town attorney. 
(Ord. No. 2010-03, 2-9-2010) 
Sec. 2-22. - Introduction and enactment of ordinances and resolutions. 
(a)  Introduction. 
(1)  An ordinance or resolution may be proposed by any member of council. 
(2)  Every proposed ordinance must be introduced in writing and in the form required for final adoption. 
(3)  A voice motion of a member of council shall be considered to be the introduction of an oral resolution which shall require no written record other than a notation of the town clerk in the council minutes. A resolution proposed in writing shall be introduced in the same manner as an ordinance. 
(b)  Enactment. 
(1)  No ordinance shall be adopted until it shall have been read two times on two separate days with at least six days between each reading. 
(2)  Emergency ordinances may be adopted on one reading without notice or hearing by affirmative vote of one-third of the members present. An emergency ordinance may not levy taxes, relate to a franchise or a service rate and shall expire on the 61st day following enactment. 
(3)  The introduction and reading of any ordinance shall be by the reading of the title only unless full reading is requested by a member of council. 
(4)  The second reading of an ordinance shall be by title only and shall be for the purpose of passing the same to have the full force of law. Amendments and privileged motions are appropriate at this time and shall be made prior to the second reading. 
(5)  Upon final adoption by vote of council, an ordinance shall be signed by the mayor or presiding member, members of council, and the town clerk, who shall file the original as a matter of public record. 
(6)  After the introduction of an ordinance, any member of council or any citizen of the town interested therein may request a public hearing which may be held at any time designated by council prior to final adoption. 
(Ord. No. 2010-03, 2-9-2010) 
ARTICLE II. - CLERK/TREASURER 

Sec. 2-23. - Appointment; term; salary. 
    The town clerk/treasurer shall be appointed by the town council, and, shall serve said office indefinitely or until a successor is appointed and qualified. The clerk shall receive a salary and expenses at a sum to be fixed by council for any service performed as clerk. 
(Ord. No. 2010-03, 2-9-2010) 
Sec. 2-24. - Bond. 
    The town clerk, prior to entering into the performance of the duties of the office, shall enter into a bond with good and sufficient surety, conditioned for the faithful and honest performance of the duties of such office. The cost of such bond shall be paid by the town. 
(Ord. No. 2010-03, 2-9-2010) 
Sec. 2-25. - General duties. 
    The town clerk/treasurer shall: 
(1)  Be the general accountant for the town; 
(2)  Attend all meetings of the town council; 
(3)  Take and maintain all official minutes of council meetings and record in a suitable manner; 
(4)  Provide council all communications addressed to it through the town clerk; 
(5)  Have charge of and be responsible for the preservation of all papers, records, and documents of every description pertaining to the town; 
(6)  Shall be the custodian of the official town seal; 
(7)  Issue all notices, personal and general, which the interest, convenience, laws and orders of the town require in the administration of its government; 
(8)  Communicate to the council all information such officer may acquire which may contribute to the efficiency of the government and the welfare of the people; 
(9)  Shall collect all taxes, fines, fees and licenses and shall pay all legal checks drawn upon the town; 
(10)  Shall receive and receipt for all revenues of the town from all sources; 
(11)  Shall provide a monthly financial statement to the council and any such other information as may be requested by the council; and 
(12)  Shall perform all duties that are now or may hereafter be required by law. 
(Ord. No. 2010-03, 2-9-2010) 
Sec. 2-26. - Signing and attesting ordinance and other documents. 
    The town clerk shall sign and attest all ordinances, deeds, contracts, and other documents. 
(Ord. No. 2010-03, 2-9-2010) 
Sec. 2-27. - Removal of documents from clerk's custody. 
    No original paper or document of the town shall be taken from the custody of the town clerk, except upon order of the mayor or town administrator. 
(Ord. No. 2010-03, 2-9-2010) 
ARTICLE III. - TOWN ATTORNEY 

Sec. 2-28. - Appointment or election of town attorney. 
    There shall be elected annually by the town council at the time of the regular election of town offices a lawyer to serve as town attorney. 
(Ord. No. 2010-03, 2-9-2010) 
Sec. 2-29. - Qualifications. 
    The town attorney shall be an attorney at law and shall be licensed to practice before the highest court in the state and shall have met the provisions for and been issued a license to practice law by the authorized authority. The town attorney shall have his place of business located within the corporate town limits of Cheraw. 
(Ord. No. 2010-03, 2-9-2010; Ord. No. 2011-06, 3-8-2011) 
Sec. 2-30. - Term. 
    The town attorney shall serve at the pleasure of the town council and be appointed for a two-year term. 
(Ord. No. 2010-03, 2-9-2010; Ord. No. 2011-06, 3-8-2011) 
Sec. 2-31. - General duties. 
    It shall be the duty of the town attorney, whenever called upon by the town council or when the necessity arises, to give his advice and direction to the town council or any member thereof or to the town clerk and treasurer and chief of police on any and all legal questions which may arise in the course of the administration of the town government or in the discharge of the duties of their respective offices; and whenever required to do so by council he shall give his legal opinion in writing. He shall draw or supervise the drawing or drafting of all ordinances and other instruments of writing relating to the business of the town when required to do so by the town councilor any member thereof, shall, whenever notified so to do, attend the municipal court of the town and meetings of the town council, shall take charge of all prosecutions of offenders and conduct the correspondence on all legal subjects which it may become necessary to investigate and generally shall be careful that the town council and officers fall into no error of law in the administration and management of the business and affairs of the town. 
(Ord. No. 2010-03, 2-9-2010) 
Sec. 2-32. - Duty to advise and assist mayor, council, and town officers. 
    When requested, the town attorney shall give advice, direction and assistance to the mayor, town council, standing committees and special committees and other officers duly charged with the administration of the town government. The town attorney shall likewise advise and assist the police officers in the performance of their duties. 
(Ord. No. 2010-03, 2-9-2010) 
Sec. 2-33. - Prosecution and defense of actions; appearance in legal proceedings. 
    The town attorney shall prosecute and defend all civil actions in which the town may be a party and shall prosecute on behalf of the town, all criminal cases in the municipal court whenever requested to do so by the mayor or council. The town attorney shall appear on behalf of the town and its officers in all legal proceedings to which any have an interest as an official of the town. 
(Ord. No. 2010-03, 2-9-2010) 
Sec. 2-34. - Drafting ordinances and instruments; legal correspondence. 
    The town attorney, when directed by the council or town administrator, shall prepare the draft of any ordinance or instrument in writing which the mayor and council may desire, and shall conduct the correspondence of the town on all legal subjects. 
(Ord. No. 2010-03, 2-9-2010) 
Sec. 2-35. - Compensation. 
    The salary of the town attorney shall be provided by the town council in the annual appropriation ordinance. 
(Ord. No. 2010-03, 2-9-2010) 
ARTICLE IV. - TOWN ADMINISTRATOR 

Sec. 2-36. - Appointment. 
    The mayor and town council shall appoint a town administrator and fix his or her compensation. He or she shall be appointed solely on the basis of his or her executive and administrative qualifications. 
(Ord. No. 2010-03, 2-9-2010) 
Sec. 2-37. - Term. 
    The town administrator shall serve at the pleasure of the mayor and town council for an indefinite term. 
(Ord. No. 2010-03, 2-9-2010) 
Sec. 2-38. - Bond. 
    The town administrator shall enter into an approved bond in such sum as prescribed by the mayor and town council, conditioned for the faithful and honest performance of such office. The cost of such bond shall be paid by the town. 
(Ord. No. 2010-03, 2-9-2010) 
Sec. 2-39. - General duties. 
    The town administrator shall be responsible to the mayor for the proper administration of the policies and affairs of the town and to that end shall have the power and authority and be required to: 
(1)  Direct, supervise, and coordinate administrative activities and operations; 
(2)  Appoint department heads with approval of the mayor and council; 
(3)  Appoint other town employees with approval of the mayor; 
(4)  Suspend or dismiss department heads with approval of the mayor and council; 
(5)  Suspend or dismiss other employees with approval of the mayor; 
(6)  Prepare and submit an annual operating budget and capital program to the mayor and council for their consideration and approval; 
(7)  Have responsibility for administration of annual operating budget after adoption; 
(8)  Prepare and annually update, a five-year capital improvement program and budget; 
(9)  Recommend and administer personnel policies, classification, compensation, and evaluations for all employees; 
(10)  Monitor the financial condition of the town and estimate present and future financial needs; 
(11)  Prepare a quarterly analysis on personnel and administrative activities; 
(12)  Prepare a quarterly analysis on the financial position of the town; 
(13)  Combine or consolidate job positions within departments as necessary or prudent to maximize manpower utilization and efficiency; 
(14)  Recommend and administer policies governing purchasing procedures and inventory control; 
(15)  Authorize the purchase of services, materials, supplies, and equipment which do not require the taking of bids, provided such items are appropriated in the town's various fund accounts; 
(16)  Authorize shifts in departmental budget line items provided overall departmental budget appropriations do not change with approval of the mayor and council; 
(17)  Investigate complaints concerning administrative matters and personnel performance with the heads of departments; 
(18)  Prepare and submit to the mayor and town council at the end of each fiscal year a complete annual report of the finances and administrative activities of the town; 
(19)  May, with the approval of the mayor, delegate to other administrative officers, subject to his or her direction and supervision, the authority to exercise specified duties and responsibilities as may be considered appropriate; 
(20)  Provide the mayor and town council with information, guidance, and leadership in matters of policy determination; 
(21)  Actively investigate the opportunities and position of the town in relation to grants, state and county-shared services and resources and prepare the necessary documents upon approval of the mayor and council. 
(Ord. No. 2010-03, 2-9-2010) 
Sec. 2-40. - Removal from office. 
    The town administrator may be removed from office by a majority vote of the mayor and council. Those members voting for removal shall state their reasons for such vote. The action of the mayor and council in removing the town administrator shall be final. In all cases, except for misconduct in office, the town administrator shall receive 90 days notice of his removal or severance pay for 90 days where such removal is made effective immediately by a majority vote of the mayor and council. 
(Ord. No. 2010-03, 2-9-2010) 
Sec. 2-41. - Communication between administrator and council. 
    The town administrator shall relate to and communicate with the mayor and council on any and all problems, situations, and conditions which arise concerning any department or activity of the town which, in the opinion of the administrator is of significance. Except for the purpose of inquiry, the mayor and town council shall communicate directly with the town administrator in any and all matters concerning any department or activity of the town. No member of town council shall give orders to any subordinate of the town administrator except in case of an emergency. 
(Ord. No. 2010-03, 2-9-2010) 
ARTICLE V. - ARTS COMMISSION 

Sec. 2-42. - Creation; powers. 
(a)  There is created in the town, the Cheraw Arts Commission. 
(b)  The commission shall develop, promote, and coordinate arts activities in the community. More specifically, the commission shall have the authority to sponsor cooperative planning, research, fund raising, and public education programs, to administer property, and undertake other services and programs deemed necessary to encourage participation and appreciation of the arts by all citizens of the area. The powers granted in this section shall be exercised only by recommendation to and with approval of the director of the department of parks, recreation, and cultural arts. 
(Ord. No. 2010-03, 2-9-2010) 
Sec. 2-43. - Arts-Definition. 
    The term "arts" is understood to include, but not be limited to, the performing, visual, and literary arts, as well as the allied arts of architecture and historic preservation, landscape architecture, industrial design, and production crafts. 
(Ord. No. 2010-03, 2-9-2010) 
Sec. 2-44. - Responsibilities. 
    It shall be the responsibility of the commission to: 
(1)  Act as sponsor for programs and services made available through the South Carolina Arts Commission and through local arts resources. 
(2)  Survey artists and cultural resources in the area. 
(3)  Encourage cooperation with and community support for existing organizations involved in arts activities. 
(4)  Act as a clearinghouse for the collection and dissemination of information among existing arts groups by developing a mailing list and establishing a close working relationship with local new media. 
(5)  Encourage the expansion of arts activities in the school curriculum. 
(6)  Identify available space in the community for arts functions. 
(7)  Work to secure government support for the arts at all levels. 
(8)  Seek out and encourage contributions and grants to the arts from private and public sources and to receive and allocate such funds. 
(9)  Maintain liaison with neighboring arts councils, as well as state and federal arts commissions. 
(Ord. No. 2010-03, 2-9-2010) 
Sec. 2-45. - Membership. 
(a)  The commission shall be composed of 12 members to be appointed by the mayor, initially by recommendation of the steering committee and subsequently by recommendation of the current commissioners. Commission members shall serve without compensation. 
(b)  The 12 members of the commission shall be residents of Cheraw and the total membership shall be divided as follows: 
(1)  One representative of the Cheraw Parks, Recreation and Tourism Commission, recommended by its chairperson. 
(2)  One representative of the Chesterfield County School District administrative offices, recommended by the county school superintendent. 
(3)  One representative of Northeastern Technical College, recommended by its president. 
(4)  Nine members appointed at-large. 
(Ord. No. 2010-03, 2-9-2010) 
Sec. 2-46. - Terms. 
    The term of office shall be three years. Terms shall be staggered to provide for the appointment of three new members whose terms shall be effective on the fourth Monday of May in each year. Any commissioner may succeed himself. 
(Ord. No. 2010-03, 2-9-2010) 
Sec. 2-47. - Officers. 
    Immediately upon appointment of the commission, it shall organize by electing an executive committee to be composed of a chairman, vice-chairman, secretary, and a treasurer. The term of each office shall be one year and no officer shall serve in the same capacity for more than three consecutive terms. 
(Ord. No. 2010-03, 2-9-2010) 
Sec. 2-48. - Committees. 
    The commission shall create and the chairman shall appoint those committees deemed necessary to further its purpose and execute its authority. These committee members need not be members of the Cheraw Arts Commission. 
(Ord. No. 2010-03, 2-9-2010) 
Sec. 2-49. - Fiscal policy. 
(a)  The commission shall propose and adopt its budget under the direction of the director of the department of parks, recreation and cultural arts. The commission shall seek funds for its operation and programs from any and all legitimate sources including town, county, state, and federal government; local, regional, and national business establishments; foundations; and the citizens of the community. The commission shall not enter into any contracts involving financial liability or incur any indebtedness on the part of the town except upon written authority from the mayor and council, but the commission shall have the power to enter into agreements with any government agency or with any private individuals or corporations for the purpose of effectuating its objectives, where no liability of the town is involved. 
(b)  Although the commission may solicit and receive donations, operate concessions, and accept and receive funds from government and private sources, it shall not disburse any funds. Such funds are to be disbursed by and through the town. 
(Ord. No. 2010-03, 2-9-2010) 
Sec. 2-50. - Cooperation with existing commissions. 
    The arts commission shall cooperate and coordinate its activities with the parks, recreation and tourism commission and other existing town and county commissions. 
(Ord. No. 2010-03, 2-9-2010) 
Sec. 2-51. - Meeting procedures. 
    Meetings of the commission shall be conducted according to Robert's Rules of Order. A quorum shall consist of a majority of the members of the commission and a quorum must be present to officially conduct business. Minutes of the commission meetings shall be kept in written form and passed from chairman to chairman. The chairman shall report at least quarterly to the mayor as to the activities, programs, and needs of the Cheraw Arts Commission and further shall make such other reports as requested by the mayor, town administrator, or the director of the department of parks, recreation, and cultural arts. 
(Ord. No. 2010-03, 2-9-2010) 
ARTICLE VI. - REDEVELOPMENT COMMISSION 

Sec. 2-52. - Creation; duties. 
    There is established pursuant to Act 451 of 1985 of the S.C. General Assembly a redevelopment commission with all of the powers and duties of said Act. 
(Ord. No. 2010-03, 2-9-2010) 
Sec. 2-53. - Membership. 
    The redevelopment commission shall consist of seven members to be appointed by the mayor and town council. Members shall be appointed for two-year staggered terms. The town administrator and community development director shall serve as ex-officio members. 
(Ord. No. 2010-03, 2-9-2010) 
Sec. 2-54. - Responsibility for operating commission. 
    The town council may at any time abolish the office of commissioners and assume the responsibility for operating the commission. 
(Ord. No. 2010-03, 2-9-2010) 
Sec. 2-55. - Powers. 
(a)  The redevelopment commission will have all powers necessary or appropriate to prevent or eliminate slums and urban blight. It will prepare redevelopment plans and carry out such redevelopment projects. 
(b)  The commission may temporarily lease, rent, operate, and maintain real property in a redevelopment area. 
(c)  With the approval of the town council, the commission may also sell, exchange, transfer, assign, subdivide, retain for its own use, pledge, or encumber or dispose of any real or personal property and enter into contracts regarding the real property. 
(d)  The redevelopment commission is empowered to borrow money, to issue bonds, and to provide security for such bonds. The commission is further authorized to apply for an [and] accept forms of financial assistance for any source, public or private. 
(Ord. No. 2010-03, 2-9-2010) 
Sec. 2-56. - Financing incentives. 
(a)  Bonds may be issued where the principal and interest are payable exclusively from the income, proceeds, and revenues that accrue from the redevelopment project. The bonds may be additionally secured by a pledge of any loan, grant, or contribution from the federal or state government. A redevelopment project may also be mortgaged to secure the bonds. The redevelopment commission may also do any other acts necessary, convenient, or desirable to secure its bonds, or take any action that will tend to make the bonds more marketable. 
(b)  Bonds of a commission are declared to be issued for an essential public and governmental purpose and together with interest thereon and income wherefrom shall be exempt from all taxes except inheritance, estate, or transfer taxes. 
(Ord. No. 2010-03, 2-9-2010) 
Sec. 2-57. - Issuance of bonds. 
(a)  Prior to issuing any bonds, the redevelopment commission shall publish a notice in a newspaper of general circulation. Any interested person may within 20 days after such publication, but not thereafter, challenge the issuance of such bonds by action initiated in the circuit court in the area in which the redevelopment commission is located. If so such action is initiated, provided the bonds are issued not later than six months after the publication, the bond issue shall be conclusively presumed to be valid and binding. 
(b)  Neither the commissioners nor any person executing the bond shall be liable personally on the bonds by reason of the issuance. The bonds and other obligations shall not be a debt of the town or the state and neither the town nor the state is liable on them. In no event will such bonds or obligations be payable out of any funds or properties other than those of the redevelopment commission acquired for the purposes of the community development law. 
(Ord. No. 2010-03, 2-9-2010) 
Sec. 2-58. - Redevelopment plan. 
(a)  The redevelopment plan by the commission should provide for land uses and building requirements that are designed with the general purpose of accomplishing a coordinated and harmonious development. The development should promote health, safety, and general welfare of the community. 
(b)  The commission must submit the redevelopment plan to the mayor and town council for approval. The commission shall also conduct a public hearing prior to adopting the plan. 
(c)  The redevelopment plan shall include the following: 
(1)  The boundaries of the redevelopment area; 
(2)  Land use plan of the area; 
(3)  Standards of population densities; 
(4)  Land coverage; 
(5)  Building intensities in the redevelopment area; 
(6)  A preliminary site plan; 
(7)  A statement of any proposed changes in zoning ordinances, maps, street layouts, or street levels; 
(8)  A statement of the estimated cost and method of financing the redevelopment; 
(9)  A statement of necessary controls; and 
(10)  A statement of the proposed method of relocating families displaced by the redevelopment plan. 
(Ord. No. 2010-03, 2-9-2010) 
Sec. 2-59. - Designated areas. 
    The redevelopment commission established by this article shall exercise its power within the corporate limits of the Town of Cheraw. 
(Ord. No. 2010-03, 2-9-2010) 
ARTICLE VII. - MUNICIPAL AIRPORT COMMISSION 

Sec. 2-60. - Function and authority. 
(a)  There is hereby created in the town the Cheraw Municipal Airport Commission. Its function shall be to consider the airport needs of Cheraw and the surrounding area and to make recommendations concerning the same to the mayor, town council, and town administrator. 
(b)  The commission shall study and compile the needs of the Cheraw Municipal Airport and together with the airport manager/operator shall recommend by April 1 of each year the annual budget and, upon approval by the town council, shall help to implement the same. The annual budget shall include both operating and capital expenses, and budgeted revenue sources shall include revenues from the town's general fund, from donations, and from any state and federal government grant programs. The commission shall be furnished a monthly report of the revenue and disbursements of the Cheraw Municipal Airport by the town treasurer. 
(c)  The commission may solicit and receive donations, and/or services, operate concessions, and may accept and receive funds and/or services from any governmental or other source, but they cannot disburse any funds. All funds and payment of bills for goods or services concerning the airport shall be disbursed in accordance with procurement requirements of the Town of Cheraw. 
(d)  The commission shall not enter into any contracts involving financial liability or incur any indebtedness on the part of the town except upon written authority from the mayor and council, but the commission shall have the authority to enter into agreements with any government agency or with any private individuals or corporation for the purpose of effectuating its objectives, where no liability of the town is involved. 
(Ord. No. 2010-03, 2-9-2010) 
Sec. 2-61. - Membership; terms of office. 
(a)  The commission shall consist of seven regular members, one of whom shall be elected chairman by the full membership. The airport manager/operator shall be a non-voting, ex-officio member of the commission. 
(b)  Members shall be appointed for two-year, staggered, terms by the mayor and shall expire on June 30. Members shall continue to serve until their successors are appointed. 
(c)  Members shall serve without compensation. 
(Ord. No. 2010-03, 2-9-2010) 
Sec. 2-62. - Organization; meetings; rules; reports. 
(a)  The commission shall meet annually to elect from their group a chairman, vice-chairman, and secretary-treasurer. Officers shall serve for serve for one-year terms but may be re-elected. The commission shall meet on a regular basis and on call by the chairman at a time and place designated by the chairman. 
(b)  Robert's Rules of Order shall be followed as a procedure guide for all meetings. A quorum shall consist of a majority of the members of the commission and must be present to officially conduct business. Any member having three unexcused absences during the course of a year may be asked to resign from the commission. 
(c)  The chairman may appoint such temporary committees from within or outside the membership if he may deem necessary to affect the function of the commission. 
(d)  Any member who resigns shall be replaced by appointment by the mayor for the unexpired term of the resigned member. In the event of the resignation of the chairman from the commission, he shall be replaced on the commission by appointment by the mayor, and the members shall elect a new chairman. 
(e)  The chairman and the airport manager/operator together shall report at least quarterly to the mayor and council as to the activities, programs, and needs of the Cheraw Municipal Airport and further shall make available such other reports as requested by the mayor and council and/or the town administrator. 
(f)  Minutes of commission meets shall be kept in written form and passed from chairman to chairman. Copies of the minutes shall be forwarded to the mayor and town council. 
(Ord. No. 2010-03, 2-9-2010) 
ARTICLE VIII. - COMMISSION ON PARENTING 

Sec. 2-63. - Creation; powers and duties. 
(a)  There is created in the town a commission which shall be named the Cheraw Commission on Parenting. Its function shall be to consider the responsibility of raising capable young people in the Cheraw area. The commission will explore resources on effective parenting available to the town, present community-wide programs to raise the consciousness of parents as to the problems of raising capable young people, and work with established social agencies to refer parents and young people with specific needs to the proper sources. The commission on parenting also will work with schools, law enforcement, and recreational groups in developing its programs and meeting the needs of parents and young people in Cheraw. 
(b)  The commission shall make a recommendation of any person to be employed by the Cheraw Commission on Parenting. All such recommendations shall develop a job description for any proposed employee and submit it to the mayor and town council for approval. The commission shall approve, assist, guide, and direct volunteers and any employees in programs and activities relating to parenting. 
(c)  The commission shall study and compile the needs of the parenting commission and shall recommend by March 1 of each year the annual budget and, upon approval, shall help to implement [the] same. The annual budget may include both operating and capital expenses, and budgeted revenue sources may include revenues from the town's general fund, from donations, and from any state and federal grant programs. The commission shall be furnished a monthly report of the revenues and disbursements of the Cheraw Commission on Parenting. 
(d)  The commission may solicit and receive donations, operate concessions, and accept and receive funds from any governmental and other source, but cannot disburse any funds. All funds and payment of bills for goods or services shall be disbursed in accordance with South Carolina General Assembly Act 283 of 1975 (Home Rule Act), Part II (Municipal Government) Article 4. 
(e)  The commission shall not enter into any contracts involving financial liability or incur any indebtedness on the part of the town except upon written authority from the mayor and council, but the commission shall have power to enter into agreements with any government agency or with any private individuals or corporation for the purpose of effectuating its objectives, where no liability of the town is involved. 
(Ord. No. 2010-03, 2-9-2010) 
Sec. 2-64. - Membership. 
(a)  The commission, except for the original commission, shall consist of nine regular members, one of whom shall be elected chairman by the full membership. Ex-officio members may be appointed from time to time by the mayor and council. 
(b)  Members shall be appointed for a three-year, staggered term by the mayor and terms of members, other than the original commission, shall expire on June 30. Members shall continue to service until their successors are appointed. A member shall continue to serve until their successors are appointed. A member may be appointed to succeed himself. 
(c)  Commission members shall serve without compensation. 
(d)  Any member who may resign shall be replaced by appointment by the mayor for the remainder of the regular term of the resigned member except in the event of the resignation of the chairman who may be replaced on the commission by appointment by the mayor and the members shall elect a new chairman. 
(Ord. No. 2010-03, 2-9-2010) 
Sec. 2-65. - Officers. 
    The commission shall meet in July of each year to organize and elect from their group a chairman, vice-chairman, a secretary, and a chairman of publicity. Officers shall serve for one year. 
(Ord. No. 2010-03, 2-9-2010) 
Sec. 2-66. - Meetings. 
(a)  The commission shall meet by call of the chairman at a time and place designated by the chairman. 
(b)  Robert's Rules of Order shall be followed. A quorum shall consist of a majority of the members of the commission and a quorum must be present to officially conduct business. Any member having three unexcused absences may be asked to resign from the commission. 
(c)  Minutes of commission meetings shall be kept in written form and passed from chairman to chairman. Copies of the minutes shall be forwarded to the mayor and council. 
(Ord. No. 2010-03, 2-9-2010) 
Sec. 2-67. - Committees. 
(a)  The chairman may appoint such temporary committees from time to time and such standing committees as he may deem necessary to effect the function of the commission. 
(b)  A standing committee to be known as the youth center committee, and its chairman, shall be appointed by the mayor and town council to serve at their pleasure and shall be responsible for the organization and operation of a youth activities center and such other duties as may be assigned to the committee from time to time by the mayor and council. The chairman of the youth center committee shall report directly to the mayor and council. The chairman of the commission on parenting shall be an ex-officio member of the youth center committee, and the chairman of the youth center committee shall be an ex-officio member of the commission on parenting. 
(Ord. No. 2010-03, 2-9-2010) 
Sec. 2-68. - Reports. 
    The chairman shall report at least quarterly to the mayor and town council as to the activities, programs, and needs of the commission and further shall make such other reports as requested by the mayor and council or the town administrator. 
(Ord. No. 2010-03, 2-9-2010) 
ARTICLE IX. - TOWN COMMISSIONS GENERALLY 

Sec. 2-69. - Membership and terms. 
    The town council may change the number of members of any town commission and their terms of office from time to time by vote at any council meeting, but in no event shall any commission be composed at any time of less than three members. 
(Ord. No. 2010-03, 2-9-2010) 
Chapter 3 - ANIMALS[1] 

Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
Editor's note- Ord. No. 2010-03, adopted Feb. 9, 2010, repealed the former Ch. 3, §§ 3-0-3-27, and enacted a new Ch. 3 as set out herein. The former Ch. 3 pertained to similar subject matter. See also the Code Comparative Table. 

Sec. 3-1. - Purpose. 
    The purpose of this chapter is to promote harmonious relationships in the interaction between man and animal by: 
(1)  Protecting animals from improper use, abuse, neglect, exploitation, and inhumane treatment and health hazards; 
(2)  Delineating the animal owner's responsibility for the acts and behavior of his animal at all times; 
(3)  Providing security to residents from annoyance, intimidation, injury, and health hazards by animals; and 
(4)  Encouraging pet ownership. 
(Ord. No. 2010-03, 2-9-2010) 
Sec. 3-2. - Definitions. 
    For the purpose of this chapter the following words and phrases are hereby defined: 
    Animal. Any living creature which is commonly or actually domesticated. 
    Animal control officer. Any person or employee of the town designated by the town administrator to administer and enforce the provisions of this chapter. 
    Animal nuisance. Any nuisance arising out of the keeping, maintaining, or owning of, or failure to exercise sufficient control of an animal. 
    Animal shelter. An establishment operated by the town for the temporary care, confinement, and detention of animals that come into the custody of the animal control officer. 
    At large. An animal is off the premises of the owner and not on a leash or otherwise under the immediate control of a person physically capable of restraining the animal. 
    Cruelty. Any act or omission whereby unjustifiable physical pain, suffering, or death of an animal is caused or permitted, including failure to provide drink, air, shelter, or protection form the elements, a sanitary and safe living environment, veterinary care, or nutritious food in proper quantity. 
    Domesticated. Any animal kept, cared for, sheltered, fed or harbored or used as a pet, work or as a source of food, raw materials or in-kind. 
    Exotic animal. Any live monkey, alligator, crocodile, cayman, raccoon, skunk, fox, bear, sea mammal, poisonous snake, member of the feline species other than domestic cat, member of the canine species other than domestic dog and any other animal that would require a standard of care and control greater than that required for customary household pets. 
    Guard or attack dog. Any dog trained to attack on command or to protect persons or property and who will cease to attack upon command. 
    Impoundment. The taking into custody of any animal by the animal control officer or any other duly authorized representative of the town. 
    Kennel. The premises of any person or partnership or corporation engaged in the business of breeding, buying, selling, or boarding dogs and cats or other four-legged animals. Any person keeping more than eight such animals on his premises shall be conclusively presumed to be operating a kennel. 
    Owner. Any person, groups of persons or entity possessing, keeping, having charge of, sheltering, feeding, harboring or taking care of any animal covered by this chapter. 
    Private property. Property owned, rented, or leased by a resident or business. 
    Public nuisance. Any animal found at-large or making loud or objectionable sounds, chasing vehicles or pedestrians, or behaving in any manner which is deemed to be doing damage to property or to public health and well-being, or which is known to have bitten one or more persons, or which has been determined by the animal control officer to be a detriment to public health, welfare or safety, or that constitutes a physical threat to human beings or to other animals by virtue of its specific training or demonstrated behavior. 
    Restraint. When an animal is on the premises of its owner or keeper or when an animal is controlled by a leash or is under the control of an owner or a responsible person and obedient to that person's commands or when an animal is in a vehicle being driven. 
    Strict voice command. Demonstrable control or governance of the behavior or [of] any animal as if said animal were controlled by a leash. 
    Vicious animal. An animal that has bitten any person or which displays or shows a propensity to attack, bite, or harm human beings or other animals without provocation. Any dog or cat which has bitten any person at any time shall be deemed prima facie vicious upon proof thereof. 
(Ord. No. 2010-03, 2-9-2010) 
Sec. 3-3. - General powers and duties of animal control officer. 
    The animal control officer shall be charged with the following responsibilities: 
(1)  Seeing that all dogs and cats in town are adequately inoculated against rabies and have proof thereof. 
(2)  Will cooperate with the health officers of the various state governmental units and assist in the enforcement with regard to the control or [of] animals and especially with regard to the vaccination of animals against rabies. 
(3)  Investigates all complaints with regard to animals covered by this chapter. 
(4)  Enforces all local and state laws governing the care, control, and custody of animals covered by this chapter. 
(5)  Supervises and maintains the operation of the town-owned animal shelter. 
(Ord. No. 2010-03, 2-9-2010) 
Sec. 3-4. - Inspection and right of entry. 
    Whenever it is necessary to make an inspection to enforce any of the provisions of or perform any duty imposed by this chapter or other applicable law, or whenever the animal control officer has probable cause to believe that there exists in any building or upon any premises any violation of the provisions of this chapter or other applicable law, the animal control officer is hereby empowered to enter such property at any reasonable time and to inspect the same and to perform any duty imposed by this chapter or other applicable law, but only if the consent of the occupant or owner of the property is freely given or a search or inspection warrant is obtained as hereinafter provided. 
(1)  If such property is occupied, he shall first present proper credentials to the occupant and request entry, explaining his reasons therefore; 
(2)  If such property is unoccupied he shall first make a reasonable effort to locate the owner or other such persons having control or charge of the property, present proper credentials and request entry, explaining his reasons therefore; and 
(3)  If such entry is refused or cannot be obtained because the owner or other person having charge or control of the property cannot be found after due diligence, the animal control officer shall obtain a warrant to conduct a search for inspection of the property. 
(Ord. No. 2010-03, 2-9-2010) 
Sec. 3-5. - Animal control officer-Interference by others. 
    No person shall interfere with, hinder or molest the animal control officer in the performance of his duty to enforce this chapter; nor shall any person seek to release any animal in the custody of the animal control officer except as provide in this chapter. 
(Ord. No. 2010-03, 2-9-2010) 
Sec. 3-6. - Restraint and confinement. 
(a)  It shall be unlawful for the owner of any animal to fail to keep such animal under restraint or to permit such animal to run at-large within the town limits. 
(b)  Any animal, while on a street, sidewalk, public right-of-way or in any park, public square, or other public space, and upon any private property without the consent of the owner, shall be secured by a leash or chain, no longer than eight feet in length, of sufficient tensile strength to restrain the particular animal, or shall be at heel and securely muzzled. Pet owners may walk their animals without leashes only when such animal responds to strict voice control commands of the owner and only when accompanied by the owner. 
(c)  No owner or custodian of any animal shall fail to exercise proper care and control of such animal to prevent the same from becoming a public nuisance. 
(d)  Every female dog or cat in heat shall be confined in a building or other enclosure in such a manner that such dog or cat cannot come into contact with another animal except for planned breeding. 
(Ord. No. 2010-03, 2-9-2010) 
Sec. 3-7. - Concealment of pets. 
    No one shall hide, conceal, or aid or assist in hiding or concealing any pet owned, or harbored, when the pet is in violation of this chapter. 
(Ord. No. 2010-03, 2-9-2010) 
Sec. 3-8. - Keeping and displaying of animals. 
(a)  It shall be unlawful for any person in the town to exhibit, keep, or display pets, animals, birds of [or] fowl of any kind, in show windows for a period longer than six hours per day. 
(b)  It shall be unlawful for any person in the town to exhibit, keep, or display pets, animals, birds or fowl of any kind in a manner without shading to keep such animals from the sun and providing adequate food, water, and ventilation for their use. 
(Ord. No. 2010-03, 2-9-2010) 
Sec. 3-9. - Limitation on the number of animals. 
    No person shall keep, lodge, or maintain in the same household in excess of four four-legged animals more than one year of age in the town. Any animals in excess of this number may be impounded by the animal control officer. This section shall not apply to premises operated by a licensed veterinarian in the conduct of his profession or to licensed kennels or pet shops. 
(Ord. No. 2010-03, 2-9-2010) 
Sec. 3-10. - Animal care. 
(a)  No owner shall fail to provide such person's animals with sufficient, good and wholesome food and water, proper shelter and protection from the weather, veterinary care when needed to prevent suffering, and with humane care and treatment. 
(b)  No person shall beat, cruelly ill treat, tease, molest, bait, torment, bother, overload, overwork, or otherwise abuse an animal, or cause, instigate, or permit any dogfight or other combat between animals or between animals and humans. 
(c)  No owner of an animal shall abandon such animal. 
(d)  No person shall give away any live animal, reptile or bird as a prize for, or as an inducement to enter, any contest, game, or other competition, or as an inducement to enter a place of amusement. 
(e)  Any person operating a motor vehicle, who strikes a domestic animal shall stop at once and render such assistance as may be possible and shall immediately report such injury or death to the animal's owner. In the event the owner cannot be ascertained and located, such operator shall at once report the incident to the animal control officer or a police officer. 
(f)  No person shall expose any known poisonous substance, whether mixed with food or not, so that the same shall be liable to be eaten by any animal, provided that it shall not be unlawful for a person to expose on such person's own property common poisons against household rodents and vermin. 
(g)  It shall be unlawful to raise or keep chickens within the town limits unless the chickens are maintained as follows: 
(1)  An annual permit fee of $20.00 will be charged. 
(2)  No more than six chickens can be maintained. 
(3)  No roosters can be kept within the town limits. 
(4)  All chickens must be contained in a pen or coop constructed in a manner satisfactory to the codes enforcement officer. 
(5)  The pen or coop must be located in a backyard no closer than 25 feet of any property line. 
(6)  Persons wishing to maintain chickens must have written permission from their neighbor(s) whose property lines are within 100 feet of the chicken coop. 
(7)  Any person receiving two complaints regarding the care of chickens shall forfeit the right to raise chickens and the town will take legal steps to remove the chickens from the premises. 
(8)  All of the requirements mentioned in items [subsections] (1)-(6) must be met in order to receive approval to maintain chickens. 
(h)  It shall be unlawful to raise or keep horses, cattle, sheep, goats, swine, or any other farm animal or any kind of fowl, other than parrots, parakeets, mynah birds, and canaries, with[in] the town limits. 
(i)  It shall be unlawful to leave an animal in a closed vehicle or other enclosure for such duration or at such temperature that is potentially harmful to the animal. 
(Ord. No. 2010-03, 2-9-2010; Ord. No. 2011-10, 8-9-2011) 
Sec. 3-11. - Voluntary registration of animals. 
(a)  Pet owners are encouraged to register their pets with the town by providing a copy of the current rabies vaccination tag for each pet. 
(b)  This information will assist the animal control officer in the prompt identification of the owner of any pet that might be lost, impounded, or injured. 
(c)  There will be no fee charged for this registration. 
(Ord. No. 2010-03, 2-9-2010) 
Sec. 3-12. - Keeping of reptiles or dangerous wild animals. 
    No person shall keep or maintain within the town limits any poisonous reptiles or dangerous carnivorous wild animals without first having registered such animals or reptiles with the animal control officer. 
(Ord. No. 2010-03, 2-9-2010) 
Sec. 3-13. - Squirrels and songbirds protected. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to willfully kill or maim any squirrel or songbird or rob the nest of either. Provided, however, with the approval of the animal control officer and the police chief, any person shall be allowed to kill any squirrel that has become a nuisance upon the person's premises. 
(Ord. No. 2010-03, 2-9-2010) 
Sec. 3-14. - Dead animals. 
    No person shall place or leave the carcass of any dead animal or fowl in any street, alley, or lot or allow the same to remain on his lot. Any person whose animal dies may contact the animal control officer to arrange pickup of the carcass. 
(Ord. No. 2010-03, 2-9-2010) 
Sec. 3-15. - Transporting of animals. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person or persons to transport any animal in or upon the back of an open vehicle without proper restraints so as to keep the animal within the sides of such vehicle. 
(Ord. No. 2010-03, 2-9-2010) 
Sec. 3-16. - Vicious or dangerous animal. 
(a)  It shall be unlawful for any person to own, keep, have charge of, shelter, feed, and harbor or take care of any vicious or dangerous animal within the town limits except under the conditions set forth in this section. 
(b)  The police chief, animal control officer, or their designee, shall have the authority to determine if there is probable cause to establish whether or not a dog is vicious or dangerous animal and then must notify the owner of the dog in writing that the dog has been found to be vicious or dangerous.
