1.  Provide a minimum of two openings on different walls having a total net area of not less than one square inch for every square foot of enclosed area subject to flooding. 
2.  The bottom of each opening must be no more than one foot above the higher of the interior or exterior grade immediately under the opening, 
3.  Only the portions of openings that are below the base flood elevation (BFE) can be counted towards the required net open area. 
4.  Openings may be equipped with screens, louvers, valves, or other coverings or devices provided they permit the automatic flow of floodwaters in both directions. 
5.  Fill placed around foundation walls must be graded so that the grade inside the enclosed area is equal to or higher than the adjacent grade outside the building on at least one side of the building. 
b.  Hazardous velocities. Hydrodynamic pressure must be considered in the design of any foundation system where velocity waters or the potential for debris flow exists. If flood velocities are excessive (greater than five feet per second), foundation systems other than solid foundations walls should be considered so that obstructions to damaging flood flows are minimized. 
c.  Enclosures below lowest floor. 
1.  Access to the enclosed area shall be the minimum necessary to allow for parking of vehicles (garage door) or limited storage of maintenance equipment used in connection with the premises (standard exterior door) or entry to the living area (stairway or elevator). 
2.  The interior portion of such enclosed area shall not be finished or partitioned into separate rooms, must be void of utilities except for essential lighting as required for safety, and cannot be temperature controlled. 
3.  One wet location switch and/or outlet connected to a ground fault interrupt breaker may be installed below the required lowest floor elevation specified in the specific standards outlined in subsection 6-19(1)-(3). 
4.  All construction materials below the required lowest floor elevation specified in the specific standards outlined in subsection 6-19(1)-(4) should be of flood resistant materials. 
(5)  Floodways. Located within areas of special flood hazard established in section 6-4, are areas designated as floodways. The floodway is an extremely hazardous area due to the velocity of floodwaters that carry debris and potential projectiles and has erosion potential. The following provisions shall apply within such areas: 
a.  No encroachments, including fill, new construction, substantial improvements, additions, and other developments shall be permitted unless: 
1.  It has been demonstrated through hydrologic and hydraulic analyses performed in accordance with standard engineering practice that the proposed encroachment would not result in any increase in the flood levels during the occurrence of the base flood. Such certification and technical data shall be presented to the local administrator. 
2.  A conditional letter of map revision (CLOMR) has been approved by FEMA. A letter of map revision must be obtained upon completion of the proposed development. 
b.  If subsection 6-19(5)a. is satisfied, all new construction and substantial improvements shall comply with all applicable flood hazard reduction provisions of article IV. 
c.  No manufactured homes shall be permitted, except in an existing manufactured home park or subdivision. A replacement manufactured home may be placed on a lot in an existing manufactured home park or subdivision provided the anchoring and the elevation standards of subsection 6-19(3) and the encroachment standards of subsection 6-19(5)a. are met. 
d.  Permissible uses within floodways may include: general farming, pasture, outdoor plant nurseries, horticulture, forestry, wildlife sanctuary, game farm, and other similar agricultural, wildlife, and related uses. Also, lawns, gardens, play areas, picnic grounds, and hiking and horseback riding trails are acceptable uses, provided that they do not employ structures or fill. Substantial development of a permissible use may require a no-impact certification. The uses listed in this subsection are permissible only if and to the extent that they do not cause any increase in base flood elevations or changes to the floodway configuration. 
(6)  Recreational vehicles. 
a.  A recreational vehicle is ready for highway use if it is: 
1.  On wheels or jacking system; 
2.  Attached to the site only by quick-disconnect type utilities and security devices; and 
3.  Has no permanently attached additions. 
b.  Recreational vehicles placed on sites shall either be: 
1.  On site for fewer than 180 consecutive days; or 
2.  Be fully licensed and ready for highway use, or meet the development permit and certification requirements of section 6-15, general standards outlined in section 6-18, and manufactured homes standards in subsection 6-19(3) and (4). 
(7)  Map maintenance activities. The National Flood Insurance Program (NFIP) requires flood data to be reviewed and approved by FEMA. This ensures that flood maps, studies and other data identified in section 6-4 accurately represent flooding conditions so appropriate floodplain management criteria are based on current data. The following map maintenance activities are identified: 
a.  Requirement to submit new technical data. 
1.  For all development proposals that impact floodway delineations or base flood elevations, the community shall ensure that technical or scientific data reflecting such changes be submitted to FEMA as soon as practicable, but no later than six months of the date such information becomes available. These development proposals include; but not limited to: 
i.  Floodway encroachments that increase or decrease base flood elevations or alter floodway boundaries; 
ii.  Fill sites to be used for the placement of proposed structures where the applicant desires to remove the site from the special flood hazard area; 
iii.  Alteration of watercourses that result in a relocation or elimination of the special flood hazard area, including the placement of culverts; and 
iv.  Subdivision or large scale development proposals requiring the establishment of base flood elevations in accordance with subsection 6-19(12)d. 
2.  It is the responsibility of the applicant to have technical data, required in accordance with subsection 6-19(7), prepared in a format required for a conditional letter of map revision or letter of map revision, and submitted to FEMA. Submittal and processing fees for these map revisions shall also be the responsibility of the applicant. 
3.  The local administrator shall require a conditional letter of map revision prior to the issuance of a floodplain development permit for: 
i.  Proposed floodway encroachments that increase the base flood elevation; and 
ii.  Proposed development which increases the base flood elevation by more than one foot in areas where FEMA has provided base flood elevations but no floodway. 
4.  Floodplain development permits issued by the local administrator shall be conditioned upon the applicant obtaining a letter of map revision from FEMA for any development proposal subject to subsection 6-19(7). 
b.  Right to submit new technical data. The floodplain administrator may request changes to any of the information shown on an effective map that does not impact floodplain or floodway delineations or base flood elevations, such as labeling or planimetric details. Such a submission shall include appropriate supporting documentation made in writing by the local jurisdiction and may be submitted at any time. 
(8)  Accessory structures. 
a.  A detached accessory structure or garage, the cost of which is greater than $3,000.00, must comply with the requirements as outlined in FEMA's Technical Bulletin 7-93, Wet Floodproofing Requirements, or be elevated in accordance with subsection 6-19(1) and (4) or dry floodproofed in accordance with subsection 6-19(2). 
b.  If accessory structures of $3,000.00 or less are to be placed in the floodplain, the following criteria shall be met: 
1.  Accessory structures shall not be used for any uses other than the parking of vehicles and storage; 
2.  Accessory structures shall be designed to have low flood damage potential; 
3.  Accessory structures shall be constructed and placed on the building site so as to offer the minimum resistance to the flow of floodwaters; 
4.  Accessory structures shall be firmly anchored to prevent flotation, collapse or lateral movement of the structure; 
5.  Service facilities such as electrical and heating equipment shall be installed in accordance with subsection 6-18(5); 
6.  Openings to relieve hydrostatic pressure during a flood shall be provided below base flood elevation in conformance with subsection 6-19(4)a.; and 
7.  Accessory structures shall be built with flood resistance materials in accordance with Technical Bulletin 2, Flood Damage-Resistant Materials Requirements, dated 8/08, and available from the Federal Emergency Management Agency. Class 4 and 5 materials, referenced therein, are acceptable flood-resistant materials. 
(9)  Swimming pool utility equipment rooms. If the building cannot be built at or above the BFE, because of functionality of the equipment then a structure to house the utilities for the pool may be built below the BFE with the following provisions: 
a.  Meet the requirements for accessory structures in subsection 6-19(8). 
b.  The utilities must be anchored to prevent flotation and shall be designed to prevent water from entering or accumulating within the components during conditions of the base flood. 
(10)  Elevators. 
a.  Install a float switch system or another system that provides the same level of safety necessary for all elevators where there is a potential for the elevator cab to descend below the BFE during a flood per FEMA's Technical Bulletin 4-93, Elevator Installation for Buildings Located in Special Flood Hazard Areas. 
b.  All equipment that may have to be installed below the BFE such as counter weight roller guides, compensation cable and pulleys, and oil buffers for traction elevators and the jack assembly for a hydraulic elevator must be constructed using flood-resistant materials where possible per FEMA's Technical Bulletin 4-93, Elevator Installation for Buildings Located in Special Flood Hazard Areas. 
(11)  Fill. An applicant shall demonstrate that fill is the only alternative to raising the building to meet the residential and non-residential construction requirements of subsection 6-19(1) or (2), and that the amount of fill used will not affect the flood storage capacity or adversely affect adjacent properties. The following provisions shall apply to all fill placed in the special flood hazard area: 
a.  Fill may not be placed in the floodway unless it is in accordance with the requirements in subsection 6-19(5)a. 
b.  Fill may not be placed in tidal or non-tidal wetlands without the required state and federal permits. 
c.  Fill must consist of soil and rock materials only. A registered professional geotechnical engineer may use dredged material as fill only upon certification of suitability. Landfills, rubble fills, dumps, and sanitary fills are not permitted in the floodplain. 
d.  Fill used to support structures must comply with ASTM Standard D-698, and its suitability to support structures certified by a registered, professional engineer. 
e.  Fill slopes shall be no greater than two horizontal to one vertical. Flatter slopes may be required where velocities may result in erosion. 
f.  The use of fill shall not increase flooding or cause drainage problems on neighboring properties. 
g.  Fill may not be used for structural support in the coastal high hazard areas. 
h.  Will meet the requirements of FEMA Technical Bulletin 10-01, Ensuring That Structures Built on Fill In or Near Special Flood Hazard Areas are Reasonably Safe From Flooding. 
(12)  Standards for subdivision proposals and other development. 
a.  All subdivision proposals and other proposed new development shall be consistent with the need to minimize flood damage and are subject to all applicable standards in these regulations. 
b.  All subdivision proposals and other proposed new development shall have public utilities and facilities such as sewer, gas, electrical, and water systems located and constructed to minimize flood damage. 
c.  All subdivision proposals and other proposed new development shall have adequate drainage provided to reduce exposure to flood damage. 
d.  The applicant shall meet the requirement to submit technical data to FEMA in subsection 6-19(7) when a hydrologic and hydraulic analysis is completed that generates base flood elevations. 
(Ord. No. 2011-13, 8-9-2011) 
Sec. 6-20. - Standards for streams without established base flood elevations and floodways. 
    Located within the areas of special flood hazard (zones A and V) established in section 6-4, are small streams where no base flood data has been provided or where no floodways have been identified. The following provisions apply within such areas: 
(1)  In all areas of special flood hazard where base flood elevation data are not available, the applicant shall provide a hydrologic and hydraulic engineering analysis that generates base flood elevations for all subdivision proposals and other proposed developments containing at least 50 lots or five acres, whichever is less. 
(2)  No encroachments, including fill, new construction, substantial improvements and new development shall be permitted within 100 feet of the stream bank unless certification with supporting technical data by a registered professional engineer is provided demonstrating that such encroachments shall not result in any increase in flood levels during the occurrence of the base flood discharge. 
(3)  If subsection 6-20(1) is satisfied and base flood elevation data is available from other sources, all new construction and substantial improvements within such areas shall comply with all applicable flood hazard ordinance provisions of article IV and shall be elevated or floodproofed in accordance with elevations established in accordance with subsection 6-16(11). 
(4)  Data from preliminary, draft, and final flood insurance studies constitutes best available data. Refer to FEMA Floodplain Management Technical Bulletin 1-98, Use of Flood Insurance Study (FIS) Data as Available Data. If an appeal is pending on the study in accordance with 44 CFR Ch. 1, Part 67.5 and 67.6, the data does not have to be used. 
(5)  When base flood elevation (BFE) data is not available from a federal, state, or other source one of the following methods may be used to determine a BFE. For further information regarding the methods for determining BFEs listed below, refer to FEMA's manual Managing Floodplain Development in Approximate Zone A Areas. 
a.  Contour interpolation. 
1.  Superimpose approximate zone A boundaries onto a topographic map and estimate a BFE. 
2.  Add one-half of the contour interval of the topographic map that is used to the BFE. 
b.  Data extrapolation. A BFE can be determined if a site within 500 feet upstream of a reach of a stream reach for which a 100-year profile has been computed by detailed methods, and the floodplain and channel bottom slope characteristics are relatively similar to the downstream reaches. No hydraulic structures shall be present. 
c.  Hydrologic and hydraulic calculations. Perform hydrologic and hydraulic calculations to determine BFEs using FEMA approved methods and software. 
(Ord. No. 2011-13, 8-9-2011) 
Sec. 6-21. - Standards for streams with established base flood elevations but without floodways. 
    Along rivers and streams where base flood elevation (BFE) data is provided but no floodway is identified for a special flood hazard area on the FIRM or in the FIS. 
(1)  No encroachments including fill, new construction, substantial improvements, or other development shall be permitted unless certification with supporting technical data by a registered professional engineer is provided demonstrating that the cumulative effect of the proposed development, when combined with all other existing and anticipated development, will not increase the water surface elevation of the base flood more than one foot at any point within the community. 
(Ord. No. 2011-13, 8-9-2011) 
Sec. 6-22. - Standards for areas of shallow flooding (AO zones). 
    Located within the areas of special flood hazard established in section 6-4, are areas designated as shallow flooding. The following provisions shall apply within such areas: 
(1)  All new construction and substantial improvements of residential structures shall have the lowest floor elevated to at least as high as the depth number specified on the flood insurance rate map, in feet, above the highest adjacent grade. If no depth number is specified, the lowest floor shall be elevated at least three feet above the highest adjacent grade. 
(2)  All new construction and substantial improvements of non-residential structures shall: 
a.  Have the lowest floor elevated to at least as high as the depth number specified on the flood insurance rate map, in feet, above the highest adjacent grade. If no depth number is specified, the lowest floor shall be elevated at least three feet above the highest adjacent grade; or, 
b.  Be completely floodproofed together with attendant utility and sanitary facilities to or above that level so that any space below that level is watertight with walls substantially impermeable to the passage of water and with structural components having the capability of resisting hydrostatic and hydrodynamic loads and effects of buoyancy. Certification is required as stated in section 6-15. 
(3)  All structures on slopes must have drainage paths around them to guide water away from the structures. 
(Ord. No. 2011-13, 8-9-2011) 
ARTICLE V. - VARIANCE PROCEDURES 

Sec. 6-23. - Establishment of appeal board. 
    The Cheraw Zoning and Appeals Commission as established by the Cheraw Town Council, shall hear and decide requests for variances from the requirements of this chapter. 
(Ord. No. 2011-13, 8-9-2011) 
Sec. 6-24. - Right to appeal. 
    Any person aggrieved by the decision of the appeal board or any taxpayer may appeal such decision to the court. 
(Ord. No. 2011-13, 8-9-2011) 
Sec. 6-25. - Historic structures. 
    Variances may be issued for the repair of rehabilitation of historic structures upon the determination that the proposed repair or rehabilitation will not preclude the structure's continued designation as a historic structure and the variance is the minimum necessary to preserve the historic character and design of the structure. 
(Ord. No. 2011-13, 8-9-2011) 
Sec. 6-26. - Functionally dependent uses. 
    Variances may be issued for development necessary for the conduct of a functionally dependent use, provided the criteria of this article are met, no reasonable alternative exist, and the development is protected by methods that minimize flood damage and create no additional threat to public safety. 
(Ord. No. 2011-13, 8-9-2011) 
Sec. 6-27. - Agricultural structures. 
    Variances may be issued to wet floodproof an agricultural structure provided it is used solely for agricultural purposes. In order to minimize flood damages during the base flood and the threat to public health and safety, the structure must meet all of the conditions and considerations of section 6-30, this section, and the following standards: 
(1)  Use of the structure must be limited to agricultural purposes as listed below: 
a.  Pole frame buildings with open or closed sides used exclusively for the storage of farm machinery and equipment; 
b.  Steel grain bins and steel frame corncribs; 
c.  General-purpose barns for the temporary feeding of livestock that are open on at least one side; 
d.  For livestock confinement buildings, poultry houses, dairy operations, and similar livestock operations, variances may not be issued for structures that were substantially damaged. New construction or substantial improvement of such structures must meet the elevation requirements of subsection 6-19(2) of this chapter; and 
(2)  The agricultural structure must be built or rebuilt, in the case of an existing building that is substantially damaged, with flood-resistant materials for the exterior and interior building components and elements below the base flood elevation. 
(3)  The agricultural structure must be adequately anchored to prevent flotation, collapse, or lateral movement. All of the structure's components must be capable of resisting specific flood-related forces including hydrostatic, buoyancy, hydrodynamic, and debris impact forces. Where flood velocities exceed five feet per second, fast-flowing floodwaters can exert considerable pressure on the building's enclosure walls or foundation walls. 
(4)  The agricultural structure must meet the venting requirement of subsection 6-19(4) of this chapter. 
(5)  Any mechanical, electrical, or other utility equipment must be located above the base flood elevation (BFE) so that they are contained within a watertight, floodproofed enclosure that is capable of resisting damage during flood conditions in accordance with subsection 6-18(5) of this chapter. 
(6)  The agricultural structure must comply with the floodway encroachment provisions of subsection 6-19(5) of this chapter. 
(7)  Major equipment, machinery, or other contents must be protected. Such protection may include protective watertight floodproofed areas within the building, the use of equipment hoists for readily elevating contents, permanently elevating contents on pedestals or shelves above the base flood elevation, or determining that property owners can safely remove contents without risk to lives and that the contents will be located to a specified site out of the floodplain. 
(Ord. No. 2011-13, 8-9-2011) 
Sec. 6-28. - Considerations. 
    In passing upon such applications, the appeal board shall consider all technical evaluations, all relevant factors, all standards specified in other sections of this chapter, and: 
(1)  The danger that materials may be swept onto other lands to the injury of others; 
(2)  The danger to life and property due to flooding or erosion damage, and the safety of access to the property in times of flood for ordinary and emergency vehicles; 
(3)  The susceptibility of the proposed facility and its contents to flood damage and the effect of such damage on the individual owner; 
(4)  The importance of the services provided by the proposed facility to the community; 
(5)  The necessity to the facility of a waterfront location, where applicable; 
(6)  The availability of alternative locations, not subject to flooding or erosion damage, for the proposed use; 
(7)  The compatibility of the proposed use with existing and anticipated development, and the relationship of the proposed use to the comprehensive plan and floodplain management program for that area; 
(8)  The expected heights, velocity, duration, rate of rise, and sediment transport of the floodwaters and the effects of wave action, if applicable, expected at the site; 
(9)  The costs of providing governmental services during and after flood conditions including maintenance and repair of public utilities and facilities such as sewer, gas, electrical and water systems, and streets and bridges; and 
(10)  Agricultural structures must be located in wide, expansive floodplain areas, where no other alternative location for the agricultural structure exists. The applicant must demonstrate that the entire farm acreage, consisting of a contiguous parcel of land on which the structure is to be located, must be in the special flood hazard area and no other alternative locations for the structure are available. 
(Ord. No. 2011-13, 8-9-2011) 
Sec. 6-29. - Findings. 
    Findings listed above shall be submitted to the appeal board, in writing, and included in the application for a variance. Additionally, comments from the Department of Natural Resources, Land, Water and Conservation Division, State Coordinator's Office, must be taken into account and included in the permit file. 
(Ord. No. 2011-13, 8-9-2011) 
Sec. 6-30. - Floodways. 
    Variances shall not be issued within any designated floodway if any increase in flood levels during the base flood discharge would result unless a CLOMR is obtained prior to issuance of the variance. In order to ensure the project is built in compliance with the CLOMR for which the variance is granted the applicant must provide a bond for 100 percent of the cost to perform the development. 
(Ord. No. 2011-13, 8-9-2011) 
Sec. 6-31. - Conditions. 
    Upon consideration of the factors listed above and the purposes of this chapter, the appeal board may attach such conditions to the granting of variances as it deems necessary to further the purposes of this chapter. The following conditions shall apply to all variances: 
(1)  Variances may not be issued when the variance will make the structure in violation of other federal, state, or local laws, regulations, or ordinances. 
(2)  Variances shall only be issued upon a determination that the variance is the minimum necessary, considering the flood hazard, to afford relief. 
(3)  Variances shall only be issued upon a showing of good and sufficient cause, a determination that failure to grant the variance would result in exceptional hardship, and a determination that the granting of a variance will not result in increased flood heights, additional threats to public safety, extraordinary public expense, create nuisance, cause fraud on or victimization of the public, or conflict with existing local laws or ordinances. 
(4)  Any applicant to whom a variance is granted shall be given written notice specifying the difference between the base flood elevation (BFE) and the elevation to which the structure is to be built and a written statement that the cost of flood insurance will be commensurate with the increased risk. Such notification shall be maintained with a record of all variance actions. 
(5)  The local administrator shall maintain the records of all appeal actions and report any variances to the Federal Emergency Management Agency (FEMA) upon request. 
(6)  Variances shall not be issued for unpermitted development or other development that is not in compliance with the provisions of this chapter. Violations must be corrected in accordance with subsection 6-17(e) of this chapter. 
(Ord. No. 2011-13, 8-9-2011) 
ARTICLE VI. - LEGAL STATUS PROVISIONS 

Sec. 6-32. - Effect on rights and liabilities under the existing flood damage prevention ordinance. 
    This chapter in part comes forward by re-enactment of some of the provisions of the flood damage prevention ordinance enacted September 13, 2011, and it is not the intention to repeal but rather to re-enact and continue to enforce without interruption of such existing provisions, so that all rights and liabilities that have accrued there under are reserved and may be enforced. The enactment of this chapter shall not affect any action, suit or proceeding instituted or pending. All provisions of the flood damage prevention ordinance of the Town of Cheraw enacted on August 1, 1975, as amended, which are not reenacted herein, are repealed. 
(Ord. No. 2011-13, 8-9-2011) 
Sec. 6-33. - Effect upon outstanding building permits. 
    Nothing herein contained shall require any change in the plans, construction, size or designated use of any building, structure or part thereof for which a building permit has been granted by the chief building inspector or his authorized agents before the time of passage of this ordinance; provided, however, that when start of construction has not occurred under such outstanding permit within a period of 60 days subsequent to passage of this ordinance, construction or use shall be in conformity with the provisions of this chapter. 
(Ord. No. 2011-13, 8-9-2011) 
Sec. 6-34. - Effective date. 
    This chapter shall become effective upon adoption. 
(Ord. No. 2011-13, 8-9-2011) 
Chapter 7 - GARBAGE, REFUSE, YARD DEBRIS AND RECYCLING[1] 

Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
Editor's note- Ord. No. 2009-07, adopted April 14, 2009, repealed the former Ch. 7, §§ 7-1-7-5, and enacted a new Ch. 7 as set out herein. The former Ch. 7 pertained to similar subject matter. See also the Code Comparative Table. Ord. No. 2015-01, adopted July 8, 2014, changed the title of chapter 7 from "Garbage and refuse" to read as set out herein. 

Sec. 7-1. - Definitions. 
    The following terms, phrases, words, and their derivatives all have the meaning given herein: 
    Ashes. That refuse from fires which has been wetted and cooled to the touch prior to collection. 
    Bulk container. A metal container, not to exceed eight cubic yards, to be used for the deposit of regular garbage and trash. Containers shall be covered at all times. 
    Central business district. Section of the town set aside predominately for commercial establishments. 
    Commercial establishment. Any retail, wholesale, institutional, religious, hotel, governmental, or other non-residential establishment at which garbage and trash may be generated. 
    Commercial waste. Garbage, rubbish, ashes, and other refuse, resulting from institutions and commercial concerns. 
    Construction and demolition waste (C&D waste). Waste resulting solely from construction, remodeling, repair, or demolition operations on buildings or other structures, but not inert debris, land-clearing debris, yard debris, or used asphalt, asphalt mixed with dirt, sand, gravel, rock, concrete, or similar non-hazardous material. 
    Garbage. The by-product of animal or vegetable foodstuffs, resulting from the handling, preparation, cooking, and consumption of food or other matter, which is subject to decomposition, decay, putrefaction, or the generation of noxious or offensive gases or odors, or which during or after decay, may serve as breeding or feeding material for flies, insects, or animals. 
    Hazardous refuse. Any chemical, compound, mixture, substance or article which is designated by the U.S. Environmental Protection Agency or appropriate agency of the federal or state government to be hazardous, toxic, radioactive, volatile, corrosive, flammable, explosive, biomedical, infections and/or bio-hazardous as those terms are defined by or pursuant to federal or state law or regulations. 
    Household trash. Waste accumulation of paper, sweepings, dust, rags, bottles, cans or other matter of any kind, other than garbage, which is usually attendant to housekeeping. 
    Industrial waste. Solid waste resulting from an industrial process or manufacturing operation. 
    Litter. Garbage, refuse, waste materials or any other discarded, used, or unconsumed substance which is not handled as specified herein. 
    Medical waste. Any solid waste which is generated in the diagnosis, treatment, or immunization of human beings or animals, in research pertaining thereto, or in the production or testing of biological, but does not include any hazardous, waste or those substances excluded from the definition of solid waste. 
    Mobile container. A wheeled garbage receptacle compatible with town or contracted garbage collection equipment. 
    Multiple-family dwelling. Any dwelling place occupied by more than one family. 
    Person. Any individual, firm, company, corporation, or association. 
    Recyclables. Newspapers and their inserts, aluminum beer and soft drink cans, HPDE plastic milk and water jugs, steel containers used for food and drinks, aluminum foil, bi-metal or tin cans used for food or drinks, PET plastic soft drink bottles, aluminum pie plates; clear, amber, blue, and green glass used for food and beverages; telephone directories, mixed paper goods, white office paper, magazines, "OCC"-old corrugated cardboard, yard waste, white goods, lead acid batteries, and used motor oil for cars and trucks. 
    Refuse. A collective term which encompasses all of the solid wastes for the community. 
    Single-family dwelling. Any dwelling place occupied by one family. 
    Solid waste. All solid and semi-solid garbage, refuse, and rubbish/trash, but never: (a) hazardous waste or special waste; (b) solid or dissolved materials in domestic sewage; (c) solid or dissolved materials in irrigation return flows; (d) industrial discharges which are point sources subject to permits under Section 402 of the Federal Water Pollution Control Act as amended (86 STAT.880); or (e) source, special nuclear, or by-product material as defined by the Atomic Energy Act of 1954 as amended (68 STAT.923). 
    Special waste. All waste collected in bulk container from industry and also that refuse resulting from either a commercial, industrial, or manufacturing operation which requires special handling, such as sawdust, steel springs, or other materials which would otherwise damage the garbage collection equipment. 
    Town. The Town of Cheraw. 
    White goods. Refrigerators, stoves and ranges, water heaters, freezers, swing sets, bicycles (without tires), scrap metal, copper, and other similar domestic and commercial large appliances. 
    Yard waste. Any and all vegetative matter resulting from landscaping or yard maintenance. 
(Ord. No. 2009-07, 4-14-2009) 
Sec. 7-2. - Responsibility for refuse removal. 
    Responsibility for administration of residential, commercial, and industrial refuse removal shall lie with the town's sanitation department either directly or through a contractual arrangement with a private company. 
(Ord. No. 2009-07, 4-14-2009) 
Sec. 7-3. - User collection fee. 
    A user fee for the collection of garbage and trash shall be added to each municipal customer's water bill at a rate of $14.00 per month. 
(Ord. No. 2009-07, 4-14-2009) 
Sec. 7-4. - Refuse containers. 
    All mobile garbage containers shall be of sufficient size and of material quality subject to the approval of the sanitation supervisor. 
(1)  The town will furnish, initially at no cost, one mobile garbage container to each single-family dwelling, and to certain multi-family dwellings, and commercial establishments. If an additional container is required it will be furnished by the town, or its contractor, and the resident shall be responsible for paying an additional monthly fee of $14.00 for collection and disposal services. The town shall have the option of furnishing or requiring that a single bulk container be furnished at a central location to serve more than one commercial establishment in lieu of a mobile container. This option will be exercised where economics and location dictate. 
(2)  Any apartment building or complex of more than four single units shall be serviced utilizing a bulk container at the expense of the building or apartment owner or tenant. 
(3)  Industrial and/or manufacturing operations within the town limits may be served at their own expense utilizing appropriate bulk containers serviced by the town or contract agency. 
(4)  Any household, commercial establishment, or industry requiring handling of special wastes may be subject to a monthly surcharge billing established by the town council. 
(Ord. No. 2009-07, 4-14-2009) 
Sec. 7-5. - Replacement of mobile containers. 
(a)  It shall be the responsibility of each household and/or commercial establishment to handle the maintenance and cleanliness of mobile containers to the degree of which they are capable. Containers furnished free by the town shall remain the property of the town and are provided and assigned to residences for the health, safety, convenience, and general welfare of the occupants. 
(b)  Containers which are damaged, destroyed, or stolen through abuse, neglect, or improper use of the occupants/users shall be replaced by the town at the expense of the occupant or the owner of the residence. 
(c)  Containers that are damaged through no fault of the occupant or user shall be replaced by the town at no cost to the occupant or owner of the property. 
(Ord. No. 2009-07, 4-14-2009) 
Sec. 7-6. - Responsibility to place garbage for collection. 
(a)  It shall be the responsibility of each landlord, tenant, or owner to place their refuse for collection at the proper time and in the proper manner for collection. No employee of the town shall assist any individual in the performance of their duty, except those residences approved for backdoor service. 
(b)  All refuse for single- or multi-family residences shall be placed at the curb for collection no sooner than 7:00 p.m. the day before collection and no later than 6:00 a.m. the day of collection. 
(c)  All refuse shall be containerized. 
(d)  All mobile containers shall be removed from the curb no later than 7:00 p.m. the day of collection. 
(Ord. No. 2009-07, 4-14-2009) 
Sec. 7-7. - Excess solid waste. 
    It is recognized that at certain times excess solid waste will be generated by the occupant/user above the containerized capability of the mobile container. This excess shall be bagged or boxed in a throw-away container and placed neatly beside the mobile container. The occupant/user may be required to purchase a second container at the discretion of the sanitation supervisor. 
(Ord. No. 2009-07, 4-14-2009) 
Sec. 7-8. - Policing or cleanup of bulk container storage area. 
    It shall be the responsibility of the occupant/user to keep all bulk container storage and curbside pickup points free of litter. Containers shall not be filled to overflow capacity in order to prevent the possibility of litter distribution when emptying the container. 
(Ord. No. 2009-07, 4-14-2009) 
Sec. 7-9. - Building materials. 
    No person, firm, or corporation shall use mobile and/or bulk containers as a depository for brick, blocks, rocks, hot ashes, acids, or any item destructive to the container from a weight or corrosive standpoint along with residue from residential and/or commercial construction. Every contractor, builder, carpenter, or the property owner, after completing or during the construction or alteration of a structure, must remove all trash incident to such construction or alteration at his own expense. 
(Ord. No. 2009-07, 4-14-2009) 
Sec. 7-10. - Littering of solid waste. 
    No person or persons shall deposit or cause to be deposited any form of solid waste on any property, public or private. Such material shall be prepared and placed for collection as specified in this chapter. 
(Ord. No. 2009-07, 4-14-2009) 
Sec. 7-11. - Interfering with collection practices. 
    No person shall interfere or otherwise deter the normal refuse collection process by tampering with refuse containers or their contents. 
(Ord. No. 2009-07, 4-14-2009) 
Sec. 7-12. - Availability and extent of service. 
(a)  Mobile containers shall be serviced once a week. 
(b)  Any person, firm, or corporation shall be entitled to service on more than one mobile container per pickup but will be charged a separate fee for each container. 
(c)  Households where no one is physically able to roll the cart to the street for collection will be extended backdoor service on a once a week basis. Applications for backdoor service must be made to the town clerk's office. 
(d)  All persons, firms, or corporations who generate more solid waste than can be serviced by two 96-gallon containers weekly, shall be required to furnish a bulk container, size to be determined by volume, of the type approved by the sanitation director, provided that such container can be installed and serviced. (This section does not apply to industrial waste pickup.) 
(e)  All persons, except industry, requiring service on more than one bulk container shall be charged a monthly service charge established by the town council and/or the garbage contracting authority. 
(Ord. No. 2009-07, 4-14-2009) 
Sec. 7-13. - Unlawful dumping. 
    No garbage, rubbish, trash or other refuse shall be dumped or placed for collection except garbage, rubbish, trash, or other refuse from premises within the town limits. No person residing outside the town limits shall utilize any of the mobile trash containers or the bulk containers provide by the town for commercial, industrial, or residential trash and garbage collection. No person shall move refuse from one location to another with the intent to evade the provisions of this section. 
(Ord. No. 2009-07, 4-14-2009) 
Sec. 7-14. - Removal of small dead animals. 
    Small dead animals shall be picked up at the curb on a call basis and shall not be placed in or adjacent to mobile trash containers. 
(Ord. No. 2009-07, 4-14-2009) 
Sec. 7-15. - Yard debris, refuse, and recycling collection policies. 
Yard Debris, Refuse, and Recycling Collection Policies 
Yard Debris Policy: 
    Yard debris is considered to be leaves, grass clippings, limbs, shrubs, and trees cut into sections not to exceed six inches in diameter and four feet in length. 
    Yard debris removal is a residential service. If a commercial business does yard work at your home, they are responsible for hauling away any yard waste generated with the exception of leaves or grass clippings. 
    All commercial businesses hired to cut trees will be responsible for the removal of such material. Property owners who cut down their own trees themselves may cut up the trees into sections less than four feet in length and six inches in diameter and put at the curb and they will be picked up. 
    For commercial or business properties the town will only pick up grass clippings and leaves. All other debris will be the responsibility of the business or commercial property owner to dispose of. 
    For debris generated on vacant lots the town will pick up one six cubic yard load of debris and the property owner will be responsible for the remainder of any other debris generated. Tree material will need to be cut into sections less than four feet and six inches in diameter. Anything larger will not be picked up. 
    Yard debris should be placed curbside away from regular trash for pick-up. Please keep leaves separate from other yard debris. Please do not place debris in ditches or in the street as this will clog up storm drains which can lead to flooding and mosquito problems. The town does not pick up dirt or rocks. 
    Christmas trees are collected curbside from December 26th to January 11th. Remove all decorations, including nails from the stand and place at the curb for pick-up. 
    Property owners found to be in violation of this policy can be fined and commercial businesses in violation of the policy can be fined or have their business license revoked. 
  Exceptions for yard debris pickup will be made in cases where storms cause excessive damage. 
Refuse Policy: 
    Regarding construction materials the town will pick up one six cubic yard load of any construction materials that a property owner does himself. Anything over six cubic yards the property owner will be responsible for disposing of. All contractors, builders, or carpenters hired by a property owner shall be responsible for removing any construction debris generated from construction or alteration of a structure at their own expense. 
    White goods (washers, dryers, stoves, refrigerators, hot water heaters) and furniture can be picked up but residents need to call and schedule a pick up from the town's public works department at 537-8430. For safety of children please remove all doors before placing items at the curb. 
    The town will not collect poisons, acid, caustic, infectious materials, explosives, chemical liquids and/or powders, household garbage, clothes, cloth material, sheet plastic, full or partially full paint containers. These items are to be taken to a county operated convenience center. Locations are on Tec Road and the Old Burns site near Society Hill. 
    Property owners found in violation of the refuse policy can be fined and contractors, builders, or carpenters found in violation of this policy can be fined or have their business license revoked. 
Recycling Program: 
    Items such as aluminum, steel and tin cans, #1 plastics (usually soft drink bottles), #2 plastics (milk jugs and detergent bottles), mixed paper (such as magazines, catalogs, telephone books, office paper, junk mail, cereal boxes, etc.) are considered recyclables and residents can participate in the town's curbside recycling program for a monthly fee. Please contact the Cheraw Town Hall at 537-8400 to sign up for this program. 
    For more information regarding any of these services please contact the town's public works department at 537-8430. 
(Ord. No. 2015-01, 7-8-2014) 
Sec. 7-16. - Administration and enforcement. 
    The administration and enforcement of the provisions of this chapter shall be the responsibility of the town's public works director and the town administrator. 
(Ord. No. 2009-07, 4-14-2009; Ord. No. 2015-01, 7-8-2014) 
Editor's note- Ord. No. 2015-01, adopted July 8, 2014, renumbered former § 7-15 as § 7-16 to read as set out herein. 
Sec. 7-17. - Penalties. 
    Anyone charged in violation of any section or provision of this chapter shall, upon conviction, be fined not more than $500.00 or imprisoned (imprisonment) not to exceed 30 days, or both. Each day's violation or (of) any provisions of this chapter shall constitute a separate offense. Commercial businesses in violation may also face revocation of business license. 
(Ord. No. 2009-07, 4-14-2009; Ord. No. 2015-01, 7-8-2014) 
Editor's note- Ord. No. 2015-01, adopted July 8, 2014, renumbered former § 7-16 as § 7-17 to read as set out herein. 
Chapter 8 - HOUSING CODE 

Sec. 8-1. - Legislative findings. 
(a)  The town finds that there exist in the town certain dwellings which are unfit for human habitation due to: 
(1)  Dilapidation; 
(2)  Defects increasing the hazards of fire, accident, or other calamities; 
(3)  Lack of ventilation, light, or sanitary facilities; or 
(4)  Other conditions rendering the dwellings unsafe or unsanitary, dangerous or detrimental to the health, safety, or morals or otherwise adverse to the welfare of the residents of the town. 
(b)  The town deems it necessary to exercise its police powers to repair, close, or demolish any dwelling in the manner herein provided, pursuant to the provisions of S.C. Code § 31-15-10 et seq., as the same may be from time to time amended. 
Sec. 8-2. - Reserved. 
    Adoption of International Building Code. See section 4-1. 
Sec. 8-3. - Definitions. 
    For the purpose of this chapter, the following definitions shall apply unless the context clearly indicates or requires a different meaning: 
    Board of adjustments and appeals. A board appointed by the mayor, with the approval of a majority of the council, which shall have the powers described in this chapter, in addition to any other powers granted to the board by this Code and any other ordinance or act of the town. 
    Dwellings. Any building, structure or part thereof, used and occupied for human habitation or intended to be so used, including any outhouses and appurtenances belonging thereto or usually enjoyed therewith. 
    Housing enforcement officer. An individual appointed by the town administrator who shall have powers described in this chapter, in addition to any other powers granted to the officer by this Code or any other ordinance or act of the town. 
    Owner. The holder in fee simple and every mortgagee of record. 
    Parties in interest. All persons who have interests of record in a dwelling and any who are in possession thereof. 
Sec. 8-4. - Petitions, complaint and hearing. 
(a)  Whenever a petition is filed with the housing enforcement officer by any official of the town or any department head having duties relating to health, fire, or building regulations or to any other activities concerning dwellings in the town, or by at least five residents of the town, charging that any dwelling is unfit for human habitation, or whenever it appears to the enforcement officer, or on his motion, that any dwelling is unfit for human habitation, he shall, if his preliminary investigation discloses a basis for the charges, issue, and cause to be served a complaint upon the owner of and all parties of interest in the dwelling. 
(b)  The complaint shall state the charges in that respect and contain a notice that a hearing will be held before the enforcement officer or his designated agent, at a place therein fixed as soon as practical following the serving of the complaint. The owner and parties of interest shall be given the right to file an answer to the complaint and to appear in person or to otherwise give testimony at the place and time fixed in the complaint. 
(c)  The rules of evidence prevailing in courts of law or equity shall not be controlling in hearings before the enforcement officer. 
(Ord. No. 2006-06, 4-11-2006) 
Sec. 8-5. - Orders determining fitness. 
(a)  If, after notice and hearing as provided above, the housing enforcement officer determines that the dwelling under consideration is unfit for human habitation, he shall state, in writing, his findings of fact in support of the determination and shall issue and cause to be served upon the owner thereof an order, providing as follows: 
(1)  If the repair, alteration, or improvement of the dwelling can be made at a reasonable cost in relation to the value of the dwelling, which reasonable cost is hereby determined as 50 percent or less of the value of the dwelling, requiring the owner, within the time specified in the order, to repair, alter, or improve the dwelling to render it fit for human habitation or to vacate and close the dwelling as a human habitation; or 
(2)  If the repair, alteration, or improvement of the dwelling cannot be made at a reasonable cost in relation to the value of the dwelling, requiring the owner, within the time specified in the order, to remove or demolish the dwelling. 
(b)  (1)  If the owner fails to comply with an order to repair, alter, or improve or to vacate and close a dwelling, the housing enforcement officer may cause the dwelling to be repaired, altered, or improved or to be vacated or closed. The enforcement officer may cause to be posted on the main entrance of any dwelling so closed a placard with the following words: "This Building is Unfit for Human Habitation. The Usage or Occupation of this Building for Human Habitation is Prohibited and Unlawful." 
(2)  If the owner fails to comply with an order to remove or demolish the dwelling, the enforcement officer may cause the dwelling to be removed or demolished. 
(3)  The amount of the cost of the repairs, alterations, or improvements, vacating, and closing or removal or demolition by the housing enforcement officer, together with an administrative assessment of $150.00, shall be a lien against the real property upon which such cost was incurred and shall be collectable in the same manner as are municipal taxes. Provided, however, that nothing herein shall be construed as limiting any other right or remedy the town may have to collect such costs. 
Sec. 8-6. - Standards; conditions. 
(a)  The housing enforcement officer may determine that a dwelling is unfit for human habitation if he finds that conditions exist in the dwelling which are dangerous or injurious to the health, safety, or morals of the occupants of the dwelling, the occupants of neighboring dwellings, or other residents of the town. 
(b)  Conditions may include, but shall not be limited to the following: 
(1)  Defects therein increasing the hazards of fire, accident, or other calamities; 
(2)  Lack of adequate ventilation, light, or sanitary facilities; 
(3)  Dilapidation, disrepair, structural defects or uncleanliness; or 
(4)  Other conditions rendering such dwellings unsafe or unsanitary, dangerous, or detrimental to the health, safety, or morals or otherwise adverse to the residents of the town. 
Sec. 8-7. - Service of complaints and orders. 
    Complaints or orders issued by the housing enforcement officer pursuant to this chapter shall be served upon persons either personally or by certified mail, return-receipt requested. If the whereabouts of the persons are unknown and cannot be ascertained by the enforcement officer in the exercise of reasonable diligence, then he shall make an affidavit to that effect, the serving of the complaint or order upon the persons may be made by publishing it once a week for two consecutive weeks in a newspaper printed and published in the town. A copy of the complaint or order also shall be posted in a conspicuous place on the premises affected by the complaint or order. A copy of the complaint or order also shall be filed with the county clerk of court as a lis pendens. 
Sec. 8-8. - Sale of materials; proceeds. 
    If a dwelling is removed or demolished by the housing enforcement officer, he shall sell the materials of the dwelling and shall credit the proceeds of the sale against the cost of the removal and demolition. Any balance remaining shall be deposited in the circuit court by the enforcement officer, secured in the manner as may be directed by the court, and shall be disbursed by the court to the persons found to be entitled thereto by final order or decree of the court. 
Sec. 8-9. - Housing enforcement officer. 
    The housing enforcement officer is hereby authorized to exercise the powers as may be necessary or convenient to carry out and affect the purposes and provisions of this chapter, including the following powers in addition to others herein granted: 
(1)  To investigate the dwelling conditions in the town in order to determine which dwellings therein are unfit for human habitation; 
(2)  To administer oaths and affirmations, examine witnesses, and receive evidence; 
(3)  To enter upon premises for the purpose of making examinations, provided, that the entries are made in a manner as to cause the least possible inconvenience to the persons in possession; 
(4)  To appoint and fix the duties of the officers, agents, and employees, with the approval of the town administrator, as he deems necessary to carry out the purposes of this chapter; and 
(5)  To delegate any of his functions and powers under this chapter to the officers and agents as he may designate. 
Sec. 8-10. - Board of adjustments and appeals. 
    The board of adjustments and appeals shall have all of the powers granted to the housing enforcement officer herein and may carry out its orders through its own actions or those of the enforcement officer or other officers and agents as it may designate. 
Sec. 8-11. - Appeals. 
(a)  Any person receiving an order from the housing enforcement officer may, within 15 days following the date of posting and service of the order, enter an appeal in writing to the board of adjustments and appeals. The appeal shall state the location of the property, and the appellant shall state the variance or modification requested, the reasons therefore, the date of the notice of violations and the number of the notice. The appellant shall further state the reasons, hardship, or conditions upon which the appeal is made 
(b)  The board of adjustments and appeals shall notify the appellant at least seven days in advance of the date of the hearing set on his appeal, stating the time and place of the hearing. The board may consider any matter contained in the record of the housing enforcement officer and may take any additional testimony that may be offered by the appellant or the enforcement officer. After the hearing on appeal, the board shall report its findings of fact in support of its determination on the issues, which may affirm, modify, or reject the finding of fact, determinations and orders of the enforcement officer, and shall cause such to be served upon the appellant owner. 
(c)  The board may establish its own rules of procedure, provided the rules are not in conflict with this chapter of [or] the laws of the state. The rules of evidence prevailing in courts of law or equity shall not be controlling in appeals or hearings before the board. 
(d)  The housing enforcement officer shall not take any action on an order issued by him until after the 15-day period for the owner to appeal to the board of adjustments and appeals. An appeal to the board shall operate a stay of the order of the enforcement officer until the appeal is heard and the board has issued its order. 
(e)  Any person affected by an order issued under this chapter shall have the right to appeal to the circuit court within 60 days after the posting and service of such order issued by the housing enforcement officer, or within 60 days of posting and service of any order of the board of adjustments and appeals as provided in S.C. Code of Laws 1976, § 31-15-70, as amended. The remedies herein provide shall be exclusive remedies and no person affected by an order of the housing enforcement officer or board of adjustments and appeals shall be entitled to recover any damages for action taken pursuant to any order of the enforcement officer or board of adjustments and appeals or because of compliance by such person with any order of the enforcement officer or board of adjustments and appeals. 
Sec. 8-12. - Supplemental provisions. 
(a)  The provisions of this chapter shall not abrogate the powers of any other department of the town or repeal any criminal ordinance but shall be in addition to and is supplemental to any other provision of this Code and any other ordinance of the town. The procedures enumerated in this chapter shall be the procedures followed in dealing with dwellings unfit for human habitation, the provisions of any previously adopted standard housing code notwithstanding. 
(b)  Nothing in this chapter shall be construed to impair or limit the power of the town to define and declare nuisances and to cause their removal or abatement by summary proceedings or otherwise. 
Chapter 9 - BUSINESS LICENSES 
ARTICLE I. - GENERALLY 

Sec. 9-1. - Adoption by reference. 
    The business license regulations established by Ordinance 2007-09, as contained in a separate business license pamphlet, are adopted by reference and made a part hereof as fully as if set out at length herein. 
Sec. 9-2. - Special event permits. 
    Purpose. The town recognizes the importance and necessity of regulating special events for various reasons: traffic control, avoiding a nuisance to others, controlling the effect on the surrounding area, and the like. 
    Application. 
(A)  This chapter shall apply to all special events in the town involving an outdoor activity on public or private property. 
(1)  All such activities must be of a temporary nature and cannot become permanent. 
(2)  All such events and activities shall be allowed only upon approval, as required, and the issuance of a special event permit. 
(B)  A special event likely to have a minor impact upon the town and its environs shall be allowed following approval by the town administrator or his or her designee. Examples of special events considered to have a minor impact are: grand openings, open-air tent sales, commercial promotional activities, block parties, and craft fairs. 
(C)  Special events likely to have a major impact on the town and its environs shall be allowed, following approval by the town administrator or his or her designee. Examples of such events are as follows: circuses, carnivals, parades, motion picture productions, and activities with loudspeakers or amplified music systems. 
(1)  The following requirements shall apply to special events likely to have a major impact: 
(a)  Schools, churches, and governmental entitles engaged in special events utilizing their own property are excluded from these requirements. 
(b)  In order to ensure the public safety and protection of the Town of Cheraw, its businesses, and citizens, and to avoid conflict between events by assigning the same time and location to two or more events, the Town of Cheraw may refuse or require alterations to a special event permit. 
(c)  The applicant must provide adequate security for the event, as directed by the Town of Cheraw Police Department. Applicant may be required to hire sworn off-duty law enforcement officers or hire private security personnel approved by the Town of Cheraw Police Department to ensure public safety. 
(d)  The applicant must provide adequate patting and must submit a plan for the event's anticipated parting to include an exit plan for approval by the Cheraw Police Department. 
(e)  Special events must shut down operations no later than 10:00 p.m. Sunday through Thursday and 11:00 p.m. Friday through Saturday. Events cannot begin before 10:00 a.m. Monday through Saturday and 1:00 p.m. on Sunday. 
(f)  Applicant must provide plan for cleanup and trash removal which must be approved by the town's codes officer. 
(g)  Applicant must present certificates of liability insurance coverage with a minimum of $1,000,000.00 per occurrence. 
(h)  Special event permit must be obtained and approved at least 15 days before event. 
(i)  The special event permit will be granted for the dates indicated in the application and applicant will be required to reapply for a new special event permit should they consider returning to Cheraw during the year. Applicant will be limited to obtaining two special event permits during a calendar year. 
(j)  Preparation and sale of food requires contacting the South Carolina Department of Health and Environmental Control. 
(Ord. No. 2015-10, 6-9-2015) 
Sec. 9-3. - Regulation of garage/yard sales and outdoor flea markets. 
(a)  Purpose of section. The purpose of this section is to protect the property and to preserve the peace and safety of the people of the town by regulation and control of garage and/or yard sales and outdoor flea markets. 
(b)  [Definitions.] The following words, terms, and phrases, when used in this chapter, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
    Outdoor flea market means any person or aggregation, congregation, or assembly of vendors, whether professional or nonprofessional, that offers for sale, trade or barter any goods, regardless whether they are new, used, antique or handmade; and where offered for sale in open air areas. 
    Garage and/or yard sale means any sale operated out of one-family, two-family or multi-family dwellings including, but not limited to, a sale on the premises thereof. 
    Goods means any goods, wares, merchandise or any other personal property capable of being an object of sale as regulated herein. 
    Itinerant or transient vendor means any person, partnership, firm, corporation or association of individuals, whether public or private, charitable or noncharitable, that does not occupy a permanent space within a flea market area but does exhibit goods and offers such goods for sale, trade or barter on a day to day basis. 
    Permanent vendor means any person, partnership, firm, corporation or association of individuals, whether public or private, charitable or noncharitable, that occupies a permanent space within a flea market area, and that exhibits goods and offers such goods for sale, trade or barter. 
    Promoter means any person, associations, firm or corporation that promotes or sponsors flea market type activities by offering a space, booth or area for use by vendors to display and offer for sale goods, wares or merchandise for a fee or commission. 
(c)  General regulations pertaining to garage and/or yard sales. 
(1)  Prior to holding or conducting a garage/yard sale, a garage/yard sale permit must be obtained in person at the town hall. There is no charge for a permit. 
(2)  It shall be unlawful for any person, family or vendor to hold more than four garage/yard sales, whether in the same or another location, within the town during any calendar year. Charitable, religious, educational, governmental or nonprofit organizations are exempt from this regulation. 
(3)  Garage/yard sales are allowed between the hours of 7:00 a.m. and 5:00 p.m. 
(4)  It shall be unlawful for any person to conduct such sale for a period of longer than two consecutive days. 
(5)  Any goods offered for sale must be secondhand or used items owned by the persons or vendors conducting the sale and shall in no case have been purchased for the purpose of resale. 
(6)  No signs advertising such sale shall be located within a street right-of-way. 
(7)  Garage/yard sales on commercial property are prohibited with the exception of charitable, religious, educational, governmental or nonprofit organizations. If a nonprofit organization desires to conduct a garage sale on property not its own the nonprofit organization must present to the town a letter from the property owner authorizing the nonprofit organization to conduct a sale on the property. The letter must include the property address, the name of the nonprofit organization sponsoring the garage/yard sale and the dates the garage/yard sale is to take place and must be signed by the property owner. The nonprofit or charitable organization must also present to the town documentation that the organization is a certified nonprofit or charitable organization. 
(d)  General regulations pertaining to outdoor flea markets. 
(1)  Any person or other vendor seeking to promote or operate an outdoor flea market in the town shall file with the town administrator an application requesting a permit to conduct an outdoor flea market type activity. This application shall include complete information concerning the promoters or operators, the proposed location of the sale, the date and time when sale is to be conducted, and any other information deemed necessary by the town administrator or his designated representative. If, in the judgment of the town administrator, such an activity will not be to the detriment of the town, or its citizens, and not contrary to zoning or building regulations or other town ordinances, he shall be authorized to issue a permit. If in the opinion of the town administrator such will be to the detriment of the town or its citizens or will constitute a zoning or building code violation, he shall notify the applicant, stating the reasons for the denial of the permit; and the applicant shall have the right to appeal the denial to the town council. 
(2)  Any applicant who shall have obtained a valid permit from the town administrator to conduct an outdoor flea market shall secure from the town a business license to conduct such activity. For the purpose of procuring a business license, the promoter or vendor shall be deemed to be a commissioned merchant. The fee for such a business license is $500.00 per year. 
(3)  Location of an outdoor flea market will be limited to general commercial (GC) and limited industrial (LI) zoned districts in the town. 
(4)  Applicants desiring to hold an outdoor flea market must present a letter from the property owner authorizing such use of the property. 
(5)  Outdoor flea markets may remain open for business between the hours of 7:00 am and 6:00 pm for a maximum of two days per week. 
(6)  When an outdoor flea market type activity is sponsored or promoted by a recognized civic, nonprofit, or charitable organization and where it is deemed that the overall interest of the town will be served through a waiver of the license, then the council may, in its discretion, waive any requirements or fees associated with the operation of an outdoor flea market. 
(7)  The town council has the right to revoke any license or permit if the outdoor flea market becomes a public nuisance which includes but is not limited to the following: accumulation of any garbage or rubbish, becomes a visual blight, significant deviation from the original intent, becomes a public safety hazard including but not limited to fire and flood hazards, or creates a situation where the use interferes with parking or traffic, both vehicular and pedestrian. 
(Ord. No. 2016-06, 10-13-2015) 
Editor's note- Ord. No. 2016-06, adopted Oct. 13, 2015, set out provisions intended for use as § 9-2. To maintain the numbering of this Code, and at the editor's discretion, these provisions have been included as § 9-3. 
Secs. 9-4-9-20. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - MOBILE FOOD VENDORS[1] 

Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
Editor's note- Ord. No. 2017-03, adopted Oct. 10, 2016, set out provisions intended for use as §§ 9-3-9-12. To maintain the numbering of this Code, and at the editor's discretion, these provisions have been included as Art. II, §§ 9-21-9-32. 

Sec. 9-21. - Purpose. 
    This article establishes standards for mobile food vending that encourages a variety of food and dining choices in the Town of Cheraw. This is not applicable to peddlers and mobile food units approved for special events. Special event participation is a separate permitting process. 
(Ord. No. 2017-03, 10-11-2016) 
Sec. 9-22. - Definitions. 
    The following words, terms, and phrases, used in this chapter, shall have the ascribed meaning to them unless otherwise: 
    Branding merchandise means items bearing the business' name and/or logo used to build its brand and advertise. 
    Food trailer means a self-contained vehicle mounted to a truck or appropriate towing capacity vehicle used to sell food and hot and/or cold beverages. 
    Grocery truck means an enclosed motor vehicle facilitating the sale of locally grown fresh produce. The produce sold is in its original form and has not been altered or cooked in any way. 
    Mobile food unit means a self-contained enclosed temporary mobile retail establishment regulated and permitted by South Carolina Department of Health and Environmental Control (SCDHEC/DHEC) in order to operate. It offers pre-packaged and cooked and/or prepared edibles, locally grown vegetables, ice cream/snow cones, and hot and/or cold beverages. Examples include, but not limited to, ice cream/snow cone trucks, grocery truck, pushcart, food truck/trailer, or canteen (pre-packaged) vendors. 
    Mobile food permit means the paper/decal authorizing a mobile food vendor to operate in permitted locations. 
    Mobile vendor means a person, business, or entity permitted by the town to engage in the selling of food, beverages (no alcohol), or branding merchandise from pushcart, truck, or trailer. 
    Pre-packaged food means food already prepared and sealed as part of a food processing operation. The food does not require any cooking or preparation. They are edibles that may be microwavable. 
    Pushcart means a portable wheeled self-contained unit which does not rely on motorized assistance. A vendor pushes it from one location to another. 
(Ord. No. 2017-03, 10-11-2016) 
Sec. 9-23. - Mobile food permit, fees, transfer of permit, hospitality tax. 
    It shall be unlawful to sell or offer of sale any food, beverages, or merchandise from a mobile food unit within the town without a mobile food permit. 
(1)  Mobile food permit. 
a.  An annual business license covers one mobile food unit for the whole or any part of the year. There is a $25.00 fee for additional mobile food unit. The permit is valid from July 1 to June 30 each fiscal year. 
b.  A mobile vendor must obtain or have valid a business license from the town clerk's office as part of the application process. 
c.  The owner shall obtain and submit with application her/his South Carolina Department of Health and Environmental Control (DHEC) permit. If exempt from DHEC food permit, provide signed exemption letter on letterhead from DHEC. Mobile unit must be in good standing with DHEC in order to operate. 
d.  The permit is non-transferrable. A change in ownership requires a new permit. Permits are listed under the business owner or company name. 
e.  Approved vendors must remit hospitality taxes. 
(Ord. No. 2017-03, 10-11-2016) 
Sec. 9-24. - Application process/submissions. 
    The application for mobile food permit includes the following and required submissions. 
(1)  Application information: 
a.  The business name, business owner name, mailing address, contact numbers, fax, website, if applicable, and DHEC permit number. 
b.  A description of activity included the number of mobile food units on a property, the physical address, and days of the week, and vending times. 
c.  A list of items to be sold. 
(2)  Submissions: 
a.  Provide an eight and one-half-inch by 11-inch color aerial map(s), Google, Bing, Mapquest, of the vending locations with streets. Print the property's business name and physical address and your business atop of the page. 
b.  Provide the latest copy of South Carolina Department of Health and Environmental Control (DHEC) permit/certification. Provide the original notarized property owner permission letter/lease agreement. 
c.  Provide the original permission authorization letter or lease agreement: 
1.  Private property owner permission letter must be signed and dated by property owner(s), included length of time (i.e. one year, six months, or month "x" to month "x"). 
2.  For town, Chesterfield County, and/or a division of the State of South Carolina owned properties. If the property owner is, written permission on entity's letterhead authorizing the use of property with length of time is required. 
(Ord. No. 2017-03, 10-11-2016) 
Sec. 9-25. - Location and operation. 
    Mobile food units shall conform to the following standards: 
(1)  Operate on private property in commercial, office, and industrial zoning districts from 7:00 a.m. to 12:00 p.m. Mobile food vendors are prohibited from operating on any street, sidewalk, alley, trail, or other right-of-way unless approved by the town as part of a permitted special event or contract with the town. 
(2)  Be self-contained. 
(3)  Cannot move to a location not covered by permit(s). 
(4)  Cannot block entrances block aisles, or other access to loading/service or emergency service (i.e. fire lanes) areas, create traffic congestion, or imped/obstruct pedestrian access or vehicular circulations. 
(5)  Are not allowed to use audio amplification to attract customers. 
(6)  Must visibly display permit decal and DHEC inspection grade for review and inspection. For trucks and trailers, the permit decal and DHEC Inspection Grade need to be displayed in the front right corner of the windshield. For push carts, both need to be displayed in somewhere on the cart. 
(7)  Can only occupy premises actively used (property has a business) or improved (abandoned/closed business parking lot). No vacant, uninhabited, or wooded parcels. 
(8)  Permitted one display rack to showcase sellable items. Display rack can be no taller than four feet in height and width. Display rack or table shall be within three feet of unit. A display table cannot be larger than three feet by five feet in size. 
(9)  Cannot conduct sales from customer vehicles. 
(10)  Allowed one temporary outdoor seating area within ten feet of mobile vending unit. 
(11)  Cannot lean against or hang from any building or other structure. This includes any associate furniture or materials. 
(12)  Must be attended at all times during hours of operation. 
(13)  May not be parked in an approved location after operation hours. 
(14)  Outdoor seating, display, and associated materials must be removed from all permitted locations after closing hours at all locations. No associated material including mobile unit(s) may be stored or parking on premise, sidewalks, or public right-of-ways overnight. 
(15)  Allowed one menu board. 
(16)  Sell only items listed on mobile food vendor permit application and branding merchandise. 
(17)  Must have an operational 51b ABC rated fire extinguisher and/or K-class fire extinguisher all fryer operations on-site. 
(Ord. No. 2017-03, 10-11-2016) 
Sec. 9-26. - Minimum separation. 
    The following distances minimize land use conflicts, ensure access for egress/ingress and emergency services, and promote pedestrian and vehicular safety. Mobile units must adhere to the setbacks in accordance with the zoning district. Mobile food units shall be located: 
(1)  Two hundred feet from any customer entrance of any brick and mortar restaurant and/or outdoor dining area, unless authorized by restaurant owner. Restaurant owner must provide notarized permission and any stipulations. The written authorization must be submitted to the town with the mobile food vendor permit application. Vendor operator must be display letter or have it readily available for review. 
(2)  Three hundred feet from a school during school hours and two hours after dismissal. 
(3)  Fifteen feet from any fire hydrant, utility box/vault, or handicap ramp. 
(4)  Twenty-five feet from any driveway, entrance and/or exits. 
(5)  Minimum distance between mobile food units: 
a.  Fifty feet between food trucks/trailers. 
b.  Twenty feet between pushcarts. 
c.  Forty feet between pushcarts and food trucks/trailers. 
(Ord. No. 2017-03, 10-11-2016) 
Sec. 9-27. - Maximum number of mobile units per property. 
(a)  Two units on parcels between one-fourth and one-half acre. 
(b)  Three units on parcels between one-half and one acre. 
(c)  Four units on parcels over one acre. 
(Ord. No. 2017-03, 10-11-2016) 
Sec. 9-28. - Advertising. 
(a)  No off-premises signage. 
(b)  No third party advertising on mobile food unit or at vending location. A mobile food unit can only advertise its business operation and product(s). The vendor can sell branding items (i.e. t-shirts, pens, key chain) bearing business name to enhance its brand. Branding merchandise can be displayed in unit or on display rack. 
(c)  One sandwich board advertisement sign shall be permitted. The sign cannot be internally lit or have lighting incorporated in the design. The sandwich board sign cannot exceed an area of 12 square feet and no taller than four feet. It can only display business name and/or specials. Sandwich board must be within three feet of mobile unit. 
(Ord. No. 2017-03, 10-11-2016) 
Sec. 9-29. - Litter/waste disposal. 
    The town's trash receptacles may not be used to dispose of trash or waste without permission. Adjacent dumpsters may be utilized without written permission of the property owner. 
(1)  Mobile food units must have at least one trash receptacle sufficient on-site for customers to dispose wrappers, paper, disposable utensils, plates, and cups. The town encourages recycling. Recycling receptacles must be visible and marked. 
(2)  Vendors must keep a 25-foot radius around the mobile food unit clean during operation and upon ceasing operation at all locations. 
(3)  Grease and liquid waste shall not be disposed in tree pits, storm drains, any sanitary sewer system, parking lot or wooded area/vacant lot, or street. Grease and liquids can be disposed through a private contractor or contact the town's wastewater treatment plant. 
(Ord. No. 2017-03, 10-11-2016) 
Sec. 9-30. - Ice cream/snow cone truck provisions. 
(a)  Ice cream/snow cone trucks are permitted in any zoning district. 
(b)  The allowable hours of operation are between 8:00 a.m. to 30 minutes after sunset. 
(c)  A bell or musical may be sounded for a period not to exceed two minutes to announce arrival of the vehicle at each location. 
(d)  Truck must remain mobile except for periodic stops for short intervals of time to make sales.
