(e)  Vendor is prohibited from parking on private property to sell items. Sales must be conducted off a public street only. In order to sell on private streets and drives, vendors must provide written notarized letter from property owner. 
(f)  Vendor can only sell items listed mobile food vendor permit application and branding merchandise. 
(Ord. No. 2017-03, 10-11-2016) 
Sec. 9-31. - Suspension and revocation. 
(a)  The town may suspend or revoke mobile food permit, if the vendor violates the provisions contained in this article or the vendor's South Carolina DHEC permit to operate as a mobile food unit is suspended or revoked. 
(b)  The vendor permit may be suspended or revoked if it is determined the mobile operation causes parking and/or traffic congestion, litter problems, community divisiveness, engages in illegal activity, and/or threatens public health and safety. 
(c)  Fraud or misrepresentation on the mobile vendor permit application will result in permit suspension or revocation. 
(Ord. No. 2017-03, 10-11-2016) 
Sec. 9-32. - Penalties. 
    Failure or refusal to comply with a notice of violation (NOV) is punishable per section 1-6, General penalty; continuing violations. The violation carries a fine not exceeding $500.00 or imprisonment not exceeding 30 days, or both. 
(Ord. No. 2017-03, 10-11-2016) 
Chapter 10 - MOTOR VEHICLES AND TRAFFIC 

Sec. 10-1. - Adoption of state laws. 
    All the provisions of the general laws of the state in regard to vehicles, traffic, and pedestrians contained in the S.C. Code of Laws 1976, as amended, and acts amendatory thereof, insofar as such provisions can be applied within the town limits are hereby adopted and made a part of this chapter as fully as though set out herein. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to fail to comply with the provisions of the acts and code referred to above, and this section shall be cited in arrant for violation of any of the provisions applicable to the town. 
Sec. 10-2. - Powers and duties of town council. 
(a)  The town council, except as otherwise directed by this chapter, shall have the power and is, hereby, authorized to regulate the operation and parking of vehicles within the town by the erection or placing of proper signs or markers indicating prohibited or limited parking, restricted speed area, one-way streets, through or arterial streets, U-turns, school zones, hospital zones, loading or unloading area, quiet zones, and any other signs, markers, and official traffic-control devices indicating the place or manner of operating or parking vehicles within the town. 
(b)  The council shall have the power and is authorized to secure all necessary signs, markers, or official traffic-control devices to be erected or placed on any street or part of a street when such action is deemed appropriate by the South Carolina Department of Transportation. 
Sec. 10-3. - Careless operation of a vehicle. 
(a)  It shall be unlawful for any person to operate any vehicle without care and caution in full regard for the safety of persons and property. Any person failing to do so, shall be guilty of careless driving or riding. The operation of any vehicle when the same or any of its appliances is not in proper or safe condition shall be prima facie evidence of the careless driving or riding; careless operation is unlawful and may be a lesser included offense of reckless driving. 
(b)  It is a misdemeanor for any person to do any act or fail to perform any act required in this chapter. 
Sec. 10-4. - Parking heavy vehicles on town streets prohibited. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to park or leave unattended on any street within the town any truck or tractor-trailer unit of over two-ton capacity. For the purpose of this section, "any street" shall include any sidewalks and tree zones bordering such streets and belonging to the town. "Tractor trailer unit" shall encompass the entire unit, the tractor alone, or the trailer alone. 
    Nothing in this chapter shall be construed to prohibit or otherwise limit the loading and unloading of trucks, not [nor] shall the prohibitions herein pertain to emergency stops and parking. 
Sec. 10-5. - Emergency vehicles to operate without interference. 
    It shall be unlawful for a driver of any vehicle other than one on official business to follow an ambulance, a fire truck, a police vehicle, or any other vehicle designated as an "authorized emergency vehicle" in S.C. Code of Laws 1976, § 56-5-170, as amended, actually engaged in emergency activities closer than 500 feet or drive into or park such vehicle within a block where the emergency vehicle has stopped in response to the emergency, whichever is greater. 
Sec. 10-6. - Parking of heavy vehicles in town. 
(a)  Parking of commercial vehicles and buses in residential districts prohibited. 
(1)  No person shall park, store, or knowingly permit any person to park or store a commercial vehicle on any street, road, right-of-way within the town in a residential district or on any residential lot at any time of day or night. 
(2)  A commercial vehicle includes a vehicle that is: 
a.  A tractor-trailer; or 
b.  Transports 16 or more passengers; [or] 
c.  Used to transport hazardous materials; or 
d.  Having more than six tires and which bears any sign or marketing which advertises or identifies any business or commercial interest. 
The above restrictions shall not apply to churches, or private or public school buses. 
(3)  Individuals who have a commercial vehicle as their only means of transportation may park the tractor, only, on their own residential property as long as the vehicle is completely off of the public right-of-way. Individuals wishing to park such vehicles on properties of other individuals must have a notarized approval letter from such property owner before they are allowed to park said vehicle. 
(4)  Moving or delivery vans being loaded or unloaded for a period not to exceed 48 hours are exempt from this section. 
(5)  Trailers used in construction, renovations, or improvement activities shall be allowed on the construction site with a permit issued by the town's building official. 
(b)  Parking of trucks over three-quarters ton on street. No truck exceeding three-quarters ton on capacity shall park on any street within the town limits between the hours of 6:00 p.m. and 6:00 a.m.; provided, however, that the operator of such truck may park for the purposes of eating and other personal needs for a period not exceeding one hour. No such truck shall park on any street within the town limits between the hours of 6:00 a.m. and 6:00 p.m. except for the purposes of loading and unloading and no such truck shall be permitted to remain parked. 
(Ord. No. 2008-06, 12-11-2007; Ord. No. 2008-10, 3-11-2008) 
Sec. 10-7. - Prohibition of truck traffic in residential areas. 
(a)  Definitions. The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this article, shall have the meaning ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
    No truck zone means an area comprised of all roads within the town limits of Cheraw as defined in subsection (f) below. Trucks, as defined in this section, are not allowed in the no truck zone unless they are delivering to or taking on freight from a business located within the no truck zone. 
    Truck means a vehicle which either (a) has six or more tires, or (b) that has a gross weight of 20,000 pounds or more. 
    Truck route means designated roads that trucks use to travel around the no truck zone. 
(b)  Penalties. A violator of any provision of this section shall upon conviction be deemed guilty of a misdemeanor and shall be subject to the following fines: 
(1)  First offense, $100.00; 
(2)  Second offense, $200.00; 
(3)  Third offense, $300.00; 
(4)  Fourth offense, $500.00. 
(c)  Through traffic truck route. All trucks traveling through the Cheraw area to destinations outside of the no truck zone are prohibited from entering the no truck zone. All such trucks shall instead use the truck route, which is comprised of Highway 9, Highway 52 and Highway 1, as well as the truck route connecting Highway 9 to Highway 52 along the western side of Cheraw, and the truck route along the eastern side of Cheraw connecting Highway 1 and Highway 52 to a point where those highways rejoin Highway 1 and 52 and Highway 9. 
    Exceptions to this will apply to trucks traveling through the Cheraw area to destinations inside the Town of Cheraw. They may enter the no truck zone to deliver or pick up freight from businesses located in the town limits using the most direct route. 
(d)  Trucks making deliveries or pickups inside no truck zone. Trucks are allowed to enter the no truck zone to deliver to or pick up freight from businesses located within the zone. Such trucks must have a bill of lading which verifies the point of delivery or pickup. 
(e)  Intra-city conveyance. Every truck conducting intra-city conveyance shall use the most direct route from the point of original within the town limits to the destination inside the town limits. 
    All trucks based at a town business leaving Cheraw shall use the most direct route from the point of origin to SC Highway 9 and US Highways 1 and 52. 
(f)  No truck zone. Trucks are prohibited from traveling the following sections in town: 
(1)  That section of West Greene Street (S-13-146) from the intersection of Jersey Street (S-13-200) east to Greene Street (S-13-203). 
(2)  That section of Powe Street (S-13-227) from the intersection of Greene Street (S-13-203) east to Second Street (S-13-148). 
(3)  That section of Kershaw Street (S-13-27) from the intersection with SC Highway 9 east to the intersection with Second Street (S-13-148). 
(4)  That section of State Road (S-13-413 and S-13-341) from the intersection with SC Highway 9 north and east to the intersection with US Highway 52. 
(5)  That section of Depot Street (S-13-197) from the intersection of SC Highway 9 south to West Market Street (S-13-22). 
(6)  That section of Beverly Drive (S-13-180) from the intersection of SC Highway 9 and US 1 north to Victory Drive (S-13-733). 
(7)  That section of Lynn Avenue (S-13-732) from the intersection of Front Street (S-13-205) east to Beverly Drive (S-13-180). 
(8)  That section of Victory Drive (S-13-733) from the intersection of Front Street (S-13-205) east to Beverly Drive (S-13-180). 
(9)  That section of Market Street (S-13-589) from its intersection with Jersey Street (S-13-200) east to the intersection with Front Street (S-13-205). 
(10)  That section of Second Street (S-13-148) from its intersection with Powe Street (S-13-227) south to the intersection with Church Street (S-13-86). 
(11)  That section of Church Street (S-13-86) from its intersection with Christian Street (S-13-639) east to the intersection with Second Street (S-13-148). 
(12)  That section of ACL Avenue (S-13-188) from its intersection with Martin Luther King Drive north to Chestnut Street. 
(13)  That section of Davis Street (S-13-426) from its intersection with the Cheraw Truck Route, formerly Cash Road (S-13-148), west to Godfrey Street (S-13-731). 
(14)  That section of Maynard Street (S-13-229) from its intersection with Second Street west to Huger Street (S-13-97). 
(15)  That section of Howard Street (S-13-380) from its intersection with the Cheraw Truck Route, formerly Cash Road (S-13-148), west to Davis Street (S-13-426). 
(Ord. No. 2008-05, 2-12-2008; Ord. No. 2016-14, 5-10-2016) 
Editor's note- Ord. No. 2008-05, adopted Feb. 12, 2008, set out provisions intended for use as § 10-9. To maintain the numbering of this Code, these provisions have been included as § 10-7. See also the Code Comparable Table. 
Sec. 10-8. - Display of motorized vehicles for sale in residential areas. 
(a)  Displaying of motorized vehicles for sale will be limited to one vehicle per lot in residential areas. 
(b)  Motorized vehicles includes automobiles, boats, motor cycles, RV's, personal watercraft, scooter, noncommercial trailers, pieces of motorized lawn equipment, etc. 
(c)  Maximum length of time a motorized vehicle can be displayed for sale is 30 days. 
(Ord. No. 2013-02, 11-23-2012) 
Sec. 10-9. - Engine compression brakes prohibited. 
(a)  Definitions. Engine compression brakes means the use of the engine and transmission to retard the forward motion of a vehicle by compression of the engine. Engine compression brakes are also referred to as "jake brakes". 
(b)  No person shall use engine compression brakes anywhere within the Town of Cheraw unless the brakes are muffled. It shall be an affirmative defense that said unmuffled engine compression brakes were applied in an emergency to protect persons and/or property. 
(c)  This section will not apply to fire engines, ambulances, aid trucks, police vehicles, and any other emergency vehicles. 
(Ord. No. 2013-05, 12-11-2012) 
Chapter 11 - MUNICIPAL COURT 

Sec. 11-1. - Established. 
    There is hereby established a municipal court for the Town of Cheraw, which shall be a part of the unified judicial system of the State of South Carolina, pursuant to Act. No. 480 of 1980, for the trial and determination of all cases within its jurisdiction. 
Sec. 11-2. - Municipal judge. 
(a)  Each municipal judge shall be appointed by the council for a term set by the council of not less than two years but not more than four years and until his successor is appointed and qualified. 
(b)  The council shall notify the South Carolina Court Administration of any persons appointed or reappointed as municipal judges. 
(c)  Before entering the discharge of the duties of his office, each judge shall take and subscribe the oath of office prescribed by Article VI, Section 5 of the South Carolina Constitution. 
(d)  The compensation of the municipal judge shall be as from time to time determined by council. 
(e)  Vacancies shall be filled in accordance with S.C. Code § 14-25-25. 
Sec. 11-3. - Eligibility for judgeship; vacancy in office, and temporary absence. 
(a)  A municipal judge shall not be required to be a resident of the Town of Cheraw. The town may contract with any other municipality in the county or with the county governing body to employ the municipal judge of the other municipality or a magistrate to preside over its court. 
(b)  In case of a vacancy in the office of municipal judge, a successor shall be appointed in the manner of original appointment for the unexpired term. 
(c)  In case of temporary absence, sickness, or disability of a municipal judge, the court shall be held by a judge of another municipality or by a practicing attorney or some other person who has received training or experience in municipal court procedure, who shall be designated by the mayor and take the prescribed oath of office before entering his duties. 
Sec. 11-4. - Clerk of court. 
    The police department shall designate a clerk of the municipal court, who shall keep such records and make such reports as may be required by the municipal judge or the state court administrator. 
Sec. 11-5. - Powers, duties, and jurisdiction of municipal court. 
    The municipal court shall have jurisdiction to try all cases arising under the ordinances of the town. The court shall also have all such powers, duties, and jurisdiction in criminal cases made under state law and conferred upon magistrates. The court shall have the power to punish for contempt of court by imposition of sentences up to the limits imposed on municipal courts. The courts shall have no jurisdiction in civil matters. 
Sec. 11-6. - Maximum penalties that court may impose; restitution; contempt. 
(a)  Whenever the municipal judge finds a party guilty of violating a municipal ordinance or state law with[in] the jurisdiction of the court, he may impose a fine of not more than $500.00 or imprisonment for 30 days, or both. 
(b)  In addition, a municipal judge may order restitution in an amount not to exceed $5,000.00. In determining the amount of restitution, the judge shall determine and itemize the actual amount of damage or loss in the order. 
(c)  A municipal judge may hold a party in contempt for failure to pay the restitution ordered if the judge finds the party has the ability to pay. 
Sec. 11-7. - Disposition of fines and penalties. 
    All fines and penalties collected by the municipal court shall be forthwith turned over to the clerk for deposit to the general fund of the town. 
Sec. 11-8. - Appeals, procedures, and time limits. 
    Any party shall have the right to appeal from the sentence or judgment of the municipal court to the court of general sessions. Notice of intention to appeal, setting forth the grounds for appeal, shall be given in writing and served on the municipal judge or the clerk of the municipal court within ten days after sentence is passed or judgment rendered, or the appeals shall be deemed waived. The party appealing shall enter into a bond, payable to the town, to appear and defend such appeal at the next term of the court of general sessions or shall pay the fine assessed. 
Sec. 11-9. - Judge to make return in event of appeal. 
    In the event of an appeal, the municipal judge shall make a return to the court of general sessions as provided by S.C. Code § 14-25-105. 
Sec. 11-10. - Right to jury trial; composition of jury; jury commissioners. 
(a)  Any person to be tried in the municipal court, may, prior to trial, demand a jury trial, and such jury, when demanded, shall be composed of six persons drawn from the qualified electors of the municipality in the manner prescribed by law. The right to a jury trial shall be deemed to have been waived unless demand is made prior to trial. 
(b)  The town council shall serve as jury commissioners for the municipal court. 
Sec. 11-11. - Commissioners to prepare jury box. 
    The jury commissioners shall, within the first 30 days of each year, prepare a box to be known as the jury box, and shall be composed of all names on the official list of qualified electors of the town furnished by the state election commission each year. This jury box may be drawn and summoned by computer in the manner the Supreme Court by order directs. 
Sec. 11-12. - Ministerial recorder. 
    There is hereby established the office of the ministerial recorder. Ministerial recorders shall be elected from time to time by council and shall serve at its pleasure. Ministerial recorders shall have the power to set and accept bonds and recognizances and to issue summonses, subpoenas, arrest warrants, and search warrants in all cases arising under the ordinances of the town and in criminal cases as are now conferred by law upon magistrates. Ministerial recorders shall have no other judicial authority and shall not be law enforcement officers. 
Sec. 11-13. - Prosecution in magistrate's courts. 
    The town, pursuant to the authority of S.C. Code of Laws 1976, §§ 14-25-5 through 14-25-205, may prosecute apportion of its cases in the magistrate's courts of the county [town] upon approval by the county [town] council. Such courts are hereby vested with the authority to try and determine all cases arising under municipal ordinances or state law within the jurisdiction of municipal or magistrate's courts. 
Chapter 12 - PUBLIC NUISANCES 

Sec. 12-1. - Definitions. 
    As used in this chapter, the following terms shall have the following meaning unless the context clearly indicates that a different meaning is intended: 
    Abate. Repair, replace, remove, demolish, destroy, or otherwise remedy the condition in question by such means, in such time, in such a manner and to such an extent as the enforcement officer or hearing committee shall determine to be in the best interest of the public, taking into account all facts and circumstances. 
    Business days. Monday through Friday, except for a holiday. 
    Enforcement officer. A law enforcement officer, code enforcement official, or town employee or official as may be designated by the town council to enforce the provisions of this chapter. 
    Graffiti. Any unauthorized inscription, word, figure, painting, or other defacement that is written, marked, etched, scratched, sprayed, drawn, painted, or engraved on or otherwise affixed to any surface of public or private property by any graffiti implement, to the extent that the graffiti was not authorized in advance by the owner or occupant of the property, or despite advance authorization. 
    Hearing board. A board appointed by the mayor, with approval of the council, which may have the powers described within this chapter. 
    Industrial wastes. All liquid and water-born solid, liquid, or gaseous wastes resulting from industrial manufacturing, food processing operation, processing any natural resource or mixture of such wastes with water or domestic sewage. 
    Person. Any landlord, property owner, manager, lessee, tenant, or individual, group, association, corporation, partnership, trust, estate, or received [receiver?] having the capacity to sue or be sued. 
    Premises. Any building, lot, parcel, real estate, or land or portion of land whether improved or unimproved, occupied or unoccupied, including adjacent parking areas. 
    Public nuisance. As determined by the enforcement officer based upon the facts and circumstances found after reasonable inquiry, investigation or upon citizen report, those conditions or events which constitute an unreasonable interference with rights of the public in general, and where the public is likely to come within the range of influence through the senses, a person unlawfully does an act or omits to perform a duty, which act or omission does any one or more of the following: 
(1)  Annoys, injures, subverts or endangers the public's order, economy, resources, safety, health, welfare, comfort, repose, or offends public decency; 
(2)  Unlawfully interferes with, obstructs or tends to obstruct, or renders dangerous for passage any waters or public places or way. 
    Structure. Anything constructed, built or planted upon, any edifice or building of any kind, or any piece of work artificially built up or composed of parts joined together in some definite manner, which structure requires location on the ground or is attached to something having a location on the ground. 
Sec. 12-2. - Nuisances. 
(a)  Nuisances affecting public health. The following are hereby declared to be nuisances affecting public health: 
(1)  All decayed or unwholesome food products or food waste not properly contained either inside or outside for more than 24 hours before normal pick up; 
(2)  Litter, debris, trash, or refuse which has not been placed within the appropriate container or containers for waste; 
(3)  All pools of stagnant water or vessels holding stagnant water in which mosquitoes can breed, excluding required retention ponds; 
(4)  Swimming pools which either: 
a.  Are empty, excluding such pools that are completely and effectively covered; or 
b.  Contain liquids and/or debris which are not bacteriologically, chemically, or physically safe for swimming or other intended uses; 
(5)  Animal carcasses not buried or disposed of in a lawful and sanitary manner within 24 hours after its death; 
(6)  Leaking septic tanks or sewer lines or other sewage existing in an unsanitary manner; 
(7)  Weeds or other rank growths of vegetation upon private or public property and all other vegetation at any stage of maturity which: 
a.  Exceeds 12 inches in height, except for healthy trees, shrubs, or plants grown in a tended and cultivated garden or plot; 
b.  Regardless of height, harbors, conceals, or invites rodents, pests, or vermin or deposits of refuse; 
c.  Gives off noxious odors; or 
d.  Constitutes a fire or traffic safety hazard; 
(8)  Damaged or diseased limbs of trees or trees to the extent of potential injury to the public at-large due to imminent structural failure; 
(9)  Deliberate placement or discharge into any part of a storm water drainage system of: untreated sewage, sewage solids, processed wastewater, refuse, explosive or combustible liquid, solid or gas, oils, greases, industrial water or other polluted water except where a federal, state, or local permit for connections, discharge, or disposal has been obtained prior to the event; or waters or wastes containing toxic or poisonous wastes to constitute a hazard to humans, plants, or animals or to cause corrosion, discoloration or deposition on real or person property; of any solid or viscous substances in such quantities or of such size capable of causing obstruction to the flow in the storm water drainage system or other interference with the proper operation of the drainage system of the Town of Cheraw. 
(b)  Nuisances affecting public decency, peace and order. The following are hereby declared to be public nuisances affecting public decency, peace and order, when such violations are of a continual, reoccurring or constant nature, provided, however, that no person shall be held liable or no structure shall be declared a nuisance in the event that person does not generate, enable, or contribute to the occurrence of unlawful behavior by a management policy or practice, personal conduct, lack of control or supervision, absence or ineffectiveness of security or other factors. 
(1)  Any structure, whether commercial or residential, where gambling devices, slot machines, punch boards or other such contrivances of similar character involving elements of chance as a consideration or any type of gambling, bookmaking, wagering or betting is carried on, and all gambling equipment except where such specific form of gambling is permitted by applicable law; 
(2)  Any structure, whether commercial or residential, operated as a bawdy house, house of assignment, place of prostitution, or used and maintained for the commercial or criminal purposes of unlawful sexual activity in violation of federal, state, or local law; 
(3)  Any structure, whether commercial or residential, where intoxicating liquors are manufactured, sold, bartered, or given away in violation of federal, state, or local law, or where intoxicating liquors kept for sale, barter, or distribution in violation of federal, state, or local law, and all liquors, bottles, kegs, pumps, bars, and other property kept at and used for maintaining such a place; 
(4)  Any structure, whether commercial or residential, where acts of sale, possession, or distribution of controlled substances occur in violation of federal, state, or local law; 
(5)  Any structure, whether a commercial operation or residential use, where breaches of the peace, disorderly conduct or offenses against the person found in Chapter 3, Title 16 of the S.C. Code of Laws, offenses against the person as may be found in the Town Code occur with such disproportionate frequency when compared to frequency of law enforcement action required at other similarly situated structures, or where the intensity of law enforcement response, when required, is disproportionate to the intensity of response required at other similarly situated structures. After notice of the continuing nature of the nuisance and specific identification of the facts and circumstances that either generate, enable, or contribute to the nuisance, the owner, lessee, renter, management of the person in control, may be held responsible for the maintenance of a public nuisance and the structure declared a public nuisance. 
a.  For purposes of subsection (b)(5) only, a commercial operation is defined as activity in which goods or services are exchanged for money or barter, or the rental or lease of accommodations for any length of time less than 30 days; a residential use is defined as single-family residences or multi-family residences. It is the intent of this chapter that commercial operations shall be held responsible which generate, enable, or contribute to the requirement of frequent or excessive law enforcement action due to a management policy or practice, personal conduct, lack of control or supervision, absence or ineffectiveness of security or other factors. When such management policy or practice, personal conduct, lack of control or supervision, absence or ineffectiveness of security or other factors are identified by law enforcement as generating enabling, or contributing to the disproportionate need for frequent or intensive law enforcement action, notice shall be provided to the commercial operation; such notice shall identify with particularity the management policy or practice, personal conduct, lack of control or supervision, absence or ineffectiveness of security or other factors that contribute to the intensity of unlawful behavior, and that further occurrences may result in the declaration of a public nuisance. If, after notice, the management policy or practice, personal conduct, lack of control or supervision, absence or ineffectiveness of security or other factors that are generating, enabling, or contributing to the frequency and intensity of unlawful behavior are not changed or modified, the owner, lessee, renter, management or the person in control, may be held responsible of the maintenance of a public nuisance and the structure declared a public nuisance. 
b.  For the purpose of subsection (b)(5) only, a residential use is defined as any residence in which a family or individual or individuals reside for a period exceeding 30 days. It is the intent of this chapter that owners, lessees, or renters of property shall be held responsible for the conduct of the residents, invitees or guests that generate, enable or contribute to the requirement of frequent or intensive law enforcement action. When conduct is identified by law enforcement as generating, enabling, or contributing to the disproportionate need for frequent or intensive law enforcement action, notice shall be provided to the owner, lessee, or renter; such notice shall identify with particularity the conduct that is generating, enabling, or contributing to the frequency and intensity of unlawful behavior, and that further occurrences may result in the declaration of a public nuisance. If, after notice, the conduct that is generating, enabling, or contributing to the frequency and intensity of unlawful behavior is not changed or modified, the owner, lessee, renter, management of the person in control, may be held responsible and the structure declared a public nuisance. 
(c)  Nuisances affecting public welfare and safety. The following are hereby declared to be public nuisances affecting public welfare and safety: 
(1)  All trees, hedges, signs, or other obstructions, or any portion of the same, so located on private property which prevent persons driving vehicles approaching an intersection of streets from having a clear safe view of traffic approaching such intersection; 
(2)  All trees, hedges, signs, or other obstructions, or any portion of the same, so located on private property which prevents the clear and unobstructed view of a fire hydrant, fire department connection, or other such fire protection device, or directional or identification signage pertaining to the above, from a public way; 
(3)  Any obstruction erosion or depression which poses a potential hazard to vehicles or pedestrians using a right-of-way on private property where the public is invited or permitted to traverse for commercial purposes; 
(4)  All wires, strings, ropes, or lighting contrivances over streets, alleys, or public grounds which are not authorized or permitted by the town or which have been strung so that the lowest potion is less than 131/2 feet above the surface of the ground; 
(5)  All explosives, flammable liquids, and other dangerous substances stored in any manner, in any amount, other than that manner or amount permitted by law; 
(6)  All hanging signs, awnings, canopies, and other similar structures over the streets and sidewalks so situated or constructed as to endanger public safety or to be contrary to local ordinance; 
(7)  Any motor vehicle that is unregistered, inoperable, derelict, or abandoned on any highway or right-of-way, other public or private property, unless [the] vehicle is stored inside of a building; 
(8)  Any abandoned or discarded icebox, refrigerator, ice chest, freezer, or other type of air-tight container whose door, lid, or other closing device has not been removed. 
(d)  Nuisances affecting public economy. The following are hereby declared to be public nuisances affecting the public economy: 
(1)  All structures bearing graffiti, to be abated by applicable law; 
(2)  All structures in violation of the International Property Maintenance Code, as adopted, and all structures, for a period of one month, which remain unoccupied and boarded-up, and whose exterior finish is destroyed, decayed, dilapidated, or deteriorated in violation of the International Property Maintenance Code, as adopted, provided, however, unoccupied structures shall not be considered a public nuisance affecting public economy if the building exterior is weather tight and maintained for purposes of appearance and security according to the International Property Maintenance Code, and the material which secures the building is compatible with the exterior in appearance, color, texture, and design, and the premises are kept in compliance with all applicable building, property maintenance, zoning, and land use laws; 
(3)  All businesses or commercial enterprises operating without a valid, current, and displayed business license; 
(4)  All premises continually not in compliance with applicable licensing, zoning, and land use laws; 
(5)  All businesses with an outstanding arrearage of applicable town liens, taxes, fees, charges, or assessments; 
(6)  All premises which originate false fire or burglar alarms as defined by applicable law. 
(e)  Junk generally. It shall be unlawful for any person or firm, including an owner or occupant of any premises, dwelling, or structure, or vacant lot to place or leave or permit to be left outside of any premises, building, or lot any dilapidated furniture, icebox, refrigerator, stove, or other appliance, machinery, equipment, building material or parts thereof or other item which is wholly or partially rusted, wrecked, junked, dismantled, or inoperable. 
(f)  Junk yards. It shall be unlawful for any person or firm to do business as a junk dealer for any such junk materials including discarded vehicles, machinery, metal objects and other such commodities, unless the same be kept and stored within or beneath a covered, screened, or enclosed structure or in such other manner as prevents threat or occurrence of injury or damages by way of nuisance to the health or welfare of the public. It shall also be unlawful to deposit or leave such junk or permit such junk to be deposited or left on the public right-of-way in conjunction with such business. 
(g)  Noise. 
(1)  Generally. Subject to the following provisions of this section, the creation of any unreasonably loud, disturbing, or unnecessary noise in the town is prohibited. It shall be unlawful for any person to cause, make, or contribute to creating any loud or disturbing noise of such character, intensity, or duration as to be detrimental to the life or health of any individual or such noise as to disturb the quiet and peace of any citizen in the town. 
(2)  Unlawful acts enumerated. The following acts, among others, are declared to be loud, disturbing, or unnecessary noises and are not specifically prohibited by this section. The following shall not, however, necessarily include all such noises as may constitute a violation of subsection (1) of this section: 
a.  Blowing horns. The sounding of any horn, whistle, signal device on any motor vehicle, except as a danger signal or as required by law, so as to create any unreasonably loud or harsh sound or the sounding of such device for an unreasonable period of time is hereby prohibited. 
b.  Sirens. The use of any bong, bell, or siren on any motor vehicle other than police, fire, rescue, or other emergency vehicle permitted by law is hereby prohibited. 
c.  Sound amplifying devices. The playing of any radio, stereo, compact disc player, record player, tape recorder, television, musical instrument, or sound-producing or sound-amplifying device in such manner or with such volume as to annoy or disturb the quiet, repose, or comfort of any person in any dwelling, hotel, or other residence is hereby prohibited. 
d.  Blowing whistles. The blowing of any steam whistle attached to a boiler except as a warning of danger, to give notice to start or stop work, or as an indicator of time, is hereby prohibited. 
e.  Noises to attract attention. The use of any bell, drum, loudspeaker, or other instrument for the purpose of attracting attention by the creation of noise to any performance, show, sale, display, or advertisement of merchandise is prohibited. 
f.  Exceptions. The foregoing provisions of this section shall not apply to organized and lawfully permitted performances by bands, groups, etc., in parades or otherwise, or to the conduct of manufacturing operations as defined by the South Carolina Department of Revenue or the conduct of lawfully permitted vehicle races. 
g.  Emergency situations. Noise caused in the performance of emergency work for the immediate safety, health, or welfare of the community or individuals of the community or to restore property to a safe condition following a public calamity shall not be subject to the provisions of this section. 
Sec. 12-3. - Other nuisances. 
    The enumeration of specific nuisances in this chapter shall not be deemed to make lawful any other act or condition declared to be a nuisance by any other town ordinance, state or federal law, or court decision. 
Sec. 12-4. - Reporting emergencies and emergency actions. 
    Any person who directly observes a nuisance posing an emergency threat to the health or safety of the environment shall immediately report the incident to the Cheraw Police Department and shall provide any information requested by the law enforcement officer needed to investigate or abate the potential emergency. If any nuisance exists in such a condition so menacing to the public health, peace, or safety that it is necessary that it be summarily abated, the town enforcement officer, after consultation and concurrence with the town administrator may proceed to abate the nuisance without a hearing. 
Sec. 12-5. - Nuisances prohibited and unlawful. 
    No person shall create any public nuisance in the town, and no person shall by inaction permit a public nuisance to occur or continue on any real property under such person's control, whether by recorded or unrecorded instrument or permission. Nor shall any person permit a public nuisance to occur involving any personal property under such person's control. 
Sec. 12-6. - Institution of criminal process and penalty. 
    The public nature of a public nuisance must be made by an enforcement officer or other appropriate governmental official. Enforcement of this chapter's provisions may be accomplished upon the institution of criminal process by way of uniform traffic ticket, municipal ordinance summons, or warrant made only by a law enforcement officer or appropriate government official. Each day of violation constitutes a separate misdemeanor offense, subject to a fine not to exceed $500.00 and or up to 30 days imprisonment for each offense. In its discretion, the town may elect to use other applicable code sections pertaining to remediation or abatement of offenses. 
Sec. 12-7. - Public abatement; notice; service. 
(a)  If a person fails or refuses to discharge the duty imposed by section 12-5, the town may concurrently serve an administrative notice to abate a public nuisance upon the owner or occupant and demand that compliance must be achieved within seven consecutive days, after service of the notice, not including the date of receipt or posting. 
(b)  The town shall determine the individual, firm, or corporation or lien holder who, from the records in the county tax assessor's office, it appears to be the titled owner or lien holder of the property and cause a written notice of public notice to be served on such individual, firm, or corporation, or lien holder by: 
(1)  Personal service as attested to by affidavit of service; or by 
(2)  Copy mailed to such owner or lien holder at such place or address by United States Certified Mail, return receipt requested. 
(3)  After due diligence, if service is unable to be perfected as described above, the town shall cause a copy of the aforesaid notice to be posted at such structure, location, or premises, which shall serve as notice to the public. 
(c)  The notice to abate the nuisance shall inform the person of the specific nuisances with citation to this section, provide names, numbers and addresses for contact with the town; inform them of their rights to an appeal and that, upon the eighth day after receipt of service or posting, the town may abate the condition and assess an administrative fee and all public costs as a lien against the property. 
(d)  That in the event the town shall seek to demolish or remove a structure other than a dwelling, as the word is defined in section 8-3 of the Town Code, then the due process provisions of section 8-1 et seq., shall be followed in any action brought by the town as to said structure. 
Sec. 12-8. - Appeal proceedings; hearing. 
(a)  Appeal of finding of nuisance. The responsible person, owner, or occupant, or the lien holder of the property, may make a written demand to the town administrator for a hearing on the question of whether a public nuisance, in fact, exists. This appeal stays the public abatement until such time as the matter is heard and decided by the board of adjustments and appeals. The appeal must be received by the administrator within five business days of the posting or appellant's receipt of the notice to abate, excluding town recognized holidays and weekends. The written demand shall include an address, contact number, either phone or facsimile, in order for the person to be informed of the hearing location, date, and time. It shall not be a defense to the determination that a public nuisance exists that the property is boarded up or otherwise enclosed. The board may amend or modify the notice to abate the public nuisance or, when appropriate under the facts presented, extend the time for compliance by the owner to such date as the majority of the appeals board may determine. The decisions of the board are final and shall be delivered orally to the appellant on the date of the hearing and such decision shall be written and mailed to the address provided. 
(b)  Failure to appeal. Failure to appeal constitutes waiver of the right to appeal the existence of a public nuisance. 
(c)  Appeal of assessment. Further, in those instances where the nuisance has been abated by the town after the required notice of subsection 12-7(b), the owner or occupant of the property who has been served with a notice of assessment pursuant to section 12-9 of this chapter may make a written demand to the administrator for a hearing to review the cost of the abatement. This appeal stays the attachment of the lien until such time as the matter is heard and decided by the hearing board. The appeal of the assessment must be received by the administrator within five business days of the appellant's receipt of the notice of assessment. The written demand shall include an address, contact number, either phone or facsimile, in order for the person to be informed of the hearing location, date, and time. In an appeal of the assessment of costs, no testimony shall be permitted on the issue of the existence of the public nuisance. The decisions of the board are final and shall be delivered orally to the appellant on the date of the hearing, and such decision shall be written and mailed to the address provided. 
(d)  Failure to appeal assessment. Failure to timely appeal constitutes a waiver of the right to appeal the assessment of costs. 
(e)  Notice of hearing. By way of the address and contact numbers provided in the written demand, the administrator shall orally advise the owner of the location, date, and time of the hearing and shall also advise the person of the hearing in writing through regular mail. Notice of the hearing must be provided at least two business days prior to the hearing, excluding town-recognized holidays and weekends. 
(f)  Timing and manner of hearings. The hearings as allowed under this section shall be held as soon as practical, but in no event later than 20 business days after receipt of the appeal, excluding town recognized holidays and weekends. The hearing shall be informally conducted by the administrator or designee, chief of police or designee, and director of public works or designee. The enforcement officer shall present the facts and circumstances that resulted in a conclusion that a public nuisance existed. The owner, occupant, or lien holder, or their agents, representatives, or attorneys shall be given the opportunity to present evidence to the appeals board in the course of the hearing and shall have the right of cross examination of the enforcement officer. When the nuisance has been abated by the town and the person has appealed the assessment of the administrative fee and actual costs, the hearing board shall have discretion to waive the administrative fee or the public cost of abating a nuisance, in whole or in part, if, in the course of the hearing reviewing the decision, the hearing board finds that justice and equity require such waiver or that any of the following did not conform to the provisions of this chapter: 
(1)  The notice to remove the nuisance; 
(2)  The work performed in abating the nuisance; 
(3)  The computation of charges. 
Sec. 12-9. - Liability for costs. 
    In the event of refusal or neglect of a person to cause such nuisance to be abated in the manner and within the time provided herein, it shall be reported to the administrator, who may, in a reasonable and prudent manner, direct the expenditure of public resources to abate the nuisance condition. The cost of the abatement shall include an administrative assessment of $150.00 in addition to the actual cost of labor and materials expended in public abatement. The person shall be served with a notice of assessment within seven days of the completion of the abatement. The notice of assessment shall include the administrative fee and a statement of public costs, attested to by affidavit, and shall be issued and served, as provided for in subsection 12-7(b) upon the person responsible for payment who shall make payment within 30 days of the date of service. Upon the expiration of the 30-day period, if the amount has not been paid in full or contested before the administrator, the administrator may cause a lien in that amount to be filed with the county clerk of court and with the town clerk. The lien shall be of record in the county courthouse and the office of the town clerk in the book of liens, until paid or recovered, or otherwise released. Collection of the lien by way of recovery or foreclosure may be instituted by the town attorney on behalf of the town or through any other method available to the town. 
Sec. 12-10. - Liability of enforcing officers. 
    No person carrying out the provisions of this chapter shall be held to answer in any civil or criminal action. 
Chapter 13 - OFFENSES-MISCELLANEOUS 

Sec. 13-1. - Consumption of beer, wine, and alcohol restricted. 
(a)  All provisions and requirements of the general law of the state in regard to beer, wine, and alcoholic beverages as contained in the Alcoholic Beverage Control Act, S.C. Code of Laws 1976, 61-6 et seq., insofar as such provisions can have application within the town, are hereby adopted and made a part of this Code as fully as though set out herein. All persons within the town shall strictly comply with the regulations by such sections when so applicable. 
(b)  It shall be unlawful for any person to consume beer or wine on the street, sidewalk, or in lots commonly used by the public for parking within the town unless such location has been approved and licensed as a sidewalk cafe under the town's zoning ordinance and meets all local and state requirements. 
(c)  It shall be unlawful for any person to consume or sell beer, wine, liquor, or other intoxicating beverages in or upon publicly owned streets, parking lots, sidewalks, alleys, parks, playgrounds, or any other publicly owned property within the Town of Cheraw. 
Exceptions to this section will be limited to: 
(1)  Those business establishments that have obtained the proper permits to operate sidewalk or outdoor cafés. 
(2)  Events held at the Cheraw Community Center where proper permits relating to alcohol have been obtained. 
(Ord. No. 2011-16, 1-10-2012; Ord. No. 2014-06, 4-8-2014) 
Editor's note- Ord. No. 2011-16, adopted Jan. 10, 2012, changed the title of § 13-1 from "Alcoholic beverages-Adoption of state law" to "Consumption of beer, wine, and alcohol restricted." 
Sec. 13-2. - Arrest-Resisting. 
    No person shall resist any police officer or other peace officer of the town in making a legal arrest or other discharge of his duty. 
Sec. 13-3. - Burning grass and rubbish. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to burn or cause to be burned any grass, leaves, tree limbs, trash or rubbish of any kind or description whatsoever within the town, whether such grass, leaves, tree limbs, trash or rubbish be located upon private property or upon any of the public streets or alleys of the town, without first obtaining permission to do so from the fire chief. 
Sec. 13-4. - Disturbances-Assemblies. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to interrupt or disturb any audience or other lawful assembly of persons within the town limits by any noise, loud talking, indecent behavior, or other such boisterous or annoying behavior or conduct. 
Sec. 13-5. - False pretenses; obtaining property or signatures. 
    Any person who shall by any false pretense or representation obtain the signature of any person to any written instrument or shall obtain from any other person any money, valuable security, or other property, real or personal, with intent to defraud or cheat any person of the same shall be punished upon conviction in section 1-6 of this Code; provided, that this section shall only apply in cases in which the property or item of value so obtained has a value of $1,000.00 or less. 
Sec. 13-6. - Fireworks. 
    See Title 23, Chapter 35 of the S.C. Code of Laws, as amended. 
Sec. 13-7. - Loitering. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to loiter or congregate on any of the public sidewalks, streets, or public rights-of-way in such a manner as to interfere with or obstruct the free use of the same to the public. 
Sec. 13-8. - Curfew for juveniles. 
    It shall be unlawful for any minor 16 years of age of younger to loiter, wander, stroll, or play in or upon the public streets, highways, roads, alleys, parks, playgrounds, or other public grounds, public places, vacant lots, or other place unsupervised by an adult having the lawful authority to be at such places, between the hours of 12:00 midnight until 6:00 a.m. on the following day; provided that the provisions of this section shall not apply in the following instances: 
(1)  When a minor is accompanied by his or her parent, legal guardian, or other adult person (over 21 years of age) having the lawful care and custody of the minor; 
(2)  When the minor is upon an emergency errand directed by his or her parent or legal guardian or adult person (over 21 years of age) having the lawful care and custody of the minor; 
(3)  When the minor is returning directly home from a civic, school, or recreational activity; or 
(4)  When a minor is returning directly home form a lawful employment that makes it necessary for him to be in the above referenced places during the prescribed period of time. 
Sec. 13-9. - Parent, guardian, or responsible adult; penalty. 
    It shall be unlawful for the parent, guardian, or adult person having custody or control of any child 16 years of age or younger to permit, or by insufficient control, to allow such child to be in or upon the public streets or any other places listed in section 13-8 within the town between the hours of 12:00 midnight until 6:00 a.m. on the following day except in circumstances set out in subsections (1) through (4) of section 13-8. 
    Upon violation of this section for the first time, a person shall be given a warning citation. Upon conviction of this section, a person shall be subject to a fine not to exceed $500.00 and costs, or imprisonment in jail for not more than 30 days, or performance of public service work for the town for not more than 30 days, or be subject to any one or more of the stated penalties; subject to all limitations contained in the charter of the town. Each violation of this section shall constitute a separate offense. 
Sec. 13-10. - Parades. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to stage any parade or procession on any of the streets or in any other public places within the town without first having applied and secured a special permit from the police chief to do so, excepting funeral processions, the armed forces of the United States, the military forces of this state, and the force of the police and fire departments of the town. Such application shall contain the following information: the date and time of such proposed parade or processions; the streets to be used; the number of persons or vehicles to be engaged; and the purpose of such parade or procession. Upon receipt of such application, the police chief shall, in his discretion, issue such permit subject to the public convenience and public welfare. 
Sec. 13-11. - Scattering leaflets, etc. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to throw or scatter any advertising matter of any nature whatsoever on any street, lane, alley, sidewalk, public place, or on the premises or vehicle of another without permission of the owner. 
Sec. 13-12. - Discharging firearms. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to discharge, fire, or explode any handgun, rifle, shotgun, or other form of firearms, in the town limits; provide, however, that this section shall not be construed to regulate the protection of oneself from immediate dangers to life and limb. 
Sec. 13-13. - Shooting bows, arrows, slingshots, and missiles. 
    The shooting of bows and arrows, or the use of slingshots or any other device for throwing missiles within the town is hereby declared to be a nuisance and any person offending shall be liable to a fine or imprisonment for each and every offense. 
Sec. 13-14. - False alarms. 
(a)  No person shall make or cause to be made with intent to deceive, any false alarm by means of the fire alarm system, public or private alarm systems, telephone, or by any other means of communication. 
(b)  No person shall willfully make or cause to be made any false call for ambulance or rescue service by means of any communication. 
(c)  This section shall not apply to any authorized personnel while installing, testing, or repairing alarm systems in the normal course of employment. 
Sec. 13-15. - Penalties for repeated false alarms. 
(a)  Any person, firm, or corporation having a fire alarm, smoke detector, burglar alarm, or other type of alarm, and which alarm has a direct or indirect connection which calls for a response from the police or fire department, shall be allowed two false alarms during any one calendar year and will be charged a fee of $50.00 for the third false alarm responded to by the police or fire department within such calendar year and $200.00 for each false alarm responded to thereafter within such calendar year. 
(b)  Such fee may be waived if the possessor of the alarm shows to the satisfaction of the police or fire chief that the false alarm was not the result of negligence or improper maintenance. 
Sec. 13-16. - Damaging public utility poles and signposts. 
    No person shall willfully or wantonly injure or break any of the public street lights, or any lampposts, telephone, electric, telegraph, fire alarm post or any signpost or street sign. 
Sec. 13-17. - Tampering with property of public utilities; manhole covers. 
(a)  No person shall alter, remove, molest, or tamper with any wire, fixture, pipe, conduit, meter, or other appliance of the waterworks plant, gas, electrical, cable television, or telephone company or person operating a similar business; or tap any supply wires or pipes, or fraudulently or secretly extract or use water, electricity, cable television, or gas of the plant or company, or uncover or open any manhole of other opening to any sewer, unless the person doing so is an authorized employee of the company or the town, or under authority and director to do so. 
(b)  No person shall leave any manhole or other opening unprotected or open without replacing the fixtures and appliances in their proper place and position. 
Sec. 13-18. - Tampering with utility lines and posting bills on utility poles and signs. 
    No person shall meddle, tamper with, injure, break, cut, take down, or disarrange any telephone, cable television, electric light pole, fire or police alarm box or pole, or any wire cord, lamp or other apparatus used in operating or maintaining any utility or alarm system without authority to do so, or post any bills, signs, or posters of any kind whatsoever upon any such poles or posts within the town. 
Sec. 13-19. - Injury to flowers, shrubs, fences, grass plots, etc. 
    No person shall willfully and without authority cut, pull, pluck, or otherwise injure any flowers, flowering plants, shrubs, or trees growing in or around any public or private grounds or otherwise injure or destroy any gate, fence, bench, seat, bridge, building or other structures or property on public property. No person shall walk or injure any grass plots planted by the town where prohibitory signs are posted. 
Sec. 13-20. - Flags and decorations; removing or injuring. 
    No person shall remove, destroy, molest, deface, or disarrange any flag or other decoration that may be used by any person in, upon, or about any building to indicate celebration of any holiday or public event within [without] the consent of the owner. 
Sec. 13-21. - Damaging monuments and signs. 
    No person shall willfully remove, destroy, mutilate, damage, or deface, in any way or to any extent, any monument or sign in, on or upon any public park, street, cemetery, or private property of the town. 
Sec. 13-22. - Injuring public property and property open to the public. 
    No person shall willfully injure, destroy, or trespass upon, or illegally make use of any public property of any kind whatsoever belonging to, or in possession of, the town. 
Sec. 13-23. - Trespass for various purposes. 
    Any person entering upon the lands of another for the purpose of hunting, fishing, trapping, netting, gathering fruit, wild flowers, cultivated flowers, shrubbery, straw, turf, vegetables or herbs, or cutting timber on such land without the consent of the owner or manager thereof, shall be guilty of a misdemeanor and punished in accordance with section 1-6 of this Code. 
Sec. 13-24. - No smoking policy in town owned parks or recreation facilities. 
(a)  It shall be unlawful for any person to smoke within any town owned park or recreation facility. 
(b)  Smoking shall only be permitted in paved parking lots of such town owned park or recreation facility. 
(c)  Violation of such policy shall result in a fine of not less than $10.00 nor more than $25.00. 
(d)  Each day of a continuing violation of this policy shall be considered a separate and distinct offense. 
(Ord. No. 2013-12, 6-11-2013) 
Chapter 14 - POLICE DEPARTMENT 

Sec. 14-1. - Composition. 
    The police department shall consist of one chief and such other personnel as, from time to time, may be deemed necessary for the safety and good order of the town. 
Sec. 14-2. - Appointments. 
(a)  Chief. The chief of police shall be appointed by the mayor and town council and shall serve as the chief executive of the police force. 
(b)  Other police officers. The other police officers of the department shall be appointed by the chief of police with approval of the town administrator. 
Sec. 14-3. - Compensation. 
    The compensation for the services of each police department employee shall be set in accordance with the town's compensation plan within the limitations of the annual appropriations for the police department. 
Sec. 14-4. - Removal or suspension. 
    All police department employees are subject to removal or suspension in accordance with the town's personnel policy and procedures manual. 
Sec. 14-5. - Uniforms. 
    The officers of the police department shall be uniformed and equipped as may be designated by the council from time to time. All property issued to an officer shall remain the property of the town and shall be returned to the town whenever it is requested by the police chief or the town council. 
Sec. 14-6. - Police chief-Duties and responsibilities. 
(a)  The chief of police shall be responsible to the town administrator and the town council for the execution of the police mission. 
(b)  The chief shall be responsible for the organization, efficiency, training, discipline and morale of the police department. 
(c)  The chief shall ascertain that the operation of the police department and any special units under the chief's control mutually support one another in all matters requiring support and that a high degree of lateral cooperation and exchange of information is maintained. 
(d)  The chief shall ensure that all books and records are kept in accordance with current applicable federal, state, and municipal laws as required for the proper performance of the police department. 
Sec. 14-7. - Police officers-Duties. 
    It shall be the duty of each police officer to arrest and/or report any person for violating in any manner the laws or ordinances of the town and failure or neglect to do so shall make such officer liable to suspension or discharge. 
Sec. 14-8. - General demeanor. 
    Each member of the police department at all time shall conduct themselves in a quiet and orderly manner and with a deliberate and efficient determination of enforcing the laws and ordinances of the town. 
Sec. 14-9. - Off-duty conduct. 
    Each police officer while off-duty shall conduct himself in such a manner as to command the respect of the town. The officer shall wear no uniform or part thereof while off-duty without the expressed approval of the chief of police. 
Chapter 15 - STREETS AND SIDEWALKS 

Sec. 15-1. - Obstructions. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to place any obstruction on or in any way to obstruct any street, alley, bridge, ditch, or public right-of-way; provided, that this section shall not apply to any employee of the city, county, or state while such employee is immediately and actively engaged in the maintenance, improvement, or construction of any street, sidewalk, or public way in the town; nor to utility companies or others performing work thereon with approval by the town. 
Sec. 15-2. - Placing dangerous substances on streets, sidewalks, etc. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to place or cause to be placed on any of the sidewalks, streets, alleys, or other public places in the town any tacks, nails, glass, or other sharp instrument or material by which persons or animals may be injured or bicycles, automobiles, or other vehicles damaged. 
Sec. 15-3. - Depositing trash. 
    It shall be unlawful for any occupant of any house or any merchant, shopkeeper or tradesman in town to sweep or deposit in any street, public or private alley or public or private yard any paper, trash, or rubbish or any kind but the same shall be kept in boxes or appropriate receptacles. The boxes or receptacles must be provided with a cover suitable or sufficient to contain the contents. 
Sec. 15-4. - Display of goods. 
(a)  It shall be unlawful for any person, without expressed permission from the town council, to erect and maintain any table, stand, or other structure in any street, square, or alley or upon any sidewalk of the town for the purpose of exposing any commodity for sale of for any other purposes. 
(b)  No personal vehicle or motor vehicle offered for sale shall be placed or displayed within the street rights-of-way within the historic district of the town. Any such motor vehicle so parked, placed, or displayed may be towed away or otherwise removed at the direction of any police officer, and the owner of the vehicle shall be liable for the cost of towing or other removal and storage. If the motor vehicle is not reclaimed, then it shall be advertised and sold as in the case of sales of motor vehicles for nonpayment of personal property taxes, and the costs of towing or other removal and storage shall be deducted from the proceeds of the sale. 
Sec. 15-5. - Riding bicycles or skateboards on sidewalks. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to ride a bicycle or skateboard on the sidewalks along Market Street from Third Street to Front Street, on the sidewalks along Second Street from Church Street to Powe Street, and on the sidewalks on both sides of Short Market (Wall Street) within the town between the hours of 8:00 a.m. and 6:00 p.m. Monday through Saturday. 
Sec. 15-6. - Gates and doors opening onto streets and sidewalks. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to build, erect, or maintain any gate or door in such manner that the same may be opened out on to any sidewalk or street of the town. 
Sec. 15-7. - Encroaching fences. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to erect any fence that encroaches upon any street of the town, or to build any fences along the line of a street before having the property line of such street located by the appropriate official of the town. 
Chapter 16 - SUBDIVISIONS 
ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Sec. 16-1. - Short title. 
    These regulations shall be known, cited, and references [referred] to as the subdivision and development regulations of the Town of Cheraw. 
Sec. 16-2. - Policy. 
(a)  It is hereby declared to be the policy of the Town of Cheraw to consider the subdivision of land and the subsequent development of the subdivided plat as subject to the control of the town council to the official land development plan of the council for the orderly, planned, efficient, and economic development of the town. 
(b)  Land to be subdivided shall be of such character that it can be used safely for building purposes without danger to health or peril from fire, flood, or other menace, and land shall not be subdivided until available public facilities and improvements exist and proper provisions have been made to drainage, water, sewage, and capital improvements such as schools, parks, recreation facilities, transportation facilities, and improvements. 
(c)  The existing and proposed public improvements shall conform to and be properly related to the proposals shown in the land development plan, official map, and the capital budget and program of the town, and it is intended that these regulations shall supplement and facilitate the enforcement of the provisions and standards contained in building and housing codes, zoning ordinances, comprehensive plans, official maps, and land use plans and capital budgets and programs of the town. 
Sec. 16-3. - Purpose. 
    These regulations are adopted for the following purposes: 
(1)  To protect and provide for the public health, safety, and general welfare of the town. 
(2)  To guide the future growth and development of the town in accordance with a comprehensive plan. 
(3)  To provide for adequate light, air, and privacy to secure safety from fire, flood, and other danger, and to prevent overcrowding of the land and undue congestion of population. 
(4)  To protect the character and the social and economic stability of all parts of the town, and to encourage the orderly and beneficial development of all parts of the town. 
(5)  To protect and conserve the value of land throughout the town and the value of buildings and improvements upon the land and to minimize the conflicts among the uses of land and buildings. 
(6)  To guide public and private property and action in order to provide adequate and efficient transportation, water, sewage, schools, parks, playgrounds, recreation, and other public requirements and facilities. 
(7)  To provide the most beneficial relationship between the users of land and buildings and the circulation of traffic throughout the town, having particular regard to the avoidance of congestion in the streets and in the highways, and pedestrian traffic movements appropriate to the various uses of land and buildings, and to provide for the proper location and width of streets and building lines. 
(8)  To establish reasonable standards of design and procedures for subdivisions and re-subdivisions, in order to further the orderly layout and use of land; and to insure proper legal descriptions in monumenting of subdivided land. 
(9)  To insure that public facilities are available and will have a sufficient capacity to serve the proposed subdivision. 
(10)  To prevent the pollution of air, streams, and ponds; to assure the adequacy of drainage facilities; to safeguard the water tables; and to encourage the wise use and management of natural resources throughout the town in order to preserve the integrity, stability, and beauty of the community and the value of the land. 
(11)  To preserve the natural beauty and topography of the town and to insure appropriate development with regard to these natural features. 
(12)  To provide for open spaces through the most efficient spaces and layout of the land, including the use of average density in providing for minimum width in area of lot, while preserving the density of land as established in the zoning code in the town. 
Sec. 16-4. - Definitions. 
    For the purposes of these regulations, certain terms shall be defined as follows: 
    Governing body. The town council of the Town of Cheraw. 
    Official maps or plans. Any maps or plans officially adopted by the town council as a guide for the development of the town and surrounding area. 
    Right-of-way. The property, improved or unimproved, dedicated to and accepted by a unit of government for street or road purposes for vehicular or pedestrian travel. The right-of-way line generally separates abutting private property from that reserved for public use. 
    Subdivider. Any person, firm, or corporation who undertakes the subdivision of land as herein defined. 
    Subdivision: 
(1)  The division of a tract or parcel of land into two or more lots, building sites, or other divisions for the purpose, whether immediate or future, of sale or building development, including all development of land involving a new street or a change in existing streets; including re-subdivision; and, where appropriate to the context, relates to the process of subdividing or to the land or area subdivided. The following exceptions should not be included within this definition nor be subject to these regulations; however, the planning commission shall be informed and have records of such subdivisions: 
a.  The combination or recombination of portions of previously platted lots where the total number of lots have not increased and the resultant lots are equal to the standards of the governing authority; 
b.  The division of land into parcels of five acres or more where no new street is involved. Plats of such exception shall be received as information by the building official and the planning commission which shall indicate such fact on the plat. 
(2)  Plats of such exceptions shall be received as information by the building official and the planning commission which shall indicate such fact on the plat. 
Sec. 16-5. - Official filing of regulations. 
    Under the enactment of this chapter by the town, a copy of this chapter shall be filed in the office of the clerk of court. After that time no subdivision plat for any land within the established subdivision jurisdiction shall be filed with or recorded by the county clerk of court until such plat has been submitted to and approved by the building official and the planning commission according to the procedure set forth in this chapter. 
Sec. 16-6. - Application of regulations. 
    No street or other public way or land shall be accepted or maintained; nor shall any municipal water lines, sewerage, electricity, gas, street lighting, or similar improvements be extended or connected; nor shall any permits be issued by any department of the municipality for construction of a building or other improvement in any subdivision established hereafter which does not meet the requirements set forth in this chapter. 
Sec. 16-7. - Land subject to flooding. 
    Land subject to flooding and land otherwise deemed by the planning commission to be unsuitable for development, shall not be platted for such uses as may increase danger to health, life, or property, or aggravate the flood hazard, but such land within the plat shall be set aside for such uses as shall not be endangered by periodic or occasional inundation. 
Sec. 16-8. - Effective date. 
    This chapter shall take effect and be in force from and after January 1, 1986. 
ARTICLE II. - PLAT REQUIREMENTS AND REVIEW PROCEDURES 

Sec. 16-9. - Sketch plans. 
(a)  Prior to filing an application for preliminary plat for preliminary plat approval, the subdivider or his representative shall submit a project description of the proposed subdivision to the building official. This description shall contain general information but must contain: name of developer; location of project; number and types of structures to be constructed; date utilities required; and any other pertinent information. This project description may be in the form of a letter with accompanying sketches. Oral requests shall not be substituted for the written description. 
(b)  After reviewing the project description, the building official shall respond as to the development's feasibility and availability of utilities. If roads are to be constructed which are to ultimately become the property of the town, they shall also be addressed at this time. The building official's review shall also be presented in the form of a written report. 
Sec. 16-10. - Preliminary plat required. 
    The subdivider shall prepare and submit four copies of the preliminary plat and of any supplemental material required for submission to the building official. 
Sec. 16-11. - Content of preliminary plat. 
    The preliminary plat shall be prepared by a registered surveyor or engineer. The plat shall be drawn on a standard sheet of 24-inch by 36-inch paper and to a scale of one inch equals 100 feet or one inch equals 50 feet, and shall contain or be accompanied by the following information: 
(1)  General information. 
a.  Names and location of adjoining subdivisions' streets and the location and ownership of adjoining un-subdivided property. 
b.  Boundaries of the tract to be subdivided with all bearings and distances indicated. 
c.  Existing zoning classification of the tract, if any. 
(2)  Existing site data. 
a.  Town limits lines; property lines; rights-of-way; easements; streets; utility transmission lines; storm sewers, ditches, and culverts; sanitary sewers; water mains; bridges, and buildings. 
b.  Wooded areas, marshes, watercourses, ponds, and any other similar conditions affecting the site. 
c.  Contours showing the topography of the site at a vertical interval of five feet or as determined by a certified engineer to adequately determine drainage needs. 
d.  Areas subject to flooding, accompanied by high water elevation, if available. 
(3)  Proposed site data. 
a.  Street rights-of-way, pavement widths, grade, and street names. (Street profiles and cross sections shall be provided when required by the building official or the planning commission.) 
b.  Preliminary plans prepared by an engineer for sanitary sewers, storm sewers, water, electricity, and gas lines, showing connections to existing systems or proposals for developing new water supplies, storm drainage, and sewerage disposal systems. (Storm and sanitary sewer profiles, cross sections, and sizes shall be provided when required by the building official or public utility director.) 
c.  Other easements and rights-of-way including locations, dimensions, and purposes. 
d.  Contour changes to be made by grading. 
e.  Lot lines, lot dimensions, lot and block numbers, and minimum building setback lines along street rights-of-way and rear and side property lines. 
f.  Parks, schools sites, and other public areas, if any. 
g.  Areas to be used for purposes other than residential and public, if any, with the purpose, location, and dimension of each indicated. 
(4)  Other information. 
a.  Name of subdivision and surveyor or engineer. 
b.  Name and address of owner or owners. 
c.  Date of survey and plat preparation, north point, and graphic scale. 
d.  Surveyor's certification of accuracy certifying that the error of closure is at least 1:10,000. 
e.  Site data: total acreage in tract; acreage in public or other land usage; average lot size; total number of lots; linear feet in streets. 
f.  Other supplemental materials; any deed restrictions proposed for the subdivision and any other information considered by either the subdivider or the building official to be pertinent to the review of the preliminary plat. 
Sec. 16-12. - Action of building official on preliminary plat. 
(a)  Review; decision. The building official shall review and shall approve, approve conditionally, or disapprove the preliminary plat within 60 days from the date of its submission by the applicant. If no action is taken by the building official at the end of the 60 days after submission, the preliminary plat shall be deemed to have been approved. 
(b)  Approval. If the preliminary plat is found to conform to all of the requirements of this chapter, approval shall be given by the building official. Approval shall be noted on at least two copies of the preliminary plat by the building official and town administrator. One copy shall be retained in the records of the building official; another shall be given to the subdivider. 
(c)  Disapproval; conditional approval. If the preliminary plat is disapproved or approved conditionally, reasons for such actions shall be stated in writing and signed by the building official. The reasons for disapproval shall refer specifically to those parts of the general plan or ordinance or regulation with which the plat does not conform. One copy of the reason shall be retained in the records of the building official and another shall be given to the subdivider. On conditional approval the building official may require the subdivider to resubmit the preliminary plat with all recommended changes before approval. 
Sec. 16-13. - Final plat.
