(a)  Copies required. The subdivider shall submit four dark line prints of the final plat to the town before receiving final approval from the building official. At the same time there shall be submitted one set of the proposed plans and specifications for all improvements and any proposed deed restrictions. 
(b)  Subdivisions not requiring platting. Subdivisions that do not involve construction or opening of new streets, water or sewer facilities, or improvements to existing streets may be accepted by the building official in the form of a final plat. Such subdivision shall comply with all requirements of these regulations. 
(c)  Time of submission. The final plat of the proposed subdivision shall be submitted to the building official for final approval within one year of the date on which the preliminary plat was approved. If not submitted for final approval within such time, the preliminary plat shall be considered as having been disapproved, unless the building official agrees to an extension of time. 
(d)  Recording. The final plat shall constitute only that portion of the approved preliminary plat which the subdivider proposes to record and develop at the time. The final plat shall be filed in the office of the county clerk of court within 30 days after approval, of [or] it not, approval shall be considered void. 
(e)  Contents. The final plat shall conform substantially to the preliminary plat as it was approved. The final plat shall be prepared by a registered surveyor or engineer and shall be drawn on a standard sheet of 24-inch by 36-inch paper to a scale of one inch equals 100 feet or one inch equals 50 feet. It shall contain or be accompanied by the following information: 
(1)  Survey data: 
a.  Exact boundary of the tract to be subdivided; the error of closure shall be at least 1:10,000. 
b.  Names and location of adjoining subdivisions and streets, location and ownership of adjoining un-subdivided property. 
c.  Accurate location and description of all monuments, markets, and control points. 
d.  Sufficient engineering data to determine regularly and reproduce on the ground every straight or curved boundary line, street line, lot line, right-of-way line, easement line, and set-back line, including linear dimensions, bearings or deflection angles, tangents, radii, arcs, chords, and central angles. (All dimensions shall be measured to the nearest one-hundredth of a foot and all angles to the nearest minute.) 
e.  The error of linear closure for lots shall be at least 1:5,000. 
(2)  Site data: 
a.  All rights-of-way, easements, and areas to be dedicated to public use with the purpose of each stated. 
b.  Areas to be used for purposes other than residential and public, if any, with the purpose, location, and dimensions of each indicated. 
c.  Lot and block numbers; street names. 
d.  Such cross section and profiles of streets as may be required by the building official and public utility director. 
e.  Such plans for water mains, sanitary sewers and storm sewers, showing sizes, cross sections, and profiles as required by the building official and the public utility director. 
(3)  Other information: 
a.  Name of subdivision, owner, and surveyor or engineer. 
b.  Date of survey and plat preparation; north arrow; graphic scale. 
c.  Deed restrictions proposed for the subdivision, if any. 
d.  Any other information considered by either the subdivider or the building official to be pertinent to the review of the final plat. 
(f)  Certificates. The following signed certificates shall be shown on the original and all copies of the final plat submitted to the building official. 
(1)  Certificate of ownership and dedication. 
(2)  Certificate of approval of water supply and sewage disposal systems (where necessary). 
(3)  Certificates of surveying and mapping. 
(g)  [Signed statement.] A statement signed by the town administrator as to the town's acceptance of utilities. 
Sec. 16-14. - Action of building official on final plat. 
(a)  Approval. The building official shall approve or disapprove the final plat within 60 days after it has been submitted for final approval. Approval and the date thereof shall be known on the plat over the signature of the building official and town administrator. If no action is taken by the building official at the end of the 60 days after submission the plat shall be deemed to have been approved. 
(b)  Disapproval. If the final plat is disapproved by the building official, the grounds for such action shall be stated in writing. The reasons for disapproval shall refer specifically to those parts of the general plan or ordinance or regulation with which the plat does not conform. One copy of the reasons for disapproval shall be retained in the records of the building official and another shall be given to the subdivider. 
(c)  Reconciliation with preliminary plat. During review of the final plat, the building official shall check the final plat against the preliminary plat. The building official shall appoint an engineer or surveyor to check the accuracy of the subdivision layout and the final plat. If substantial errors are found, the cost of checking the plat shall be charged to the developer. 
(d)  Conformity to land development plan. All proposed subdivisions of land shall conform to the applicable portions of the land development plan for the town. 
(e)  Post approval procedure. After final approval, the subdivider shall file the original approved final plat with certificates with the county clerk of court. The subdivider shall provide the building official with one dark line print thereof. 
ARTICLE III. - DESIGN STANDARDS 

Sec. 16-15. - Minimum requirements. 
    The following design standards shall be considered minimum requirements; however, higher standards are to be encouraged in subdivision designs. If only minimum standards are used the result will be a standardized and monotonous urban area. Subdivision designs should carry out the purpose of the general plan in this chapter but not be limited to the minimum requirements as provided in this article. 
Sec. 16-16. - Easements. 
(a)  Easements not less than 20 feet wide centered on side or rear lot lines shall be provided where necessary for use by public or private utilities. Where a subdivision is traversed by a water course, drainage way, channel, or stream, they shall be provided a storm water easement or drainage right-of-way conforming substantially with the lines of such water course and of sufficient width to carry off storm water. 
(b)  The governing body concerned shall maintain only those easements it accepts for public maintenance as will be adequate for this purpose. Parallel streets or parkways may be required in connection therewith. 
Sec. 16-17. - Blocks 
(a)  Lengths. 
(1)  The lengths, widths, and shapes of blocks shall be determined with regard for the following: 
a.  Provision of adequate building sites suitable to the special needs for the types of use contemplated. 
b.  Zoning requirements as to lot sizes and dimensions. 
c.  Needs for convenient access, circulation, control and safety of street traffic. 
d.  Limitations and opportunities of topography. 
(2)  Blocks for residential use shall be not longer than 2,400 feet, and shall not be less than 200 feet in length, measured along the center line of the block or as directed by the building official. 
(b)  Width. Blocks used for residential purposes should be of sufficient width to allow for two tiers of lots and appropriate depth where practical considering natural topography or man-made boundaries. Blocks intended for business and industrial use shall be of a width suitable for the intended use, with due allowance for off-street parking and loading facilities. 
Sec. 16-18. - Lots. 
    Lot size, width, depth, shape, and orientation shall be appropriate for the location of the subdivision and for the type of development and use contemplated. All lots shall conform to the requirements of the zoning chapter (Chapter 20) of this Code. 
Sec. 16-19. - Building lines. 
    In all residential subdivisions the minimum setback from the street right-of-way or property line shall be in conformance with the applicable zoning classifications. 
Sec. 16-20. - Public sites and open spaces. 
    Where a proposed park, playground, school, or other public use shown in the general plan is located in whole or in part of a subdivision, the building official may require the reservation of such area for a period not exceeding 90 days from the date of approval of the preliminary plat in order to give the public body concerned opportunity to acquire such site for that expressed purpose. 
Sec. 16-21. - Areas subject to flooding. 
    A plat of a proposed subdivision submitted to the building official and public utility director for approval which contains land subject to flooding shall have such areas delineated as being subject to flooding. No new construction shall take place within 50 feet of a natural drainage way or any area so designated as a flood prone area by the Federal Emergency Management Agency. 
ARTICLE IV. - IMPROVEMENTS 

Sec. 16-22. - Water lines; fire hydrants. 
    Every lot in every subdivision shall be provided with an approved water supply. It shall have an adequate supply of water for domestic and fire purposes, with sufficient pressure in the main to meet the minimum standards for fire purposes at all time[s], in accordance with underwriters' standards. The water mains in the subdivision shall: 
(1)  Be of sufficient size to provide at least one standard fire hydrant within 1,000 feet (to be measured along rights-of-way of streets or public ways) of each residence or other structures and 500 feet of any commercial or industrial buildings and at locations designated by the fire chief. 
(2)  Provide circulation within the system where practical. 
(3)  Should the town require a larger water line to be installed in order to allow for future growth, the town will be responsible for the cost between the larger size line and that required for development. 
(4)  Comply will all rules and standards of the water and fire departments of the town. 
a.  Where a public water main, in the opinion of the building official and public utility director, is reasonably accessible the subdivider shall connect with such water main and provide a connection stub-out for each lot. For the purpose of this section "reasonably accessible" is considered 1,000 feet from the property proposed to be subdivided. 
b.  The developer shall be required to furnish the following documents to the town upon the installation of such water lines: 
1.  Certificate of approval from DHEC for use of water system. 
2.  As-built drawings of all work completed. 
3.  A one-year warranty on all lines installed by the developer. 
Sec. 16-23. - Sanitary sewer system. 
(a)  Where a public sanitary sewer is reasonably accessible, the subdivider shall connect with such sanitary sewer and provide a connection with cleanout for each lot. For the purpose of this section "reasonably accessible" is considered 1,000 feet from the property proposed to be subdivided. The design, grade, and capacity shall be approved by the public utility director; however, in no event shall the town be required to furnish sewer service to persons or subdivisions outside the corporate limits of the town. 
(b)  The developer shall be required to furnish the following documents to the town upon the installation of such water lines: 
(1)  Certificate of approval and acceptance by DHEC. 
(2)  As-built drawings of all work completed. 
(3)  A one-year warranty on all lines installed by the developer. 
Sec. 16-24. - Sanitary sewer lines. 
    The subdivider shall install sanitary sewers that are large enough to provide adequate service to every house in the subdivision when it is completely developed. Sanitary sewers shall be installed in accordance with town specifications and standards. Should the town require a larger sewer line to be installed in order to allow for future growth, the town will be responsible for the cost between the larger size line and that required for the development. 
Sec. 16-25. - Storm sewers and drainage. 
    An adequate storm drainage system designed to protect the proposed development from flooding shall be installed in accordance with good engineering practices. The system shall be adequate to carry all storm water in its drainage area and shall complement systems on adjacent property upstream and downstream. Where a public storm sewer is reasonably accessible, as determined by the building official and the public works director, the subdivider shall connect with such drainage system. The developer shall also be required to submit to the town an easement for any drainage ditch draining more than one lot. The size of such easement shall be determined by the public works director. 
Sec. 16-26. - Streets. 
(a)  Streets to be developed. Developers shall be required to develop paved streets in any development in accordance with acceptable standards. 
(b)  System design and improvements. The street system shall be designed to permit the safe, efficient, and orderly movement of traffic; to have a simple and logical pattern; to respect natural features and topography; and to present an attractive streetscape. 
(1)  Layout and alignment. 
a.  Proposed streets shall be coordinated with the street system in the surrounding area and where possible shall provide for the continuation of existing streets abutting the development. 
b.  All streets shall be opened to the exterior property lines of the development unless permanently terminated by a vehicular turnaround or an intersection with another street. 
c.  No half street shall be permitted. 
(2)  Alleys. 
a.  Alleys are not permitted in residential subdivisions. 
b.  Paved alleys are permitted in commercial and industrial developments to provide service access, off-street loading and unloading, and parking consistent with and adequate for the uses proposed. 
(3)  Culs-de-sac. 
a.  Dead-end streets designed to be permanently closed at one end shall not exceed 1,000 feet in length measured from the right-of-way of the intersecting street to the center point of the turnaround. 
b.  Turnarounds shall be provided at the closed end of the street. 
(4)  Intersections. 
a.  No more than two streets shall intersect at any one point. 
b.  All streets shall intersect as nearly as possible at 90-degree angles. 
c.  Streets entering upon opposite sides of a given street shall have their center lines directly opposite or shall be offset a minimum distance of 150 feet for minor streets and 400 feet for major streets, measured along the center line of the streets being intersected. 
d.  Street intersections shall be located at least 150 feet from the right-of-way of any railroad track, measured from the center point of the intersection to the railroad right-of-way nearest the intersection. 
e.  Private drives shall not intersect a public street within 40 feet of an intersection, measured from the street right-of-way. 
(5)  Right-of-way, lane and pavement widths. Minimum street right-of-way, lane, and pavement widths shall be as follows: 
Classification Pavement Width Right-of-Way Width Minor Street 50 feet  - with barrier curb 25 feet 50 feet  - with roll curb 25 feet 50 feet  - with valley gutter 50 feet Major Street 66 feet  - with barrier curb 27 feet 66 feet  - with roll curb 36 feet 66 feet  - with valley gutter 36 feet 66 feet Alley 18 feet 22 feet  
Sec. 16-27. - Driveway tiles. 
    The property owner shall be responsible for the placement of proper driveway drainage tiles as each lot is developed or until such time that the county or the state department of transportation assumes such responsibility. 
Sec. 16-28. - Survey accuracy. 
    The error of lineage closure for land surveys shall not exceed one foot per 10,000 feet of perimeter of land (1:10,000). 
ARTICLE V. - TOWN PARTICIPATION IN INSTALLATION OF WATER AND SEWER MAINS 

Sec. 16-29. - Policy. 
    The town may participate in the installation of water mains and sanitary sewer lines in any new and undeveloped subdivision for the sale of lots, within the corporate limits of the town as provided in this article. 
Sec. 16-30. - Town participation. 
    The owner or owners of any such subdivision within the town limits after approval of subdivision plat by the building official and with the consent, permission, and approval of the town council shall install water mains and sanitary sewer lines at their own expense in such subdivisions. The town requires that all improvements made in the public rights-of-way and easements of the subdivision be supervised by an approved licensed engineer whose services would be retained by the developer. If and when the water mains and sanitary sewer lines are approved and accepted by the town as part of the water works and sanitary sewer systems of the town, then the town shall reimburse the developer at a rate as herein described. 
Sec. 16-31. - Method of reimbursement. 
(a)  Reimbursement to the developer of such water mains and sanitary sewer lines shall be contingent upon storm sewers having been installed by the developer, when required, in accordance with the approved plat. 
(b)  A developer shall be eligible for reimbursement from the town for the installation of water mains and sanitary sewer lines as each individual lot within the subdivision has upon it a completely constructed house which is connected to the town's utilities; that is, reimbursement shall be made to the developer on a lot by lot basis. The rate of reimbursement to the developer shall be $10.00 per front foot, with a minimum of no less than $750.00 and a maximum not to exceed $1,500.00 per lot. 
(c)  Any commercial, industrial, or multiple-family housing projects will be dealt with on a case-by-case basis. 
Sec. 16-32. - Term of agreement. 
(a)  This agreement for reimbursement will terminate ten years after the date of the approval of the agreement by the town council. 
(b)  This reimbursement amount shall be reviewed by council from time to time and revised as seen fit to maintain a fair and equitable return to the developer. 
ARTICLE VI. - ADMINISTRATION AND ENFORCEMENT 

Sec. 16-33. - Effect of plat approval on dedication. 
    The approval of a plat by the building official and the planning commission shall not be deemed to constitute or affect an acceptance by the governing body of the dedication of any street or other ground shown upon the plat. 
Sec. 16-34. - Variances. 
    Whenever the tract to be divided is of such unusual size or shape or is surrounded by such development or unusual conditions that strict application of the requirements in this chapter would result in substantial hardship or inequity, the planning commission may vary or modify, except as otherwise indicated, requirements of design, but not of procedure or improvements, so that the subdivider may develop the property in a reasonable manner, but so at the same time, the public welfare is protected and the general intent and spirit of this chapter is preserved. 
Sec. 16-35. - Amendments. 
    This chapter may be amended form time to time by the town council; however, no amendment shall become effective unless it shall have been submitted to the planning commission for review and recommendations. The planning commission shall have 60 days within which to submit it[s] report to the town council. If the planning commission fails to submit a report within the specified time period, it shall be deemed to have approved the proposed amendment. 
Sec. 16-36. - Enforcement. 
(a)  No plat of any subdivision shall be entitled to be recorded in the office of the clerk of court of Chesterfield County or shall have any validity until it has been approved in the manner prescribed herein. 
(b)  It shall be unlawful for the owner, or the agent of any owner, to transfer or sell any land by reference to or by other use of a plat unless such plat has been approved as prescribed herein. The town council may enjoin such transfer, sale, or agreement by appropriate legal action. 
(c)  In case of any violation of this chapter the town administrator or any appropriate official as may be designated by the planning commission is authorized and directed to institute legal action to put an end to such violations. 
Sec. 16-37. - Interpretation and conflict. 
    In interpreting and applying the provisions of this chapter, the provisions shall be held to be minimum requirements necessary to uphold the purpose of this chapter. It is not intended by this chapter to interfere with or abrogate or annul and easements, covenants, or other agreements between parties, provided, however, where this chapter imposes greater restrictions on the subdivision and/or use of buildings or land, or requires more open spaces or more stringent development standards than required by other resolutions, ordinances, rules, or regulations, or by easements, covenants, or agreements, the provisions of this chapter shall govern. When the provisions of any other statute require more restrictive standards than are required by the regulations of this chapter, the provisions of each statute shall govern. 
Sec. 16-38. - Sale of plat before approval; remedy. 
(a)  After the adoption of this chapter any person who, being the owner or agent of the owner of any land located within the established subdivision jurisdiction, transfers or sells or agrees to sell or negotiates to sell any land by reference to or exhibition of or by other use of a plat of a subdivision, before such plat has been approved by the building official and the planning commission and recorded in the office of the county clerk of court, shall forfeit and pay a penalty of $250.00 to the town for each lot or parcel so transferred or sold or deeded or negotiated to be sold. 
(b)  The description of such lot or parcel by metes and bounds in the instrument of transfer or other document used in the process of selling or transferring such lot or parcel shall not exempt the transaction from such penalties or from the remedy provided in this section. The town attorney or other official designated by the town may enjoin such transfer or sale or agreement by an action for injunction brought in any court of competent jurisdiction and may also recover such penalty by civil action in any court of competent jurisdiction. 
Sec. 16-39. - Penalty. 
    Any violation of this chapter will be punishable by a fine not exceeding $500.00 or imprisonment not exceeding 30 days, in accordance with S.C. Code of Laws, § 5-7-30, as amended. 
Chapter 17 - TAXATION 
ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Sec. 17-1. - Adoption of budget. 
    The Cheraw Town Council shall prepare a budget for the fiscal year ending June of each year and estimated revenues for payment of same. The budget shall be made a part hereof by reference as fully as if incorporated herein. 
Sec. 17-2. - Administration of budget. 
    The town administrator shall administer the budget and shall authorize the transfer of appropriated funds within and between departments as necessary to achieve the goals of the annual budget. 
Sec. 17-3. - Taxes imposed. 
    A tax to cover the fiscal year period from July 1 to June 30 of the following year shall be established annually by the town council. Said tax rates shall be levied on the assessed value of real estate and personal property of every description known and used by the Town of Cheraw except such as exempt from the taxation under the Constitution and laws of the State of South Carolina. 
Sec. 17-4. - Assessments prepared by county. 
    The town shall utilize the tax assessment of evaluation of properties prepared by the county auditor and county tax assessor as the basis for determining the assessments of taxes for municipal purposes. 
Sec. 17-5. - Billing dates; penalties. 
(a)  The billing dates, the dates and amount of penalty which shall be levied for delinquent taxes shall be as follows: Tax notices for each calendar year shall be mailed in October and are payable by January 15 of the following year. 
(b)  Penalty dates for payments paid in the following calendar year are subject to a penalty of three percent on or after January 16, ten percent if paid by February 1, and 15 percent plus collection costs if paid by March 16. After June 1 additional collection costs will be added. 
Sec. 17-6. - Tax collector; delinquent tax sale. 
    The Chesterfield County Treasurer shall serve as the collection agency for the real estate taxes for the town and shall remit said portion to the town according to a prescribed schedule in a timely manner. Chesterfield County shall also handle the sale of all delinquent sales for the town. 
Sec. 17-7. - Exemption of certain manufacturing establishments from ad valorem taxation. 
(a)  There shall be exempt from ad valorem taxation, within the Town of Cheraw, all new manufacturing establishments located wholly within the corporate limits of the Town of Cheraw, for two years from the establishment and all additions to the existing manufacturing establishments, located wholly within the town for two years from the time each such addition is made, if the costs of such addition is $50,000.00 or more, provided, however, that the exemption shall first apply to qualified properties upon which a tax would ordinarily be paid beginning January 1, 1989. Such additions shall include additional machinery and equipment installed in the manufacturing establishment. 
(b)  No new manufacturing establishment shall be entitled to the exemption unless construction of the new manufacturing establishment is commenced after August 9, 1988. 
(c)  No additions to existing manufacturing establishments shall be entitled to the exemption unless construction of the new addition is commenced after August 9, 1988. 
(d)  Exemptions granted pursuant to this section shall not result in any refund of taxes. 
(e)  Any manufacturing establishment seeking to obtain the exemption from ad valorem taxes levied by the Town of Cheraw shall comply with all requirements of state law to obtain exemption of local property taxes on manufacturing property allowed under S.C. Code of Laws 1976, § 13-37-220(7), as amended. 
(f)  Except with respect to the question of whether or not the property was constructed or acquired after the effective date of this section, the town clerk shall annually use information provided by the South Carolina Department of Revenue to the appropriate county official under S.C. Code of Laws 1976, § 12-3-145, as amended. 
(g)  The tax exempt status shall be revoked if it is determined that the property does not qualify annually under the provisions of the Constitution, the general laws of this state, and this section. 
(h)  If it is found, within three years from the date that taxes would have been due on property that has been granted an exemption, that the exemption was improperly granted, the town clerk, upon receiving notice thereof, shall enter, on the duplicate, the taxes that would have been due for any years that the property escaped taxation, with a ten percent penalty added thereto. 
(i)  The annexation of existing manufacturing establishments into the Town of Cheraw shall not result in the creation of a new manufacturing establishment which would be entitled to an exemption under this section. 
ARTICLE II. - LOCAL HOSPITALITY FEE 

Sec. 17-8. - Declaration of policy; purpose; intent. 
    This article is enacted to preserve the general health, safety, and welfare of the general public and to promote and enhance the tourism industry in the Cheraw area by imposing a fee for the purpose of creating a fund which will be utilized for purposes enumerated in S.C. Code of Laws, § 6-1-730(A), as such may be amended. 
Sec. 17-9. - Local hospitality fee of two percent. 
    There is hereby imposed a local hospitality fee of two percent on the gross proceeds of the sale of all prepared meals and beverages served by any establishment within the Town of Cheraw including those licensed for on-premise consumption of alcoholic beverages, beer, or wine within the town. 
Sec. 17-10. - Payment of fee. 
(a)  Payment of the fee established herein shall be the liability of the consumer of the services for items described in section 17-9. The fee shall be paid at the time of delivery of the services or items to which the fee applies and shall be collected by the provider or seller of the items. 
(b)  The fee collected by the seller or provider of services or items as required under section 17-9 shall be remitted to the town as follows: 
(1)  On a monthly basis when the estimated amount of average collections is more than $50.00 a month. 
(2)  On a quarterly basis when the estimated amount of average collections is between $25.00 a month to $50.00 a month. 
(3)  On an annual basis when the amount of average collections is less than $25.00 a month. 
(c)  Total collections and required reports shall be submitted to the town by the twentieth day of the month and shall cover sales for the pervious [previous] month. 
(d)  A copy of the completed South Carolina State Sales and Use Return Form (Form ST-3) shall be attached along with such required forms prepared by the town. When a hospitality fee return is filed and the fees due are paid in full on or before the final due date, the filer is allowed a discount of two percent on the fees shown to be due by the return. Payments covered under the provisions of subsection 17-10(b)(2) shall be submitted quarterly by the twentieth day of January, April, July, and October for the previous quarterly sales or annually by the twentieth of January for the calendar year sales as provided in subsection 17-10(b)(3). When the twentieth of the month falls on a weekend or a holiday the town will accept, without penalty, payment on the following work day. 
(e)  Any collections not remitted by the deadlines outlined in this article shall be subject to a penalty of five percent of the unpaid amount for any calendar month or portion thereof after the due date until paid. The failure to collect from patrons the amount imposed by this article shall not relieve any establishment subject to this article form making the required remittance. 
(f)  Any person violating this article shall be deemed guilty of an offense and shall be subject to punishment by a fine of not more than $500.00 or imprisonment for up to 30 days, or both. Each day of violation shall be considered a separate offense. Punishment for violation shall not relieve the offender of liability for delinquent amount, penalties, and costs provided for herein. 
Sec. 17-11. - Local hospitality fee fund established. 
    A separate fund or account, to be known as the local hospitality fee account, shall be established and all revenues received from the hospitality fee shall be deposited into this account and shall remain segregated from the general fund. The principal and any interest accrued from this account shall be expended only as permitted in section 17-12. 
Sec. 17-12. - Permitted use of funds. 
    The town is hereby authorized to utilize funds collected from the imposition of the hospitality fee for the purposes enumerated in S.C. Code of Laws, § 6-1-730, as such may be amended. 
Sec. 17-13. - Inspection and audits. 
    For the purposes of enforcing the provisions of this section the town clerk, licensing and permitting official, or any other authorized agent of the town is empowered to enter upon the premises of any person subject to this section to make inspection, examine, and/or audit the books and records, and it shall be unlawful for any person to fail or refuse to make available the necessary books and records. In the event that the audit or inspection reveals that the establishment has filed false information, the cost of the audit shall be added to the corrected amount due and late penalties in addition to other penalties provided herein. Each day of failure to pay the proper fee shall constitute a separate offense. The town clerk, licensing and permitting official, or other authorized agent of the town shall make systematic inspections of the businesses within the town to ensure compliance with this section. Records of inspections and audits shall not be deemed public records and shall not be released by the town. 
Sec. 17-14. - Authorization for use. 
    Authorization to utilize revenues from the local hospitality fee account shall be by the annual budget ordinance, or budget amendment, duly adopted by the town council. 
Sec. 17-15. - Severability. 
    If any section, phrase, sentence, or portion of this article is for any reason held invalid or unconstitutional by any court of competent jurisdiction, such section, phrase, sentence, or portion shall be deemed a separate, distinct, and independent provision and such holding shall not affect of the remaining sections, phrases, sentences, or portions thereof. 
    This article shall become effective immediately upon its adopting and all applicable businesses shall be responsible for collecting and remitting the tax beginning on July 1, 2006. 
ARTICLE III. - LOCAL ACCOMMODATIONS TAX 

Sec. 17-16. - Imposition. 
    There is hereby imposed a local accommodations tax of three percent upon the gross proceeds derived from rental or charges for accommodations furnished to transients as is more fully defined and described in S.C. Code of Laws 1976, § 6-1-520, as amended. 
Sec. 17-17. - Payment of tax; past due penalty. 
    Payment of the accommodations tax as herein established shall be remitted to the town on a monthly basis, along with such return forms as established by the town for such purposes, not later than the twentieth day of the month and shall the tax due for the previous month. Any tax not timely remitted shall be subject to a penalty of five percent of the sum owed for each month or portion thereof until paid. 
Sec. 17-18. - Use of revenue. 
    The revenue generated by the local accommodations tax, with accumulated interest, placed in the local accommodations tax fund shall be used exclusively for the following purposes: 
(1)  Tourism-related buildings, including, but not limited to, civic enters, coliseums, and aquariums; 
(2)  Cultural, recreational, or historic facilities; 
(3)  Beach access and re-nourishment; 
(4)  Highways, roads, streets, and bridges providing access to tourist destinations; 
(5)  Advertisements and promotions related to tourism development; or 
(6)  Water and sewer infrastructure to serve tourism-related demand. 
Chapter 18 - TAXICABS 

Sec. 18-1. - Definitions. 
    The following words, terms, and phrases, when used in this article, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
    Taxicab means any motor vehicle used for or engaged in the transportation of passengers for hire or compensation, except vehicles commonly known as buses. 
Sec. 18-2. - Compliance; exceptions. 
    No person shall drive a taxicab or engage in the business of operating taxicabs upon the town streets until that person has complied with this article. This article shall not apply to vehicles operating under a special franchise or to vehicles transporting persons to or from school or college. 
Sec. 18-3. - Ownership of vehicle required. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to engage in the business of operating or maintaining taxicabs in the town pursuant to a license issued in accordance with this section unless such person shall be the bona fide owner of the motor vehicles so operated or maintained. All such persons shall deposit with the town a copy of certificate or other satisfactory evidence covering each vehicle so operated or maintained. 
Sec. 18-4. - Lease of vehicles to third parties. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to engage in the business of operating or maintaining taxicabs in the town, pursuant to a license issued in accordance with this section, to rent or lease any motor vehicle, the operation of which is covered under such license, to any other person without first surrendering to the town for cancellation the license covering the operation of such motor vehicle as a taxicab. 
Sec. 18-5. - Application for operator's business license; contents. 
(a)  Any person desiring a license to operate a taxicab business shall file any application for a license upon a form furnished by the town, provided that the license shall be issued within 30 days after a written application has been made. 
(b)  The application referred to in subsection (a) shall give the full name, age, and home address of the applicant and shall state whether or not he has been convicted of a violation of any town ordinance or of any state or federal law and, if so, the number of times, the dates, and the nature of the violations and all other information that shall be required. 
(c)  If the applicant for a license to operate a taxicab business is a firm or corporation, the requirements of subsections (a) and (b) of this section shall be complied with by each member of the firm or by the principal or managing officer of the corporation in charge of actual operation of the business in the town. 
Sec. 18-6. - Age limit of licensees; residency requirement. 
(a)  No license for the operation of a taxicab business or a taxicab driver's permit shall be issued to any person under the age of 21 years. 
(b)  No license for the operation of a taxicab business shall be issued to any person who has not, for a period of six months immediately prior to the date of the application therefore resided in the county. 
Sec. 18-7. - Taxicab license fee. 
    The taxicab business must pay a business license fee for the operation of the business plus an additional fee of $25.00 per year per taxicab. 
Sec. 18-8. - Limitation on the number of taxicabs. 
    The number of license[d] taxicabs for any one business is limited to 12. 
Sec. 18-9. - Liability insurance requirement. 
    No license shall be issued by the town to any person to operate a taxicab or other like vehicle within the town unless the vehicle is covered by a paid-in-full annual liability insurance policy with limits of at least $100,000.00 per individual; $200,000.00 per incident; and $25,000.00 for property damage. Proof of such annual paid-in-full insurance coverage must be exhibited to the town by delivering a copy of the liability insurance policy for each vehicle insured and a paid receipt for the premium indicating that the annual insurance coverage is paid-in-full. 
Sec. 18-10. - Notice of cancellation of insurance. 
    Each policy of insurance required under this section shall contain a clause authorizing and directing the insurer to notify the town of any cancellation thereof, and immediately upon notice of cancellation, the town shall revoke the license to operate a taxicab or other like vehicle within the town. 
Sec. 18-11. - Issuance of license. 
(a)  The town clerk shall collect, correlate, and submit to the town council the application and all other reports of information and findings required under this section, together with a report of any additional pertinent information and a recommendation. 
(b)  The town council shall review the application, finding, and report and recommendations and shall authorize the issuance of a license to operate a taxicab business if it finds that the applicant therefore has complied with all requirements of this section and is fit, willing, and able to perform public transportation and to conform to this chapter and that further taxicab service in the town is required by public convenience and necessity. In making these findings, the town council shall take into consideration the number of taxicabs already in operation, whether existing transportation is adequate to meet the public need, the probable effect of increased service on local traffic conditions, and the character, experience, and responsibility of the applicant. 
(c)  Upon authorization by the town council the town clerk shall issue to the applicant a license to operate a taxicab business upon payment to the town of the license fee required. 
Sec. 18-12. - Identification markings. 
    Upon the issuance of any license for the operation of a taxicab business, the licensee shall paint or affix to each side and the rear of each vehicle operated under his license, in letters at least two inches high, the number of the license and the name of the holder thereof, or, in the alternative, he shall place on the top near the front a sign which may be illuminated designating the vehicle as a taxicab and giving the license number. Magnetic signs may be substituted for the required signs. 
Sec. 18-13. - Report of suspicious persons. 
    Every taxicab driver shall report to the police department any suspicious person or activity coming to his attention as soon as possible or immediately upon the discharge of any such person from his vehicle. 
Sec. 18-14. - Vehicles from other areas. 
    Taxicabs or other public vehicles for hire, having no town license and whose place of business is not in the town, may bring passengers into town but shall not solicit any passengers for any destination within or outside the town limits. 
Sec. 18-15. - Employment of driver without taxicab driver's permit prohibited. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person engaged in the business of operating or maintaining taxicabs pursuant to this section to permit the driving of such taxicab in the town by any person to whom a taxicab driver's permit shall not have been granted and currently in effect. 
Sec. 18-16. - Revocation of taxicab driver's permit. 
    A taxicab driver's permits shall be revoked upon bond forfeiture, guilty plea or conviction in connection with the violation of any town ordinance or state statute relating to the operation of motor vehicles. 
Sec. 18-17. - Appeals. 
    Upon the failure of the town to issue a taxicab driver's permit or upon the town's revocation of a taxicab driver's permit, such aggrieved applicant or licensee shall have the right to appeal to the town council and be heard in connection therewith. 
Chapter 19 - WATER AND SEWER 
ARTICLE I. - WATERWORKS 

Sec. 19-1. - Liability of owner for broken meters. 
(a)  The individual contracting for water service with the Town of Cheraw shall be responsible for any negligent or willful damage to meters, meter boxes, valves, locking devices, or other fixtures pertaining to water service, and the actual cost of labor and materials used in replacement or repair of such damaged fixtures shall be added to the customer's utility bill. 
(b)  It shall be unlawful for any person to receive water from any part of the town's water system without a valid permit/approval from the town clerk, or without an in-service meter. It shall be unlawful for any person to tamper with, open, close, remove, bypass, or otherwise deal with any fire hydrant, valve, valve box, meter, meter box, tank, pump, structure, or fixture appertaining to the town's water system. Upon conviction, there shall be a fine imposed of not less than $200.00 for the first offense. Each subsequent offense shall, upon conviction, be imposed a fee of an additional $100.00 with a maximum fine not to exceed $500.00 or imprisonment for a period not exceeding 30 days. Each violation shall constitute a separate offense. 
(Ord. No. 2009-04, 12-9-2008) 
Editor's note- Ord. No. 2009-04, adopted Dec. 9, 2008, set out provisions intended for use as § 18-1. To preserve the chapter numbering of this Code, and at the editor's discretion, these provisions have been included as § 19-1. See also the Code Comparative Table. 
Sec. 19-2. - When connection and meter required. 
(a)  Every residence or other building which is located within 250 feet of any water main or within 250 feet of any sewer collector line shall be connected thereto and shall utilize the same for water and for the disposal of all sewage originating on said premises. Such connections shall be forthwith made and for the purposes of the penal provisions of this chapter (subsection 19-1(b)), each day during which such building shall not be connected to such water main or collector line shall be a separate offense and punishable as hereinafter provided. 
(b)  All water service shall be rendered upon a meter basis. 
Sec. 19-3. - Reading of meters; billing; second notices; discontinuation of service and reconnection fee. 
(a)  All meters shall be read once a month and water bills shall be due when rendered and payable in their entirety within 30 days. Customers will receive a second notice concerning their account approximately seven days prior to their service being terminated. 
(b)  If any bill remains unpaid at the end of the 30-day period, thereafter all service to such user shall be discontinued (usually around the sixteenth of the month) until such user shall have paid the current bill and penalties, together with a reconnection fee of $15.00. 
Sec. 19-4. - Water bill adjustment policy. 
(a)  Water users experiencing a severe increase in their utility bill may be eligible for an adjustment to that bill, if and only if, the bill being considered is twice the normal six-month average for water and sewer charges for that individual account. 
(b)  No adjustments will be made to any bill within the first six months of activity. 
(c)  The garbage fee, meter rent, and service fee will not be included in determining the six-month average for one's account. 
(d)  Water users may have no more than two adjustments to their account during any calendar year. 
(e)  A "leak" will be defined as the loss of water due to broken or burst water lines/pipes, an improperly functioning toilet, or a damaged value [valve] on a water heater. Outside spigots left on will not be considered a "leak" and, therefore, no adjustment will be made on that individual's account. 
(f)  Individuals requesting such adjustments must have had a valid leak and show some proof of repair. 
(g)  The formula for determining the adjustment to the customer's water and sewer bill will be as follows: the high bill minus the six-month average equals the base rate. The base rate divided by two equals the charges. 
    The charges plus the six-month average equals the total adjusted water and sewer bill. 
    After the adjustment to the water and sewer bill, the garbage, meter rent, and service fee will be added for a final adjusted bill. 
Sec. 19-5. - Connection fees. 
    For each new residential and commercial connection to the town's water system, the person or firm applying for such service shall pay connection fees in the following amounts: 
    For each new residential and commercial connection to the town's water system, the person or firm applying for such service shall pay connection fees in the following amounts: 
(a)  For standard water connections: 
Water Meter Size Inside Town Outside Town 3/4" $600.00 $800.00 1" $700.00 $1,100.00 11/2" $1,100.00 $1,925.00 2" $1,600.00 $2,925.00  
(b)  All water connections over two inches for in-town customers are charged at a rate equal to the town's actual cost of installation plus 20 percent with a minimum charge of $3,500.00. Out-of-town customers will be charged at a rate equal to the town's actual cost of installation plus 40 percent, with a minimum charge of $6,500.00. 
(c)  A backflow prevention device may be required for any residence, business, or industry. Frequent testing of this device will be required of every business at regular intervals. 
(d)  Water connection to apartment units or multi-business commercial complexes shall be determined in one of two ways: 
(1)  If the town installs the water line to the property line the fee will be based on the cost of providing such service plus 20 percent (40 percent for out-of-town customers) plus an additional fee equal to the tap fee for each unit; or 
(2)  If the developer installs the water line and all appurtenances to meet the town's specifications the developer will only pay $75.00 per unit as a connection fee if the property is in-town and $200.00 per unit if the property is out-of-town. 
(e)  No individual will be allowed to connect to any tap which has been inactive for a period of five years without first paying a new connection fee. 
(f)  There shall be no refund for unused or abandoned taps. 
(g)  Connections for meters larger than two inches, if installed to the town's specifications by the owner's contractor, shall be charged $600.00 per connection for customers inside town and $1,100.00 per connection for customers out-of-town. Ownership of these meters shall be with the customer who shall be responsible for meter testing at intervals not exceeding five years and any necessary repairs in accordance with a five-year schedule or as necessitated by performance. 
(Ord. No. 2008-09, 2-12-2008; Ord. No. 2009-04, 12-9-2008)

No. 2009-04, adopted Dec. 9, 2008, set out provisions intended for use as § 18-4, which have been included as § 19-5. See also the Code Comparative Table. 
Sec. 19-6. - Service fees and transfer fees. 
    Each new residential and commercial customer of the town's water and sewer system shall pay a nonrefundable fee in order to establish the appropriate account. Rates of service fees are as follows: 
(1)  Owner occupants ..... $35.00 
(2)  Renters/tenants ..... 50.00 
    Customers moving to another location in the town's water and sewer system and desiring to transfer their service fee to that location will be charged a $5.00 transfer fee to cover the cost of transferring the account. The present account must be paid in full before the account may be transferred to another location.
